<div id="workskin">
  <div class="preface group">
    <h2 class="title heading">
      scorpion, before the frog
    </h2>
    <h3 class="byline heading">
      <a rel="author" href="/users/Stratisphyre/pseuds/Stratisphyre">Stratisphyre</a>
    </h3>


        <div class="summary module" role="complementary">
          <h3 class="heading">Summary:</h3>
            <blockquote class="userstuff">
              <p><em>During the Sunshot Campaign, the Two Lords had wed and consolidated their power and authority over their newly joined territory and then shown up to the battlefield astride </em>dragons<em> to win what should have been an unwinnable war. Lan Xichen, the Lord of Jade, was beautiful and possessed a brilliant tactical mind; Nie Mingjue, the Lord of Blades, fierce and formidable. They had collected warriors and rulers to their side in the aftermath, though without the fierce expansionist tendencies against which the war had been fought.</em><br/> </p><p>Two years after the end of the Sunshot Campaign, negotiations commence for the marriage of Jiang Yanli and Jin Zixuan. Caught between his father's ambitions and a family he'd never anticipated finding for himself, Meng Yao finds himself fighting a war against his own nature.</p>
            </blockquote>
        </div>

        <div class="notes module" role="complementary">
  <h3 class="heading">Notes:</h3>





    <blockquote class="userstuff">
      <p>When I first watched CQL, it honestly did not occur to me the first thing I would want to write for it would be MY-centric, and yet here we are. This ended up being far more self-indulgent than intended, but that literally means it fits in with everything else I've ever written. While it is tagged as "Alternate Universe - Canon" please note it is definitely more the former than the latter. </p><p>I have to say that there are tonnes of amazing dragon-based works in this fandom already, and this offering would definitely not exist without the trailblazing efforts that have come before it. </p><p>Please heed the tags, and feel free to ask if there's anything you would like clarification on. Despite this being very AU, I did incorporate a number of canonical themes which I've tried to capture in the tags.</p>
    </blockquote>

    <p class="jump">(See the end of the work for <a href="/chapters/71414454#work_endnotes">more notes</a>.)</p>
</div>

  <div class="chapter preface group" role="complementary">
    <h3 class="title">
      <a href="/works/29091798/chapters/71412687">Chapter 1</a>
    </h3>

    <!-- only display byline if different from the main byline -->


  </div>

  <!--main content-->
  <div class="userstuff module" role="article">
    <h3 class="landmark heading" id="work">Chapter Text</h3>
    <p>When it came to negotiating the marriage of Jiang Yanli and Jin Zixuan, Meng Yao was essential only insofar as his calligraphy remained infallible even under the greatest pressure. And such pressure there was. Not necessarily from the representatives sent by the Two Lords to discuss terms, though they were both obviously accomplished negotiators who took their roles very seriously, but from the insouciant black shadow lounging next to the window across the room. </p>
<p>Wei Wuxian, the only family representative in the room, had everyone guessing. On the one hand, if rumour were to be believed, Sect Leader Jiang rarely left the Unclean Realm since the end of the Sunshot Campaign, an unspoken edict he maintained even in the event of commencing negotiations for his own sister’s marriage contract. On the other hand, Wei Wuxian was her adopted brother, and older than Sect Leader Jiang, though not included in the line of succession. With the major sects still recovering from the Sunshot Campaign, he was probably the one one in any position to represent the interests of the Yunmeng Jiang. And yet he had not said a word the entire morning, save for the brief greeting he’d offered upon arrival. If he did plan to make any procolomations, he’d decided to bide his time. </p>
<p>Meng Yao visibly kept his attention on the scroll before him, following along with the proceedings as closely as humanly possible and with as much detail as possible. It wouldn’t do for anything to be missed, after all, especially not certain clauses that needed to be included, though his father obviously considered them not worth mentioning. An oversight, considering the dignity and prestige of the woman in question, not to mention her… extensive collection of allies. </p>
<p>(It was not an oversight—when the negotiators had mentioned the standard considerations of a marriage contract between equally dignified sects, Jin Guangshan had chuckled and waved a hand and easily conceded, but with a pointed look towards Meng Yao that suggested certain articles be best forgotten. Meng Yao had included them regardless of Jin Guangshan’s  disapproval. The negotiators would be the ones reviewing the document first and omitting them would make Meng Yao look incompetent at best. While there was little in the way that Meng Yao would not allow to win his father’s favour, he drew the line at being seen as incompetent. His aggressive competence was all he had.)</p>
<p>They had been going back and forth little over two hours before a halt for refreshments was called, and Meng Yao was excused to organize the necessary arrangements. He slipped out a discreet side door reserved for servants and made his way down the narrow hallways towards the kitchens. </p>
<p>He emerged in the family courtyard, only to be immediately accosted by an unwelcome voice shouting at him from across the way. </p>
<p>“Meng Yao!” </p>
<p>He closed his eyes a moment in search of inner fortitude, and then turned with a pleasant smile. “Jin Zixun.” He bowed slightly lower than called for, hoping the deference would save him from whatever Jin Zixun wanted of him. </p>
<p>“Any word on the dragons yet?” </p>
<p>Meng Yao’s smile remained frozen in place, even as his gut churned unpleasantly. “Dragons, cousin?” </p>
<p>As expected, Jin Zixun’s face contorted in fury. He fisted a hand in the front of Meng Yao’s robes and pulled him close. “Cousin?” he repeated with a hiss. “You dare speak to me as though we are kin?”</p>
<p>“My apologies,” Meng Yao replied evenly. He aspired to remain neutral in such situations, no matter how frequently they occurred. If anything, it drove Jin Zixun even more furious, from which Meng Yao derived a lot of personal satisfaction.  “I was acting under the assumption that the child of one’s uncle was typically referred to as ‘cousin.’” </p>
<p>“My Uncle hasn’t acknowledged you. The only reason you’re even here is because Zixuan is an idiot.” </p>
<p>Meng Yao sharpened his gaze. “And likewise, Jin Zixuan is the only reason these negotiations are even taking place. Perhaps it might behoove you to remember that, in case he were to overhear you offering him such disrespect.” </p>
<p>Jin Zixun scowled. “Will you answer my question?” </p>
<p>“What question was that?”</p>
<p>“<em>About the dragons</em>!” He shook Meng Yao’s robes, the sudden violent jerk whipping Meng Yao’s neck to the side and pulling the muscles in his neck. He shoved down an undignified sound of pain, bottling it up within his chest as he had every other assault to which he’d been subjected since coming to Koi Tower. </p>
<p>A dagger, such as the one currently concealed within his robes, could put a quick stop to the abuse. His aim with the blade was impeccable; his mother had insisted. He knew exactly where to drive the blade to cripple, to kill, or merely emphasize a point. And for all he clutched those fantasies desperately to his breast, he never acted upon them. Not when his position in Koi Tower remained one of servitude. </p>
<p>Meng Yao fondly thought about the bouncers at the brothel, and their willingness to remove clients who spoke to the women with such disrespect. “At this time, discussions have not reached any considerations of dowry.” </p>
<p>Jin Zixun grimaced in annoyance. “Why not?” </p>
<p>“When the parties involved are gentry, these things take longer.” </p>
<p>Another haughty huff of displeasure. “Maybe I’ll sit in this afternoon.”</p>
<p>“I don’t believe you were invited to attend proceedings, Jin Zixun.” </p>
<p>“I’m the second heir, I do what I want.” </p>
<p>Alas, in Koi Tower, such was the truth of matters. </p>
<p>“If you’d care to join them, then, we are taking a small recess while I arrange for food and drink. I will ensure there is enough for you to partake as well.” </p>
<p>Jin Zixun nodded brusquely. “Good.” He turned on his heel and strode away, rounding the courtyard to approach the meeting room from the family entrance instead. Meng Yao watched him go with no small measure of relief. Nothing had ended in real violence, this time. </p>
<p>“Meng Yao?” </p>
<p>This time, he couldn’t help a roll of his eyes, but at least he was positioned in such a way that it wasn’t observable. At this rate, he’d need to arrange for dinner instead. </p>
<p>When he turned around to face Jin Zixuan, his smile was back in place, composure regained. “Jin Zixuan. I apologize—have I tarried too long? Only, the courtyard is so beautiful.” It was not. The flowers were all transplants from outside Lanling, withering under the oppressive atmosphere of Koi Tower. The gardeners all despaired of succeeding where their frequently replaced predecessors could not.</p>
<p>Jin Zixuan appeared troubled. “Was Zixun bothering you again?” </p>
<p>“I’m certain I don’t know what you mean.” ‘Bothering’ couldn’t be the word, surely, for unrelenting, escalating harassment. Meng Yao’s only reliable shield was forged in and maintained by the strength of his words. </p>
<p>His half-brother’s face drew in consternation, one of his more reliable expressions. “I had thought they would stop, once you proved your worth.” </p>
<p>“My worth is only in that I am a faithful servant to your father.” </p>
<p>The furrow in Jin Zixuan’s brow deepend at the word ‘servant,’ though he did not argue. “Is he always this bad?” </p>
<p>Meng Yao declined to answer; there was nothing he could give. </p>
<p>Frustrated, though Meng Yao could not decipher exactly why, Jin Zixuan shook his head, tossed his hair, and made his way back to the receiving chamber, finally allowing Meng Yao to make his way to the kitchens. Anticipating drawn-out proceedings, he had made earlier arrangements for slightly more substantial fare than one might typically receive between a midday meal and dinner, glad for it when it was presented to the room’s occupants, which now included Jin Zixun. He returned to the table he’d occupied earlier, the ink still drying on the scroll with the first of the clauses, and awaiting further additions. </p>
<p>Surprisingly, Jin Zixuan had moved from his seat at their father’s side. Instead, he had approached their silent guest, who had settled in with a jar of wine. Jin Zixuan whispered with low urgency, attention entirely affixed on Wei Wuxian, who seemed content to maintain his bored stare out the window, which Meng Yao suddenly realized looked out upon the courtyard below, likely having given him a full view of the altercation with Jin Zixun. How mortifying. </p>
<p>“What are you boys whispering about?” Jin Guangshan laughed as the remainder of the party reconvened, a demand carefully concealed in the grin rounding his cheeks. “Certainly nothing that can’t be shared among friends?” </p>
<p>Jin Zixuan turned back and bowed his head, but gave no answer. Wei Wuxian did not bother with acknowledging father at all. Dangerous and stupid, Meng Yao decided. Already a reputation Wei Wuxian carried with him from the war, though he’d seen little proof of either before now. Dangerous to ignore a man as powerful as Sect Leader Jin, stupid to offer insult to the man who would eventually be his sister’s father-in-law. </p>
<p>“Nothing worth mentioning,” Jin Zixuan replied easily, retaking his seat. </p>
<p>Meng Yao blinked, though he did not raise his head. Had… Jin Zixuan just <em>lied</em>? It was smooth, though not effortless in the way Meng Yao deceived the world around him. There was something in his turn of phrase, a deliberate lightness in his words Meng Yao had never heard from his half-brother before. There was no way their father hadn’t noticed—Jin Zixuan was too unpracticed at deception. </p>
<p>Except Jin Guangshan merely chuckled again and applied himself to his cups. “Excellent, then. Shall we proceed?” </p>
<p>Negotiations turned to matters of the wedding itself. It would, of course, be hosted from the Unclean Realm. Regardless of the resources and pretentious magnificence of Lanling, the Unclean Realm had emerged from the Sunshot Campaign as the unequivocal seat of power in their world. It had been requested, and granted, that Jin Zixuan would depart with the negotiators to live there year prior to the actual wedding, to ensure harmony between himself and Jiang Yanli, and give them both a chance to escape the marriage unimpeded if they proved ill-suited to one another. An unusual arrangement, but something to which Jin Guangshan had been obligated to agree before the negotiations even commenced. He’d spent the two years since the end of the Sunshot Campaign pursuing this marriage; by the time the Two Lords agreed to discuss it, he might have agreed to far more. </p>
<p>Unfortunately, neither of the Two Lords were present to curb Jin Guangshan’s obvious ambitions. </p>
<p>“And then, of course, they will return to Koi Tower for their married lives.” </p>
<p>The sound of a wine jar being settled on the windowsill was deafening in the ensuing silence. “No.” Wei Wuxian had a sweet, clear voice that might’ve dripped with actual human shit for all the response it received from Jin Guangshan. His father whipped around to look at the young man, whose eyes had finally turned from the courtyard to the proceedings with every indication that he had been attentive the entire time. Meng Yao decided it was better to err on the side of giving the other man the benefit of the doubt. After all, it was his sister involved. He’d spoken up now that something of matter had been said. </p>
<p>“No?” Jin Zixun repeated. “How dare you say no!” </p>
<p>Unmoved, Wei Wuxian maintained strict eye contact with Jin Guangshan. “My sister and her husband will live out their days in the Unclean Realm, with the rest of our House.” </p>
<p>The Household of the Two Lords. The words hadn’t been bandied about before now, though it rested under the surface of the proceedings; a dangerously sharpened rock hidden by otherwise gentle currents. </p>
<p>“My son is my heir,” Jin Guangshan stated, all levity drained from his voice. “How is he expected to learn the statesmanship required to rule Lanling if he is not in Koi Tower?” </p>
<p>Wei Wuxian stepped towards the table, and as one the negotiators shifted to allow him a spot between them. He settled down easily, resting his sword beside him and drawing his black dizi into his lap, giving Meng Yao the briefest glimpse of the white jade sword token hanging from the end. </p>
<p>Wei Wuxian’s mouth twisted into an affectedly confused moue. “Are you suggesting Sect Leader Jiang is an ineffective ruler, when he remains in the Unclean Realm?” </p>
<p>Meng Yao revised his opinion: dangerous, yes but not stupid. </p>
<p>His father had maneuvered himself into an untenable position with limited options. He might continue to press his point and offer grievous offense by insulting the Household’s youngest ruling member. He could back down and lose face before a man who, despite being a war hero and member of the Household of the Two Lords, remained the subject of frequent whispers about his low parentage. Or he could dismiss negotiations all together and waste away for want of what the Two Lords might offer him personally in terms of prestige and… other considerations. </p>
<p>“Perhaps we might find a compromise,” Meng Yao offered. All eyes turned to him. He had been judicious in his suggestions before now, and made them sparingly. “No one can argue that Sect Leader Jiang governs Yunmeng effectively and fairly. However, he also has the advantage of a very effective regent in Yu Ziyuan, who is more than capable of overseeing small matters in his absence, which is a luxury that will not be afforded to Jin Zixuan in the hopefully far-off event of his assumption of power. Perhaps, if it would be acceptable to everyone, Jin Zixuan and Jiang Yanli might be able to consider the Unclean Realm as their primary residence, with frequent visits to and from Koi Tower throughout the year to allow the heir to remain abreast of the local situation.” </p>
<p>The negotiators looked at Wei Wuxian for approval, further driving home Meng Yao’s decision that despite his silence, the other man had always been the one fully in charge of the situation. Though there was no obvious acknowledgment, the younger of the negotiators turned back to Meng Yao. “How frequent?” </p>
<p>A reasonable schedule was quickly decided upon, which Meng Yao dutifully recorded in its entirety. </p>
<p>Before Wei Wuxian could return to his position at the window, Jin Guangshan decided on another sweeping declaration. </p>
<p>“I must say, when I entered this discussion, it was not with an eye for giving up my only son and heir.” A deliberate jab, since Meng Yao had only managed to argue for three months of the year for the married couple. Meng Yao let the pain of the words flow through and out of him. They didn’t matter. Jin Zixuan stiffened, but before he could speak, their father continued, “Perhaps, now, you might be willing to give up something in return?”</p>
<p>In the ensuing, icy silence, Meng Yao set down his brush. </p>
<p>“My uncle is right,” Jin Zixun continued. “With my cousin going to the Unclean Realm, we lose one of our greatest warriors and most important members of the clan.” Less than a week ago, Jin Zixun had been whining into a cup of wine about what a useless shit he considered Jin Zixuan to be. Meng Yao had overheard the servants speaking of it, and doubtless his half-brother had heard the same based on the cutting look he slid towards Jin Zixun. Something between them had changed during the Sunshot Campaign, though Meng Yao had only heard about it as passing gossip, with nothing in the way of confirmed details. He wasted little mental capacity on it; the war had changed everyone. </p>
<p>“Come to your point,” Wei Wuxian said flatly. </p>
<p>Jin Zixun smirked. “A dragon seems a fair exchange.”</p>
<p>Wei Wuxian’s hand hitting the table seemed to echo in the very air outside Koi Tower, as though he’d bottled thunder and collected it in his palm. “ Dragons aren’t fucking livestock. We do not barter with their lives.” </p>
<p>“Did Nie Mingjue and Lan Xichen not ride them into battle?” Jin Zixun demanded, “As I rode a horse?”</p>
<p>This was the moment where it all fell apart, Meng Yao decided. Jin Zixun’s unique brand of aggressive stupidity would not be forgiven. If he even lived. From the way Wei Wuxian’s hand twisted on his sword’s hilt, there was a chance he’d be dead any second. Would already be dead if Wei Wuxian had the power to kill with his gaze alone. </p>
<p>“Dragons are our honoured equals,” Wei Wuxian snarled out through his teeth. “If they bear a rider, it is of their own volition, and not because they are in any way commanded.”</p>
<p>Zixun, heedless of the danger he was in—on dual fronts, as it seemed that Jin Guangshan was likely to do further violence if this fell through—prepared to reply. </p>
<p>Meng Yao stood. “I’m sure the misunderstanding is on our part, Young Master Wei,” he insisted. Hard eyes turned his way, set in an implacably outraged face. “Our understanding of dragons is limited without exposure to them. We only know of them as creatures of supreme majesty, and did not understand them to be as closely tied to the Household of the Two Lords as you’ve explained. We humbly beg your pardon for our ignorance.” He stood and bowed as deeply as he could without dropping to his knees and pressing his forehead to the floor. If Wei Wuxian would not accept the apology, that would come next. Groveling needed to be approached in steps if it was to be effective; once you were on the floor, there was nowhere else to go.</p>
<p>“A misunderstanding, is it?” Wei Wuxian demanded. The threat of unsatisfied desire for violence stuck in Meng Yao’s throat.</p>
<p>“Of course, Young Master Wei. The Lanling Jin would never offer intentional offense to such distinguished persons, especially not when looking to unify our families.” </p>
<p>There was a short huff of breath. Not haughty, as it might have been from Jin Guangshan or his contingent, but one of a gentler nature, though Meng Yao would hesitate to term it as appeased. </p>
<p>“Fine,” Wei Wuxian finally bit out. “But there will be no more talk, or mention, of the dragons during the course of these talks.” </p>
<p>“Of course, of course. I’m glad we’ve clarified the matter,” Jin Guangshan agreed. </p>
<p>Appeased or not, Jin Zixun’s misstep—likely made at the behest of Jin Guangshan to avoid making the request himself—had drawn Wei Wuxian fully to the table, and Meng Yao had little doubt he would make the rest of negotiations ruthless on behalf of his sister in recompense. He could have been satisfied with the resolutions of the negotiators, if Jin Zixun had not offered such grievous offense. The Lanling Jin would doubtless be made to pay for the trespass.</p>
<p>They did not break for dinner until late in the evening, and even then it was a painfully short meal hastily consumed before returning to the discussion. As expected, Wei Wuxian now fought for his sister the way he had reputedly fought in the Sunshot Campaign: gaining only small inches of ground before a stroke of brilliance maneuvered everything to his satisfaction and he fully claimed the field. His logic was impeccable, and Meng Yao watched with no small interest as he wove a brilliant net around Jin Guangshan with a cunning approach to each point until it seemed likely that the Jin Sect would beggar its coffers to pay for every concession made for the honour of calling Jiang Yanli its mistress. </p>
<p>Meng Yao did what he could to curtail some of the aggravation now leaking through every clause as it became a new battlefield to be won. His father’s negotiators were unaccustomed to anyone arguing with such ruthless efficiency, formerly having enjoyed being the ones with all the leverage. He stepped in more and more, until it became almost exclusively a conversation between him and Wei Wuxian. A surprisingly entertaining one, Meng Yao had to admit. The qualities he prized in himself shifted and reformed into a complementary reflection instead of a direct echo, and it made for a stimulating mental exercise. </p>
<p>He’d paused to commit the last agreement to paper when Wei Wuxian fell abruptly silent. Meng Yao glanced up through his lashes, and caught the tail end of a significant look passed between Jin Zixuan and Wei Wuxian. Wei Wuxian slumped in his seat, his perfect posture crumpling into equable agreeability. </p>
<p>“That’s all, I think,” Wei Wuxian concluded. The very room itself seemed poised to sigh in relief before he straightened and, as an afterthought, tossed out a casual, “Your seneschal is very capable. I’ve appreciated him more with each word.” </p>
<p>It took Meng Yao an embarrassingly long moment to realize Wei Wuxian was speaking about him. </p>
<p>“Meng Yao?” Jin Zixun scoffed. “He’s nothing.” </p>
<p>Meng Yao plastered on his most guileless expression and bowed in his seat. “Your words are too kind, Young Master Wei.”</p>
<p>Wei Wuxian considered him a moment before turning his attention back to Jin Guangshan. “‘Nothing?’ I think you should review the contract and look for all the ways he’s managed to keep Koi Tower on even ground with the Unclean Realm and Yunmeng.” </p>
<p>Meng Yao appreciated that Wei Wuxian was trying to compliment him, but he silently and fervently wished for the other man to shut the fuck up. When he reviewed the contract, all Jin Guangshan would see were the places where Meng Yao had failed to secure Koi Tower the advantage; equal ground would never be an acceptable state of affairs. His retrenchments might have saved the marriage, but it had failed in every other way Jin Guangshan would consider important. </p>
<p>“His administrative uses are often outweighed by the demands he places on my patience,” Jin Guangshan stated. </p>
<p>Meng Yao kept smiling. Needed to keep smiling. He was not a legitimate son, to argue his own virtues. He lived as a servant, unfit to wear the vermillion mark or hold himself up as an equal to those around him. His father frequently dangled legitimization before him as a prize to be won at the cost of his dignity, and while Meng Yao hoped the offers to be sincere, they would not come without a price he’d long ago decided to pay sight unseen. </p>
<p>Wei Wuxian’s lips twisted into a poor imitation of a smile. “Oh? That’s a shame. If you don’t want him, we’ll take him.” </p>
<p>Probably wise Meng Yao had put down his brush, as the statement would have doubtless led to him dropping it and ruining the contract entirely. </p>
<p>Jin Guangshan’s face twisted in confusion. “Why?” The echo of Jin Zixun’s declaration of ‘he’s nothing’ sat heavy in the air. </p>
<p>Wei Wuxian smirked. “Our House appreciates quality wherever it is found.”</p>
<p>“Let them take him, uncle,” Jin Zixun sniffed. “He was always going to end up serving someone in the same capacity as his mother.” </p>
<p>Jin Zixuan rounded on him, but before he could speak, Jin Guangshan’s arm swept through the air. “Now you want both of my sons?” </p>
<p>“Oh, I apologize, Sect Leader Jin, but I believe earlier you said you had only one son and heir. And if his ‘administrative uses are often outweighed by his demands on your patience,’ then won’t I truly be doing you a service in removing him?” Meng Yao paid close attention to Wei Wuxian’s appearance of innocent misunderstanding. Partly because it hurt less than acknowledging to himself what he’d always believed regarding his father’s opinions of him. Partly because it was a truly admirable bit of acting, and Meng Yao thought it a useful expression to have perfected.</p>
<p>He did not anticipate his father ceding the notion. ‘Administrative uses’ was a paltry description of the enormous amount of work Meng Yao did on his father’s behalf, and he’d successfully insinuated himself into almost every aspect of Koi Tower’s daily functions. He rose earlier than anyone, and retired later. He’d taken over the roles of six other individuals in the past year, and his father—while he didn’t appreciate anything else about him—at least understood his usefulness.</p>
<p>This time, Meng Yao decided, his father could muddle his own way out of it. </p>
<p>Except he didn’t. Either exhausted by the entire affair or, more likely, completely indifferent to Meng Yao’s fate, Jin Guangshan ordered him to enter himself into the contract. Meng Yao stared down at the page, jaw clenched. To be <em>given away</em> without any concessions to his value? Had he proved nothing of his usefulness to his father since coming to Koi Tower? </p>
<p>Jin Guangshan coughed pointedly and Meng Yao set brush to paper. He used simple language, as one might describe a single chicken bartered away as an afterthought. Doubtful his father would appreciate it, if he even noticed. </p>
<p>Evening concluded, Meng Yao stood and handed the contract to Wei Wuxian for review, ignoring his father’s call for a last look before it was delivered, and dismissed himself from the room. </p>
<p>It seemed he had to pack.</p><hr/>
<p>When Meng Yao had arrived at Koi Tower, he’d thought very highly of his chances of endearing himself to his father. Surely, after years of war, an unknown son emerging from the ashes like new life would be welcome. Meng Yao had dressed simply in the closest shade to yellow he could find, and walked up the steps with all the confidence of a man triumphantly returning home, a smiling mask already in place to hide everything from his nervous excitement to the anticipation in meeting father to whom he already owed such a great debt. </p>
<p>His trip back down the stairs had been much faster, and far less pleasant. His left knee still ached occasionally. He was well aware that, had things been even slightly less in his favour, he could have been permanently crippled. Killed, even. The Koi Tower stairs had more than a little blood soaked into the steps.. </p>
<p>Meng Yao had pushed himself up and dropped again immediately when he’d placed weight on his left leg. And suddenly there had been a hand under his elbow and a supportive arm to lean his weight against. He’d looked into a deeply concerned, conflicted face that hid itself behind an awkward inability to compose thoughts in such a way as to express them meaningfully. All of which Meng Yao read in that first, fleeting moment when his half-brother helped a complete stranger to his feet. </p>
<p>His first meeting with Jin Zixuan was defined by humiliation and pain and Meng Yao wasn’t sure he could forgive his half-brother the indignity of it. He’d been installed with war-worn healers and Jin Zixuan had somehow argued for him to be graced with the administrative position he’d come to enjoy. Almost. If he had managed to drag himself up and away from Koi Tower, disappeared into the night and found a way to create a name for himself perhaps his father would not now be sending him off as a bargaining chip for his brother’s wedding. </p>
<p>Meng Yao despised uncertainty. He understood himself to be a creature of intense preparation and deeply ingrained habits, all to his detriment as he knew next to nothing about the Household of the Two Lords save what was common knowledge. </p>
<p>During the Sunshot Campaign, the Two Lords had wed and consolidated their power and authority over their newly joined territory and then shown up to the battlefield astride <em>dragons</em> to win what should have been an unwinnable war. Lan Xichen, the Lord of Jade, was beautiful and possessed a brilliant tactical mind; Nie Mingjue, the Lord of Blades, fierce and formidable. They had collected warriors and rulers to their side in the aftermath, though without the fierce expansionist tendencies against which the war had been fought. </p>
<p>Meng Yao spent some idle time speculating on them after learning of Jin Zixuan’s intended betrothal. His half-brother somehow endeared himself to them during the uncertain period where Lanling had hesitated to engage, and came out of it on the other side with every assurance of a welcome suit if he pursued Jiang Yanli after she’d properly mourned the death of her father. </p>
<p>Frustratingly, Meng Yao knew nothing more. Jin Zixun’s suggestive words haunted him. What would they expect of him? A capable administrator? Surely the Household of the Two Lords already had those in scores. Something less seemly? The malice which had leaked from Wei Wuxian at the open insult to the dragons who lived alongside his family chilled his blood. Perhaps the insult itself was the reason Meng Yao would be brought along. Recompense could not be carved from the back of Jiang Yanli’s intended, after all. </p>
<p>His door opened without so much as a cursory knock, and Meng Yao straightened from where he’d crouched over his meagre collection of possessions as his father entered uninvited. He’d never been in Meng Yao’s room. Meng Yao was surprised he’d found it, tucked well back into the servant’s quarters.</p>
<p>“Meng Yao.”</p>
<p>He straightened, resenting the smile he had to plaster across his face. "Sect Leader Jin."</p>
<p>"Father," his father corrected. </p>
<p>Meng Yao's heart stuttered, traitorously hopeful. He’d never been invited to use such a personal address. Was this what he'd had to do to win his father's favour? Simply agree without argument to let himself be sent away and prove his unwavering obedience? He had left prior to the agreements being sealed, perhaps there had been a change at the last moment…</p>
<p>"You will leave with Zixuan in the morning." </p>
<p>Meng Yao inclined his head, resigned. "Of course."</p>
<p>"Being in the Unclean Realm will open up possibilities for you." </p>
<p>A surprisingly kind thing to say. And true, he realized. Koi Tower remained a powerhouse of the cultivation world, but the Unclean Realm? He would be potentially allowed access to the learning and knowledge of the incomparable library at Cloud Recesses. Dignitaries from all across the land visited the Unclean Realm. If Wei Wuxian spoke true and intended to bring Meng Yao along for his administrative capabilities, he might even endear himself to the Two Lords themselves. His father might not wish to acknowledge him, but perhaps this was the next best thing.</p>
<p>"You will find me a way to tame and control a dragon."</p>
<p>The swell of optimism, foolish and temporary as it had been, fled and left him cold and empty. "Sect Leader Jin?"</p>
<p>"Father," Jin Guangshan repeated with an oily smile. "You will be acting as Zixuan's servant, obviously. Do whatever they ask." He did not have to imagine the smirk tugging at his father's mouth. "Make yourself invaluable. Figure out where the dragons are being kept and find a way to bring one under my control."</p>
<p>"I…"</p>
<p>"Having a dragon will put us on equal footing with the Two Lords." The words caught on his teeth in a sneer of contempt.</p>
<p>"But surely the wedding to Jiang Yanli will afford you equal chances for advancement?"</p>
<p>"Are you suggesting a woman has the same value as a dragon." He shook his head and wagged a jovial finger. "Too much time spent at your mother's skirts, I think.” A frequent complaint, often repeated along with the regrettable similarity between Meng Yao’s eyes and his mother’s. “No. It must be a dragon.” </p>
<p>Meng Yao pressed his lips together, as though in thought. He needn’t think it out, he already saw exactly what the likelihood of success was. "And if they catch and kill me in the attempt?" ‘If’ was more than generous. </p>
<p>"Then I will have lost nothing." He placed a heavy hand on Meng Yao's shoulder. "But should you succeed, I will gain a son."</p>
<p>And a dragon, Meng Yao thought through his smile. They were both keenly aware of what mattered more.</p><hr/>
<p>Preparations for his departure took sadly little time. Everything he owned in the world tucked into a qiankun bag with room to spare. Jin Zixuan’s much more substantial collection of belongings took half a dozen men to move. When made his way to the stables the next morning, one of the Unclean Realm’s servants offered him a friendly smile and helped him atop a biddable dark bay mare quite a bit taller than anything he’d ever ridden before.</p>
<p>To the best of his knowledge, the Nie were still the predominant presence in the Unclean Realm. The Lan had yet to fully recover from the burning of Cloud Recesses. They’d been almost entirely wiped out before the Nie had arrived to offer what aid they could and inspired the Sunshot Campaign with a sweeping declaration denouncing Wen Ruohan’s unexpected attack. At the end of it, though Lan Xichen had joined his husband in the Unclean Realm, the Lan had almost entirely retreated into Gusu in favour of rebuilding themselves to their former prominence.</p>
<p>The Nie servants had only just finished packing when they were joined by Wei Wuxian and Jin Zixuan. And, behind them, Jin Guangshan to see them off personally. He met Meng Yao’s eyes and grinned as though the two of them shared a delicious joke before turning to bid farewell to his son. </p>
<p>“We will see you in the summer for the wedding,” he declared with a lusty clap to Jin Zixuan’s shoulder. </p>
<p>“Father,” Jin Zixuan said, bowing deferentially.</p>
<p>Wei Wuxian barely bowed before clamouring up onto a… donkey? </p>
<p>Noting the scrutiny he suddenly enjoyed from everyone gathered, save those he’d brought along with him, Wei Wuxian waved a hand. “I’d never subject a horse to my poor riding.” He dug his heels in and the old thing took off at a reasonable trot. </p>
<p>Meng Yao cast a confused look towards Jin Zixuan. The ride to the Unclean Realm would surely take a week, now, instead of merely a day or two. Jin Zixuan rolled his eyes, shrugged and spurred his own mount into action. </p>
<p>Meng Yao waited for the rest of their small company—Jin Zixuan, Wei Wuxian, the two negotiators and a handful of suspiciously well-armed servants—to precede him before following. He was obviously the lowest member of their party, with his recent… acquisition and uncertain place within the Unclean Realm. In truth, riding at the back didn’t bother him much. He’d slept poorly, and the chance to be alone with his thoughts was an unexpected reprieve. </p>
<p>Also, apparently a short-lived one. </p>
<p>They’d only just passed from the sight of Koi Tower when Wei Wuxian called for him. Meng Yao nudged his mount forward, thighs tightening at the sudden surge of speed as his horse cantered forward to catch up to the front of the group. Despite the donkey’s comparatively slow capabilities, Wei Wuxian had positioned himself at the front, and the group kept to his pace. </p>
<p>“Not used to being on horseback?” Wei Wuxian asked without a second’s thought to propriety or allowing Meng Yao the chance for a proper greeting. </p>
<p>“Not as such,” he replied. </p>
<p>Wei Wuxian laughed, open and genuine. “Me either. Haven’t been allowed on a horse since the war.” </p>
<p>Meng Yao pondered this a moment. “You do not enjoy riding?” </p>
<p>“I used to.” Wei Wuxian’s face was a fascinating landscape of open invitation to camaraderie and far too many obfuscations. “But you’ll find members of our House are fiercely particular in some respects. You can expect Zixuan to have his own ass when he returns to Koi Tower.” </p>
<p>Atop his horse, Jin Zixuan sniffed, but—interestingly—did not deny it. </p>
<p>“Anyway,” Wei Wuxian waved a hand, “You seem a very well-spoken and capable person. I have a mind to ask you some questions if you’re amenable.”</p>
<p>Meng Yao allowed a selfish moment to enjoy being back on familiar footing. “However I can be of service, Young Master Wei.” He doubted very much that the Two Lords desired any particular intel on the inner workings of Koi Tower—not when their dragons could presumably level a playing field completely—but he was prepared to give up incidental knowledge to gain favour with one of their most trusted men. </p>
<p>“Oh, none of that. We’re family, aren’t we?” He peered back over his shoulder. “Or we will be, if the Peacock doesn’t mess up his chances.” </p>
<p>“Wuxian,” Jin Zixuan said, chidingly. There was a… fond?... thrum in his voice. It suggested a closer relationship than Meng Yao had imagined. Of course they had fought together in the Sunshot Campaign, but he hadn’t been made aware of any particular familiarity or connection between them. It bore watching; Jin Guangshan wanted this match for political gain. There was no advantage to be had in anything of a more personal nature. </p>
<p>“I’m sure I don’t know what you mean,” Meng Yao protested. And he truly didn’t. Family? </p>
<p>Wei Wuxian hummed, a sly smile hiding in the corners of his mouth, but let it slip. “You strike me as very good at finding balance between opposing sides. Can I ask your opinion on a trade dispute we dealt with last year? Despite what Xichen-ge claims, I think we were cheated.” </p>
<p>He filed away the soft familiarity with which ‘Xichen-ge’ was spoken and nodded for Wei Wuxian to continue. </p>
<p>The day passed with surprising amicability between him and Wei Wuxian. Even Jin Zixuan offered his own insights once or twice, though Meng Yao noted with no small amount of personal pride that his half-brother often struggled to keep up. When Wei Wuxian finally called the evening’s halt, he grinned at Meng Yao ear-to-ear. </p>
<p>“You’ll do fine,” he claimed. With a complete lack of shamelessness, he squeezed Meng Yao’s arm in an overly familiar manner and moved to coordinate the set up of their small encampment. </p>
<p>This seemed very different from the Wei Wuxian who had attended the negotiations, and Meng Yao’s eyes narrowed for a moment as he tried to puzzle it out. </p>
<p>Another piece betrayed itself later that evening, after they’d set the watch. Supposedly unobserved, he caught sight of Jin Zixuan bowing to Wei Wuxian in a manner which seemed… grateful? He couldn’t see Wei Wuxian’s face, but Jin Zixuan certainly looked oddly relieved. Try as he might, he couldn’t fit it yet, and tucked it away for later examination.</p><hr/>
<p>As anticipated, the journey to the Unclean Realm took an unnecessarily long time. Surprisingly, no one complained—not even Jin Zixuan, of whose patience Meng Yao did not hold in high regard. It was… not unpleasant. Wei Wuxian was a far better conversationalist than literally anyone in Koi Tower and Meng Yao enjoyed the mental acrobatics to which their conversations treated him. It was diverting enough that he barely noticed when they passed into the territories of the Unclean Realm until the fortress itself appeared on the horizon. </p>
<p>Nothing—no paltry description or attempt at art—captured the Unclean Realm in its grandeur. Koi Tower, for all its beauty and grace, lacked the looming presence that pressed into Meng Yao’s bones as they approached. If Koi Tower was an elegant testament to beauty, the Unclean Realm was a mountainous ode sang on behalf of the natural world. It might as well have been carved from a mountain itself, stretching skyward taller than any other manmade monument might claim. </p>
<p>If they noticed the sudden hesitation in his horse’s step, they made no mention of it. </p>
<p>The gates to the Unclean Realm slid open to allow them entry, but Wei Wuxian paused before entering, waiting until Jin Zixuan fell into step with him. </p>
<p>And then, “Come on, Meng Yao!” </p>
<p>Swallowing down the queasiness in his belly, Meng Yao nudged his horse forward. This moment would clarify much of his uncertainty, he decided. It would be in how he was received by the Two Lords, how Wei Wuxian introduced him, how Jin Zixuan addressed him during these precious first encounters. His heart beat thrush-quick and he fought to maintain the pleasantly neutral composure he’d worked all his life to perfect.</p>
<p>“The Unclean Realm has a way of greeting honoured guests,” Wei Wuxian told him as they trotted forward. “You only have to agree if you want to. If you don’t, we’ll find another place for you.”</p>
<p>Before he could puzzle out Wei Wuxian’s meaning, the gates opened to a broad passage where they dismounted before stepping out into a wide courtyard. On the opposite side, spaced out on a much shallower flight of stairs than to which Meng Yao was accustomed, waited two men and a woman. Meng Yao braced himself to meet the Two Lords, and faltered in surprise when he recognized Sect Leader Jiang awaiting them instead, obvious in his personal heraldry and the colours of Yunmeng Jiang. His sister, Jiang Yanli, stood to his right, but to his left… </p>
<p>Meng Yao, mind swirling in panic at the sudden wrong-footedness, did not recognize the other man at all. Dressed in white, and wearing the traditional ribbon of the Lan, he might’ve been the Lord of Jade, but he stood lower than Sect Leader Jiang. </p>
<p>They came to a halt, and Meng Yao and Jin Zixuan dropped into deferential bows. </p>
<p>“Welcome, Young Master Jin Zixuan,” Sect Leader Jiang said. Meng Yao reluctantly rose, back tensed to descend again if he’d straightened too early. “Welcome…”</p>
<p>“Young Master Meng Yao,” Wei Wuxian offered. Meng Yao’s tongue caught in his throat. “He’s come to join our House at my request.” </p>
<p>A lifetime of careful neutrality paid off; Meng Yao was so thrown he didn’t even know what his natural reaction would be.</p>
<p>“And Wei Wuxian,” Sect Leader Jiang continued. His voice was hard, his gaze unforgiving. “You were expected much earlier than this.” </p>
<p>“Lil Apple isn’t afraid of standing still.” Wei Wuxian pouted. “You know I can’t ride a horse.” </p>
<p>Sect Leader Jiang leveled the man beside him with a look of curious irony, though his companion did not acknowledge it with so much as a blink. Without another glance towards Wei Wuxian, Sect Leader Jiang turned his attention to Jin Zixuan.</p>
<p>“Young Master Jin Zixuan, if you are here it means you are prepared to spend a year in this court, in service to the Lord of Jade and the Lord of Blades, proving yourself worthy of my sister. Do you enter the Unclean Realm with a full understanding of this?” It was painfully formal, and not a tradition Meng Yao recognized from his readings of the traditions favoured by the Jiang, Nie or Lan. He was glad to have received Wei Wuxian’s warning. </p>
<p>“I acknowledge this to be true,” Jin Zixuan nodded. He bowed again. </p>
<p>“Young Master Meng Yao,” Sect Leader Jiang continued, “If you are here to join our Household, you are welcome. We ask you for honourable service, and will demand nothing of you that will bring you shame. You are welcome to stay as you like and leave as you will. Do you enter the Unclean Realm with a full understanding of this?” </p>
<p>“I acknowledge this to be true,” Meng Yao lied. </p>
<p>“Wei Wuxian—”</p>
<p>Whatever formal greeting existed between reunited family members was forestalled as a small figured barrelled out of a door on the side of the courtyard with a prolonged and enthusiastic scream of “<em>baba!</em>” </p>
<p>Wei Wuxian spun around and dropped to his knees to collect the small child in a tight embrace. “Radish!” </p>
<p>The child, probably around six years if Meng Yao guessed correctly, proceeded to babble at such speed that the wind itself probably grumbled in envy. Wei Wuxian nodded, following along with every sign of attentiveness until the child had to stop to drag out a breath. </p>
<p>“Uncle was about to tell me my rules,” Wei Wuxian told the child. </p>
<p>“You know your rules, baba,” the child giggled. </p>
<p>“I acknowledge this to be true,” Wei Wuxian said with a playful twist of his mouth. “Hey! Jiang Cheng, is that good enough?” </p>
<p>“You!” Sect Leader Jiang, Jiang Yanli and their companion swept down the stairs as one, though the man robed in white moved a bit quicker. He reached Wei Wuxian and took his wrist, their eyes meeting intensely for a moment before he nodded and offered the smallest twitch of his lips in greeting. </p>
<p>“I am going to eat that stupid donkey,” Sect Leader Jiang grumbled, clapping his brother on the back, any and all offense apparently forgiven. He turned to Jin Zixuan and offered a much more sedate personal greeting. </p>
<p>“Shijie,” Wei Wuxian whimpered imploringly. </p>
<p>But it seemed Jiang Yanli’s eyes were only for Meng Yao’s brother. Jin Zixuan, similarly captivated, smartly remained silent instead of ruining the moment by saying something idiotic, as he was rumoured to do when flustered. Having never seen him around a woman in which he’d expressed any interest, Meng Yao was curious to see how true the words might prove.</p>
<p>“Welcome home,” she whispered. </p>
<p>Jin Zixuan’s hands twitched towards her, but at Sect Leader Jiang’s pointed cough they fell resolutely to his side. Instead, he opened his mouth and Meng Yao braced himself. </p>
<p>“I am <em>so</em> pleased to be here,” he replied. Levelly. A completely acceptable response without offering unintentional insult or disparaging the lady at all. What a shocking and unexpected development. If the mudslinging were to be believed, he was incapable of stringing together a single sentence without offering offense.</p>
<p>“Were you good for a-die, radish?” Wei Wuxian asked. He punctuated his question with a kiss to the other man’s cheek. It lingered, and Meng Yao diverted his eyes when it threatened to last longer than was appropriate for him to observe. </p>
<p>“A-Yuan is always good,” the man assured him. Wei Wuxian’s smile threatened Meng Yao’s eyes with its brightness. He turned away, which had the adverse effect of drawing the attention of the small crowd. </p>
<p>“Lan Zhan, A-Cheng, shijie, come and meet Meng Yao.” Wei Wuxian turned the full intensity of his attention to Meng Yao. “You should have seen it. If we hadn’t had such good negotiators on our side, he would’ve taken the Unclean Realm for everything including the bed linens.” </p>
<p>Meng Yao dropped his eyes to the ground. “Young Master Wei  is too generous.” </p>
<p>It was a strange experience, being formally introduced to Sect Leader Jiang, Jiang Yanli, and Lan Wangji, the brother of the Lord of Jade and—more importantly according to Wei Wuxian—Wei Wuxian’s husband. The atmosphere was less restrained than it had been during the earlier greeting, a deep feeling of camaraderie Meng Yao found puzzling. </p>
<p>Speculation around the presence of the Jiang siblings in the Unclean Realm suggested they were hostages, kept on a short leash to ensure the peace left in the wake of the Sunshot Campaign lasted. Sect Leader Yao, whenever he visited Koi Tower, was effusive in his complaints about it. When Wei Wuxian spoke of their House, Meng Yao thought it to be coded language. He wasn’t accustomed to being incorrect.</p>
<p>“And you should have heard his ideas on the trade routes we established along the river last year. I told you we were being cheated.” Wei Wuxian smacked Sect Leader Jiang’s chest. Meng Yao felt dangerously and completely out of his depth. He was aware that he had taken certain liberties in Koi Tower in the hopes of being seen as family, but nothing extended to treating anyone of such dignified personage with such casual familiarity.</p>
<p>“He’s very good,” Jin Zixuan echoed. </p>
<p>Thank heavens Meng Yao was saved from having to figure out how to feel about <em>that</em> by Jiang Yanli offering to have him shown to his rooms to rest after his journey. </p>
<p>Jiang Yanli offered a small smile of commiseration, and Meng Yao found himself considering Jin Zixuan’s desire to have her as a bride, for the first time wondering if it was the politically-motivated arrangement Jin Guangshan believed. Jiang Yanli was fair, but forgettable. His mother would have said she’d only stand out in a room that lacked any true beauties. Yet there was an open kindness to her eyes he found compelling, after living so long in Koi Tower where such things needed to be ruthlessly suppressed to avoid being shattered against colder realities.</p>
<p>Led through a maze of corridors—the Unclean Realm, truly, was more of a city than a single fortress—he did not notice the quality of the lodgings until he was shown to an impressive suite that made his breath catch. There was no real finery, but the space was pleasantly open and the obvious pride of craftsmanship in everything from the tables to the painted privacy screens was nothing less than breathtaking. There was a full sitting room, replete with a well-stocked desk and greeting area, with a second area off the side obviously designed for sleeping. </p>
<p>“Lady Jiang, I think there’s been some mistake. This looks like a room for family members.” </p>
<p>Jiang Yanli inclined her head. “Of course, Young Master Meng. You are A-Xuan’s brother, are you not?” </p>
<p>How did she know that? There had been no mention of their familial relationship during introductions, and regardless, “I have been brought here to assist with administrative duties.” </p>
<p>Her smile was small and sad. “You are a member of our House, now. And you are family.” She bowed over her hands. “I’ll leave you to collect yourself. When you’re ready, we would be happy to sit with you.” </p>
<p>How strange, Meng Yao thought as she left him standing along in a room larger than he’d ever been allowed to call his own, that his hands were shaking so badly. He tucked them deep into his sleeves and allowed a moment to collect himself, as she had suggested.</p><hr/>
<p>Collecting himself took longer than anticipated, and by the time he believed himself capable of conducting himself to the standards he considered acceptable, it was nearly time for the evening meal. He dressed in his finest robes which, to be fair, were still nowhere close to what he should be wearing to meet the Two Lords. He did his best to straighten them, prepared his most pleasing expression, and made his way into the corridors to find the main hall, glad Jiang Yanli had pointed it out to him in passing.</p>
<p>In Koi Tower, dinners were lavish affairs attended by servants in attire designed to appeal to his father's sensibilities. He guessed, based on their reputation, that the Two Lords would value austerity, and that the courses would offer nutrition over enjoyment. However, based on what he'd experienced so far, he was willing to temper those assumptions for the moment. Nothing about the Unclean Realm had been as expected, and he was tired of feeling out of his depth.</p>
<p>The main hall was decorated with the heraldry of the Two Lords, as expected, and while it was certainly large enough to host a healthy crowd, only six people occupied the table closest to the two empty thrones at the head of the room.</p>
<p>Wei Wuxian caught sight of him and waved him into one of the free seats at the table.</p>
<p>He bowed, as was proper, before taking the seat beside Jin Zixuan, across from A-Yuan and his fathers. There was one noticeably empty seat at the other end of the table, beside Sect Leader Jiang.</p>
<p>The rapid fire conversation between the man himself and Wei Wuxian barely paused at his arrival, though the latter spared him a welcoming grin.</p>
<p>He leaned closer to Jin Zixuan, "Will our hosts be joining us tonight?"</p>
<p>"Probably not for a month or more, as I understand," his half-brother helpfully supplied. "They're addressing some sort of border skirmish in the north."</p>
<p>Well, that would give Meng Yao a decent amount of time to find his footing, not to mention begin his cursory search of the Unclean Realm for evidence of the dragons. Doubtless they had accompanied their riders, but if he could find where they were kept he might find some clue as to how they could be tamed.</p>
<p>The meal was good. Less refined than those served under his father’s roof, but pleasingly spiced. He noted that three of the table’s occupants added heaping spoonfuls of roasted chilis to their dish, though his brother and Lan Wangji abstained. A-Yuan helped himself to a bite from Wei Wuxian’s plate and then to the entirety of Lan Wangji’s tea. Meng Yao smiled into his own bowl before he noticed he was doing so. </p>
<p>“Meng Yao, if you do have some thoughts on improving our trade agreements with the Yao I’d love to hear them tomorrow if you’re inclined to share your time,” Sect Leader Jiang said.</p>
<p>“This one would be honoured to offer any and all assistance,” Meng Yao agreed. Sect Leader Jiang’s face twitched into a small frown. Not a man for demure acceptance, then. Perhaps Meng Yao could have anticipated this, based on his experiences with Wei Wuxian. “I understand you’ll soon be entering into discussions with the Su as well.” </p>
<p>“Unfortunately,” Wei Wuxian rolled his eyes and leaned over to poke Lan Wangji over A-Yuan’s head. Lan Wangji easily caught his hand before it found its mark upon his cheek. “Lan Zhan, you also wanted a new tutor for A-Yuan, didn’t you? Meng Yao would be well-suited for the calligraphy bits. I’ve never seen writing so fine.” </p>
<p>“Once again, Young Master Wei is too kind,” Mang Yao said. </p>
<p>Before more could be spoken, another man swept into the room, a full course late for dinner. He plopped himself down into the last remaining seat and slumped over into the Sect Leader Jiang’s side. “Jiang Cheng, why is my life so hard?” </p>
<p>Sect Leader Jiang inspected the ceiling, possibly in search of forbearance. “I don’t want to know, Huaisang.” </p>
<p>“But Da-ge isn’t here, and I don’t have anyone else to complain to.” </p>
<p>“You’ve never seemed to mind the sound of your own voice, so I don’t know why you can’t talk to yourself.” </p>
<p>“Jiang Yanli, tell your brother to stop saying such cruel things to me. He’s supposed to be representing Xichen-ge and Da-ge while they’re gone and should be better tempered.” </p>
<p>“Hey, hey, hey, he’s nicer to you than he is to me,” Wei Wuxian pointed out. </p>
<p>“That’s because you would drive a monk to madness,” Huaisang said. He noticed Meng Yao, apparently for the first time, and straightened. “My apologies. We’re unaccustomed to guests, and this one frequently forgets his manners.” </p>
<p>“Nie Huaisang,” Sect Leader Jiang hissed. Ah. The Lord of Blades’ brother, about which little was known save for his reputation for weak cultivation. Privately, Meng Yao wished he might have attended at least one Discussion Conference in the past, if only to have seen the members of the Household in person before now. Even Jiang Wanyin and Jiang Yanli were often in attendance, despite their reluctance—forbiddance?—to leave the Unclean Realm.</p>
<p>“He learned that tone from Da-ge,” Wei Wuxian muttered.</p>
<p>“Wei Wuxian!” </p>
<p>“Boys,” Jiang Yanli said calmly. They all settled, suitably chastened. “Young Master Meng Yao is Zixuan’s brother, Huaisang, and has come to join our House.”</p>
<p>Nie Huaisang sniffed. “Better here than Koi Tower, I suppose.” He peered at Meng Yao consideringly. “Do you enjoy painting?” </p>
<p>Meng Yao tilted his chin down. “I have no talent for it.” </p>
<p>“Ah, ah, not the same thing,” Nie Huaisang said. “What about music? Do you play anything?” </p>
<p>“Unfortunately not.” </p>
<p>“Meng Yao was not fortunate enough to have much opportunity for leisurely activities, before,” Jin Zixuan said. Meng Yao blinked at his dinner and waited for the ensuing proclamation: he was here to work. “I’m hoping that will change.” </p>
<p>“It needs to, especially if he’s going to be sitting with us at meals. Ugh, could you imagine having nothing at all of substance to discuss?” </p>
<p>“We’ve eaten with you often enough there’s no need to imagine,” Sect Leader Jiang grumped. </p>
<p>“Jiang Cheng!” </p>
<p>Meng Yao allowed a moment to admit he had not anticipated the brother of the Lord of Blades to be quite so… foppish. Of course, everyone told and retold escalating and extravagant stories of Sect Leader Jiang and the dashing Wei Wuxian. Besides the Two Lords, no one else had managed to glean such a reputation during the Sunshot Campaign, a point of irritation to the Jin, who often demanded Jin Zixuan’s own contributions to be equally spoken of, for all they had failed to be as significant. </p>
<p>At the end of the meal, Wei Wuxian and Lan Wangji scooped up A-Yuan to ferry him to bed, though not before the child wished everyone sweet dreams. He continued to be impossibly adorable. Meng Yao enjoyed the simplicity of children, though he rarely had cause to interact with them these days. He decided he would not mind if Lan Wangji took Wei Wuxian’s suggestion of engaging Meng Yao in some capacity as a tutor. </p>
<p>Jin Zixuan walked Meng Yao back to his room after bidding his intended a sweet farewell at a respectable distance, under the watchful eye of her younger brother.</p>
<p>“I…” He paused when they reached Meng Yao’s door. “I hope you can be happy here, Meng Yao.” He coughed, looked at his feet and then regarded the ceiling for a moment before soldiering on. “...brother.” </p>
<p>Meng Yao’s eyes widened so far he worried for the integrity of his retinas. </p>
<p>Jin Zixuan nodded stiffly. “That is all.” He coughed once more and briskly took off down the hallway. He paused at the end of the corridor, turned back, and—eyes fixed directly forward—made his way to the door across from Meng Yao’s before nodding a final time and letting himself inside. </p>
<p>Struck completely dumb for the first time in his life, Meng Yao entered his room and barely made it to the nearby desk to lower himself down instead of plopping down indecorously to the floor. </p>
<p>Brother. Not the bastard son of Jin Guangshan, nor the semi-indentured servant purchased along with the marriage contract. <em>Brother</em>. </p>
<p>What about this place inspired madness among its occupants? And was Meng Yao in danger if he remained?</p><hr/>
<p>Before coming to Koi Tower to introduce himself, Meng Yao had worked tirelessly to gather all the information he possibly could on his father and his father's family. He spent what little coin he had left after the trip from Yunping in wine houses, buying rounds to loosen knowledgeable tongues. He learned of no less than three other illegitimate children, countless mistresses, and surprisingly considering a man of his father's particular passions, only a single heir. </p>
<p>Jin Zixuan, they said well into their first jar, was a skilled warrior. A testament to the power and dignity of Koi Tower. He fearlessly led his father's army to battle against Wen Ruohan and was present when the last blow ended the Sunshot Campaign.</p>
<p>Jin Zixuan, they said after their third jar, was hopeless with women, and if left to his own devices the Jin name would crumble for want of his finding a wife to tolerate him.</p>
<p>Jin Zixuan, they slurred after the sixth jar, was a coward who spent a month of the war hiding from.combat until the Two Lords had all but guaranteed victory, at which point he crawled out from whatever rock under which he'd hidden to stand alongside them.</p>
<p>Meng Yao had expected a craven, preening milksop whose skills were suited to a training yard instead of a battlefield. </p>
<p>The hypothesis seemed accurate at first glance. Jin Zixuan proved conceited, certainly, and incredibly skilled with the blade. Arrogant in that he had returned to Koi Tower a war hero, though without a reputation close to rivaling that of Wei Wuxian, lacking the insistence on the dramatic that drove Wei Wuxian's exploits towards inconceivability.</p>
<p>It all left Meng Yao wholly unprepared for the unexpected kindness the other man showed at the bottom of the Koi Tower steps. While the healers reset his knee, Meng Yao allowed that the drunken rumours had not painted a full picture, and wondered what else they might have overlooked.</p>
<p>That night, awake as he listened to the wind whistling outside his window, Meng Yao pondered the rest of it. Most of Jin Zixuan's reputation had been built up before the Sunshot Campaign. At Koi Tower, he leaned into it, albeit unintentionally, through remaining aloof from everyone around him.</p>
<p>Perhaps here, in the Unclean Realm, Meng Yao would find an unexpected opal concealed by ugly stone.</p>
<p>He slept fairly well, and rose early to find a simple breakfast waiting outside his door. He ate quickly and then left in search of occupation. He'd planned to begin his search after becoming acquainted with the basic layout; less chance of stumbling upon something he couldn't easily explain away without having to grovel in a humiliating fashion to avoid penalization.</p>
<p>Draconic imagery decorated the Unclean Realm in quiet dignity. No doubt, when his father possessed one of the dragons, there would be nothing save ostentatious displays reminding all and sundry of Jin grandeur. Here, the effect was subtle. Beams with the finest carved detail of scales. Wood painted a touch darker with the picture of a flank or claw. Instead of making the place oppressive, it made it majestic in ways that could not have been anything other than carefully considered ornamentation. </p>
<p>Following a long painted line of a dragon’s flank out onto a long balcony lining the outside wall, Meng Yao immediately dropped into a bow when he found himself face-to-face with an imposing figure bedecked in purple.</p>
<p>“Forgive this one, Sect Leader Jiang,” Meng Yao said. “I was only looking around.”</p>
<p>“Enough of that,” Sect Leader Jiang snapped, surprisingly irritated by the appropriate deference. He waited for Meng Yao to rise. “You and I will be family soon enough.” He paused and huffed a breath. “You may refer to me as Jiang Wanyin, if you wish.” </p>
<p>“Jiang Wanyin, then,” Meng Yao repeated, earning himself a nod and a small twist of the lips that might’ve been called a smile if it hadn’t been set beneath such a cross brow. </p>
<p>Jiang Wanyin returned his attention to the courtyard below, a spacious area filled with greenery and a calm air. “So, do you want to tell me why Wei Wuxian actually brought you here, or are people going to make me keep guessing?” </p>
<p>“I believe I impressed him with my words during the negotiations over your sister’s marriage contract.” </p>
<p>Jiang Wanyin thought it over. “Possibly. He’s always surprised when he’s not the smartest man in the room and he makes stupid decisions when surprised.” Jiang Wanyin gritted his teeth and turned his face towards Meng Yao. “Not that bringing you here was a stupid decision. I’m sure you’re very capable.” </p>
<p>“Thank you. I shall do my best.” Meng Yao tucked the morsel of insight to the back of his mind for later. “Did you care to look over the trade agreements?” </p>
<p>“If you don’t mind.” Jiang Wanyin took off along the walkway, and Meng Yao followed slightly behind him until Jiang Wanyin cut him a stern look and they fell into step together. “I’m not the one who will be conducting negotiations if there are any changes, hopefully. Xichen-ge is usually the one to handle such matters. Mingjue claims his temper runs too hot, though he has a good hand at diplomacy when he puts a mind to it.” </p>
<p>“Forgive me for asking, Jiang Wanyin, but I am not altogether familiar with the politics of the Unclean Realm.” Indeed, few people were, which led to a simply marvellous amount of speculation. “Are you not also capable of conducting such business?” </p>
<p>Jiang Wanyin’s mouth twisted, this time in a real smile. “I am. And were the discussions with regards to Yunmeng, I would do so without hesitation. But this involves Qinghe, and I happily cede the honour.” Interesting, for all they still claimed Gusu retained its sovereignty, that the Sect Leader conducted business on behalf of the Nie.</p>
<p>“Is it hard governing so far from your seat of power? Only,” Meng Yao hurried to add, “I wonder if my… if Jin Zixuan won’t find it equally difficult.” </p>
<p>“The benefits to being here far outweigh the difficulties,” Jiang Wanyin replied wryly. </p>
<p>“Of course.” A non-answer, unfortunately, but it left an opening at least. “May I ask about your decision to remain in the Unclean Realm, then? There was very little in the way of convincing reports after the war to confirm any accounts.” </p>
<p>“What do they say?” </p>
<p>“Only that the Two Lords make a habit of collecting rulers and war heroes to their side,” Meng Yao replied. </p>
<p>“I suppose they do. Any reasons speculating as to why?” </p>
<p>“None that can be repeated in polite company.” Jiang Wanyin guffawed, and Meng Yao half-tripped over himself at the sound, “I’m sorry, I speak out of turn.” </p>
<p>“Not at all. It’s refreshing.”</p>
<p>It certainly was; Jiang Wanyin seemed the sort of man to whom one could endear themselves through sly jokes made unexpectedly. Meng Yao would present a quiet and respectful young man who occasionally offered up amusing commentary in a sotto voice. Jiang Wanyin would come to see him as someone he could trust without fear of reprisal, for nothing bound two people together quite like a secret. In this case, the secret—as far as Jiang Wanyin would be concerned—would be the sense of humour hidden behind a placid expression. </p>
<p>He trailed Jiang Wanyin through the Unclean Realm, listening attentively as the other man helpfully pointed out places of interest, mapping out the hallways and labyrinthine corridors. Unlike Koi Tower, Jiang Wanyin had no forbidding words or threats regarding where Meng Yao was permitted to go. That wasn’t to suggest a dearth of hidden rooms. Jin Guangshan kept a number available for housing his mistresses—one of Meng Yao’s less desirable duties had been coordinating the rotation of women through his father’s good graces, removing the unfortunate discards and their possessions and installing new ones in the private chambers. It probably partly explained why Madam Jin hated him so intensely. Presumably the Unclean Realm already had someone on hand for such situations, if they were at all necessary. He’d never bothered to ascertain whether Jin Guangshan’s proclivities were common practice among the gentry, or particular to the man himself.</p>
<p>They ended up in a small reception room, and Jiang Wanyin poured them both tea before settling down to discuss the particulars. Very interesting. Meng Yao admitted to some astonishment that, regardless of what he’d said, a Sect Leader served him tea. While the reach of the Yunmeng Jiang did not expand over a significant area—certainly not compared to the combined area of Qinghe and Gusu—he was a ruler, and yet all his behaviours suggested it was a title as ill-fitting as a child trying on his parent’s robes. He spoke with authority, but actions did not suit words. Jin Guangshan would never lower himself to pour tea for anyone, even someone who could be described as an equal. </p>
<p>This, Meng Yao decided, was knowledge he could apply with practical application when convenient. A carefully placed “gege” here or there, once their relationship was more established, would likely yield some wonderful results. Especially with his seemingly tumultuous relationship with Wei Wuxian. </p>
<p>“It’s an acquired taste,” he warned Meng Yao. “Be warned.” </p>
<p>At the first touch of the tea to his lips, Meng Yao hummed in what he hoped sounded like polite surprise. From the way Jiang Wanyin smirked, he’d likely missed ‘polite’ by a mile. The tea licked at his lips like the brush of a burned branch and left behind a charred aftertaste he found himself wincing through under Jiang Wanyin’s amusement. </p>
<p>“It’s fortifying.” </p>
<p>“One of the kinder words for it. I try to bring in Yunmeng leaves, but my sister and Wei Wuxian hoard them like gold. And you might as well drink water instead of the Gusu blends.</p>
<p>“Now, then. Let’s get to work.” </p>
<p>They made decent progress. Jiang Wanyin’s politics were not as ruthless as those of Koi Tower, and he appeared willing to make more concessions—“might as well, before Xichen returns and makes them anyway”—but evened them out with balanced requests as well. </p>
<p>An hour later, while elbow-deep in the proposal around mining compromises, Nie Huaisang sailed into the room in a cloud of floral-scented air. Meng Yao stood and bowed, though his companion remained seated and, to all appearances, unimpressed.</p>
<p>“Jiang Cheng! This is a completely unacceptable violation of the respect due to me as a member of this house.” </p>
<p>“You’re exaggerating,” Jiang Wanyin replied.</p>
<p>“I haven’t even told you what it is.” </p>
<p>“I can confidently say that it doesn’t matter.”</p>
<p>Nie Huaisang’s mouth shifted into an angry moue. “You are not funny.” </p>
<p>Jiang Wanyin offered no reply and Nie Huaisang huffed. Then, almost as an afterthought, he looked towards Meng Yao. “I suppose we can discuss it later. Are you done with Young Master Meng? I want to have a conversation with someone I haven't seen every day for the past two years.”</p>
<p>“No I’m not. Why don’t you go bother Jin Zixuan?” </p>
<p>“I already did. He wanted my help writing Jiang Yanli a love poem. I told him the only poetry I wrote is dirty limericks and he took off before I could recite one. Probably because he knew you'd kill him.”</p>
<p>“Damn right I would. What’s he doing writing her poetry anyway? He shouldn't even be talking to her.”</p>
<p>Hesitant to insert himself, but feeling an unexpected rush of empathy for his… brother, Meng Yao offered, “Well, they are engaged.” </p>
<p>“And he thinks that gives him the right to take liberties?” Meng Yao blinked. Liberties… such as talking to her? While he was shocked at all that Jin Zixuan was capable of conducting a conversation when not explicitly discussing anything of an official capacity, he couldn’t help but wonder if Jiang Wanyin understood the point of Jin Zixuan’s year of residence. “I'm going to find Wei Wuxian so we can go remind him of the discussion we had after the war.”</p>
<p>Nie Huaisang grinned. “Oh, good, then you won't mind me taking Young Master Meng.” He snuck a hand under Meng Yao’s elbow. “Come along. You can give me your frank and honest opinion of the fan I’m working on.” </p>
<p>The fan in question, once Meng Yao had been dragged halfway across the Unclean Realm to a much more decorative living space, was without question the most hideous thing he’d ever seen. The colours—garishly pigmented and thrown together on the fan in a poor representation of a… bird? Snake? He honestly couldn’t say with any confidence what he was supposed to be looking at. The one very minor positive he could glean from it came from the fact he would never himself have to use it. </p>
<p>“Well?” Nie Huaisang demanded. </p>
<p>“Did you paint it yourself?” Meng Yao questioned. </p>
<p>Nie Huaisang blinked. “Does it matter?” When Meng Yao turned his eyes towards him, he waved the much more tasteful fan in his hand and laughed. “Of course, of course. I did.” </p>
<p>“Ah. I can see the evidence of very dedicated craftsmanship.” </p>
<p>Nie Huaisang hummed. “A very diplomatic answer. What else?” </p>
<p>“Your use of colour is very bold.” </p>
<p>“Do you like it?” </p>
<p>“...” Meng Yao bit down on his lower lip before reluctantly pasting on a smile and nodding. </p>
<p>His cheerful smile increased tenfold in intensity and he flapped the fan in his hand effusively. “I appreciate it, Young Master Meng.” He took the fan and returned it to its spot on his desk. “Would you like some tea?” </p>
<p>“Oh, I couldn’t.” He’d finished the single cup Jiang Wanyin poured for him earlier, and had not requested a refill. </p>
<p>“I do happen to have a more delicate blend if that suits your taste.”</p>
<p>Meng Yao’s smile shifted closer to genuine. “Well. In that case.” </p>
<p>He spent an hour listening to the other man talk with very little to show for it, save the much more pleasant lingering of flowery notes left on his tongue. Nie Huaisang talked much and said little, and even Meng Yao’s most careful attempts at gleaning information about the Unclean Realm was met with a flap of his fan or a shake of his head. A man of good breeding, obviously, his manners were impeccable, and he did offer up commentary that had Meng Yao hiding a chuckle behind his sleeve more than once. Unfortunately, amusing observations seemed to be all he was good for. </p>
<p>Once Nie Huaisang released him, Meng Yao spent the remainder of his day continuing his explorations of the Unclean Realm. The family living quarters were all tucked higher up in the mountains’ embrace, leaving the broad main fortress standing tall as an entryway. He thought about making his way down, but hesitated. He found it more than likely the dragons stayed in the main compound, but it wouldn’t hurt to have a thorough knowledge of the rest of the city before continuing in his explorations. </p>
<p>He hadn’t expected to be summoned for the evening meal, but yet again found himself tucked in beside Jin Zixuan, who was looking across the table at Wei Wuxian and Jiang Wanyin with poorly-veiled annoyance. On the other hand, the brothers appeared positively delighted. Wei Wuxian scooped a healthy pile of food onto his plate, all elbows and shaking mirth.</p>
<p>Jiang Yanli joined them in short order, tucked in against Lan Wangji and holding A-Yuan’s hand in her own. She alighted down beside her betrothed and smiled sweetly across the table at her brothers. </p>
<p>“I understand the three of you spent time together today,” she said with a gracious smile. “I’m glad everyone is getting along. It would be a shame if there were any misunderstandings.” Slowly, the good humour leaked from Wei Wuxian and Jiang Wanyin’s expressions. While Lan Wangji, directly across from Meng Yao, remained to all appearances unaffected, there was a lightness in his expression Meng Yao couldn’t help but think indicated amusement. “Of course, A-Cheng and A-Xian both know I am capable of protecting my own heart.” </p>
<p>Lan Wangji took the forgotten spoon from Wei Wuxian’s unmoving hand and served A-Yuan. </p>
<p>“Yes, definitely shijie!” Wei Wuxian scrambled.</p>
<p>“Without doubt,” Jiang Wanyin nodded frantically. </p>
<p>“We all know you to be very capable,” Jin Zixuan agreed, gracious enough not to be smug in his victory.</p>
<p>She hummed and took a sip of her tea.</p><hr/>
<p>Meng Yao enjoyed routines when he could. At the brothel, as a child, he had created a set schedule for himself. The Madam often required assistance with mindless chores she hesitated to pay money for when a perfectly able-bodied boy would do. Afterwards, he spent his mornings sitting outside a local home, listening to the tutor school the children within. Afternoons he dedicated himself to reading where he could. Evenings found him tucked into a small room above the brothel’s main floor, eyes closed as he tried meditating or imagining himself elsewhere. He generally fell asleep against the wall, and often woke up back in his mother’s room tucked into his bed before doing it all again. He established routines even more quickly in Koi Tower, proactively checking and rechecking on administrative matters before they could escalate into problems. </p>
<p>In the Unclean Realm, with nothing but endless free time on his hands, he found himself at odds and anxious. He walked the corridors at night to give himself a good understanding of the walls around him. Footpaths darted out between the living quarters, hewn from the stone and forests surrounding the Unclean Realm and pressing the scent of mountain air and greenery into his skin and lungs. The pathways led deeper into the mountain range, and he thought a few times of exploring further afield, until reminding himself that walking through such terrain in the dark was more likely to end with a broken neck instead of advanced understanding. </p>
<p>Solitary walks aside, he found himself itching for occupation. Thus, when Wei Wuxian and Lan Wangji sought him out a week after his arrival and tentatively asked if he wouldn’t mind assuming some role in tutoring A-Yuan, he jumped at the opportunity. </p>
<p>Supposedly, his duties extended only to calligraphy, as others had taken charge of the sundry education expected of a young master. However, A-Yuan was bright and biddable, and absorbed everything Meng Yao had to say, despite his young age. Soon enough, their lessons became longer and extended into history and what might generously be termed as philosophy, if one could claim to teach philosophy to anyone under the age of ten. He tried to make it a game, posing questions in such a way that A-Yuan could consider them in the context of a young mind and give them thought. He might not be the most robust educator, but from the serene set to Lan Wangji’s cool demeanor when he retrieved A-Yuan at the end of the day, it seemed to please. </p>
