<p>A fortnight into his stay at the Unclean Realm, after Meng Yao had wound his way around his usual paths—he could not claim it was in the name of exploration any longer, but he still enjoyed the calm night air and solitary walks surrounded on all sides by the barely-tamed wilderness around them—he froze when he reached the edge of the treeline and found himself looking at the back of Lan Wangji’s broad, white-clad shoulders. </p>
<p>He remained at a distance, and pressed himself against one of the thick-trunked trees to avoid being seen. In all his days within the realm, he’d never seen Lan Wangji out so late. Wei Wuxian constantly laughed about his husband’s strict adherence to an early bedtime, nudging Men Yao and inviting him to share in the joke. </p>
<p>Lan Wangji looked up towards the peaks surrounding them and Meng Yao craned his neck to follow his gaze. It didn’t take long for him to see the trail of white, which he initially mistook for a wisp of cloud until he noticed the weaving movements carrying it against the gentle night wind. </p>
<p>Already far enough away to make it hard to see despite the generous light offered by the full moon, Meng Yao finally beheld the dragon. He could make out no details, save for the way its silvery body caught the moonlight and held it as though it were made of moonbeams itself, but seeing it at all made his breath catch in his throat. He watched it until it disappeared over the mountaintops, sharing the moment with Lan Wangji, who seemed similarly disposed. </p>
<p>He ducked back behind the tree once the dragon vanished, narrowly avoiding being spotted by Lan Wangji when he turned to go. There was a bundle caught up in his arms; Meng Yao only noticed a glimpse of it before he had to shuffle backwards to avoid discovery. </p>
<p>He waited, concealed by the trees, long enough for Lan Wangji to make it halfway down the mountain before creeping back to his room to write a letter to his father. </p>
<p>Despite the coded language, Jin Guangshan would doubtless understand what Meng Yao had to convey; he’d written before, but briefly and with no substantial details. After all, he reasoned, his father had no designs on the Unclean Realm itself, only the dragons within. He spoke exclusively about Jin Zixuan and the duty Jin Guangshan had impressed upon him, all language and allusions easily denied if the letter was intercepted. His father would understand. </p>
<p>The next morning, another boy joined A-Yuan in his lessons, walking confidently alongside Lan Wangji into the classroom. Like Lan Wangji and A-Yuan, he wore the Lan’s style of well-made white robes and a forehead ribbon, though his was slightly askew. Like A-Yuan, an accompanying sash of dark purple etched with turquoise thread marked him as a part of the Jiang family. Very curious. </p>
<p>“Young Master Meng, may I introduce Lan Jingyi. He will be staying with us from now on. If you have no objections to taking on another pupil, we would appreciate him being invited to join A-Yuan in his lessons.” </p>
<p>The boy was, perhaps, a year older than A-Yuan, and immediately greeted Meng Yao with a delighted grin and cheerful wave. His size suited the bundle Meng Yao had witnessed Lan Wangji carrying the night before, though he couldn’t imagine what the connection was between him and the dragon. </p>
<p>“I am of course honoured to be entrusted with the education of another young mind,” Meng Yao said with a slight bow. </p>
<p>The honour was soon overwhelmed by the utter disruptive chaos his new charge brought to proceedings. </p>
<p>This was not to say that Lan Jingyi was not a bright, charming child. He proved bright, and asked excellent questions about the material. His penmanship was on par with A-Yuan’s—his motor skills better developed, though the writing itself shakier—and he seemed to have already learned some of the rudimentary skills of which Meng Yao tried to impart. </p>
<p>Instead of concerns around his learning or ability to absorb the information, it was the endless talking.</p>
<p>“Teacher, I have a question.” Words Meng Yao dreaded within an hour of him having joined the class. “You said that the important thing when listening is that you are attentive and wait until it is your turn to speak so you can best understand the person speaking with you, but the last time I spoke with Xian-gege, he interrupted me three times when I was talking about the pear tree that grew in the courtyard where I lived before this”—he frequently repeated ‘where I lived before this,’ though also failed to provide any additional details—“and I really wanted to tell him about the pears, because they were the best ones ever, and it has twenty hundred pears on it every year, it was really big and the leaves were really pretty and sometimes there were rabbits under it though they didn’t like me and always ran away even when I shouted for them to come back and Xian-gege asked me about the bunnies even though I hadn’t <em>told</em> him about them yet and I don’t understand why he interrupted when <em>you</em> say that we shouldn’t interrupt and everyone else is always telling me not to interrupt, but then he does it and I can’t?”</p>
<p>Meng Yao waited. A-Yuan listened, enthralled.</p>
<p>“And then A-Yuan and Zhan-gege asked me what the pears tasted like and if you eat them too early they are very sour and if sour things make your lips pucker so bad you can't talk should everyone eat sour pears while they're supposed to be listening?"</p>
<p>There, with chaff finally separated, waited the actual question. "It is a very unique idea, Jingyi. I think I shall propose it next time I have something important to say to Young Master Wei."</p>
<p>Satisfied, Jingyi returned his attention to his work. For the moment.</p>
<p>A-Yuan appeared utterly taken with the other boy. While there were other children in the Unclean Realm, none of them had the privilege of calling A-Yuan "cousin" and every time it happened it suffused A-Yuan's face with brilliant joy. It was, in Meng Yao's opinion, utterly worth the chaos.</p>
<p>Meng Yao expected dinners to become horrifyingly untenable with the additional chatter, but Wei Wuxian seemed happy to distract both boys, and ended up shifting the seating to ensure he was always between them.</p>
<p>"Is it nice having someone on the same level to speak to, Wuxian?" Nie Huaisang asked slyly.</p>
<p>"They are the best conversationalists I've ever known," Wei Wuxian replied with every evidence of sincerity as Jingyi splayed across his lap to ask A-Yuan a very serious question regarding the possibilities for dessert. "No offense, Lan Zhan. You're a very close third." </p>
<p>Meng Yao privately wondered at the statement, but the sincerity remained and he didn’t believe the words to be disingenuous.</p>
<p>"I don't want to think how they dealt with him in Cloud Recesses," Jiang Wanyin muttered.</p>
<p>Very interesting. If the dragon had delivered him, as Meng Yao could only surmise from available evidence, the question then became what business did the dragons—and, by extension, the Two Lords—have there, when they were supposedly on the northern border?</p><hr/>
<p>The lovely days of summer shifted towards sweltering as they drew towards autumn, as though the world sought to make a last, token protest before heading abed for the winter.</p>
<p>The blazing day pressed into Meng Yao’s pores, relentlessly seeking him out in every corner of the Unclean Realm, even those inner recesses comprised mostly of stone. Vents meant to channel in fresh air only delivered the heat directly to them, and Meng Yao’s fan—a much more tastefully painted specimen compared to the monstrosity Nei Huaisang still carried around—did little to assuage the choking heat in the air. </p>
<p>The boys slumped on their side of the desk, and Meng Yao couldn’t bring himself to fault them for it. It was a miserable day, and while both his students were generally engaged and interested in the material, the stifling air made it hard to focus on anything.</p>
<p>Nodding off, Lan Jingyi half-toppled over as his elbow slipped off the side of the table, smacking fully into A-Yuan and sending them both tumbling to the floor. They bumbled about in a tangle of tiny, uncoordinated limbs until managing to separate and snapping to an admirable facsimile of attention. </p>
<p>“I don’t believe this is working,” Meng Yao admitted. Understanding the need for strategic withdrawal was paramount when working with children, he’d discovered. </p>
<p>“We’re sorry, teacher,” A-Yuan said miserably. He stood and bowed. While Meng Yao did not share Wei Wuxian’s conviction of A-Yuan being objectively the cutest child to ever exist, this did stretch the bounds of his doubt. It was terribly adorable. Jingyi jumped up and followed suit. </p>
<p>“None of that,” Meng Yao assured them. They both straightened. “Shall I arrange for a picnic?” </p>
<p>A-Yuan and Jingyi exchanged looks of absolute delight. “Really?!” Jingyi’s already gregarious idea of volume control had been influenced by the shared association with Jiang Wanyin and Wei Wuxian; that was to say, his whisper could have been used to make announcements at the foot of Koi Tower. </p>
<p>“Really. Both of you continue with the exercise while I go and arrange for a small lunch.” </p>
<p>The boys set themselves to the task with renewed vigor, and Meng Yao went in search of nibbles. The kitchens helpfully put together a small basket of travel-friendly items, and one of the cooks—a weathered auntie who always served a mix of delicious food catering to all palates involved—suggested a small watering hole not a mile from the eastern gates. </p>
<p>“This is very good of you, Young Master Meng,” she said. She surreptitiously tucked in a few extra sweets and offered Meng Yao an agreeable smile. “Make sure the boys don’t eat them all.” </p>
<p>Meng Yao bowed. “Very kind.” </p>
<p>By the time he made it back to the boys, Wei Wuxian had appeared in the room, idly doodling what appeared to be talisman designs on one of Meng Yao’s blank pages. “Meng Yao! What’s this I hear about you abducting Jingyi and my radish?” </p>
<p>A cold splash of anxiety dropped from Meng Yao’s throat to his gut. Of course it was inappropriate to presume such familiarity when he was only a servant. “I apologize, Young Master Wei, I thought—”</p>
<p>“Ah, ah, ah. The only way to properly make amends for such a serious crime is to invite me along.” He eyed the nearly overstuffed basket. “Especially if auntie packed up any of her spicy pork buns.” </p>
<p>“There may be one or two,” Meng Yao admitted, though reluctance still squeezed at his windpipe. “Though you may have to fight Jingyi for them.” The older boy had taken to the Jiang siblings’ lamentable habit of piling their plates high with chilis. Whether or not he enjoyed them seemed entirely beyond the point.</p>
<p>Jingyi jumped to his feet, “I will win.” </p>
<p>Wei Wuxian laughed and ruffled his hair. “I have no doubt.” </p>
<p>Truthfully, having Wei Wuxian along was an unexpected blessing. Meng Yao was fully confident in his abilities to handle his charges in the classroom, but hadn’t anticipated that an easy walk for a fully grown man would be such an ordeal for the boys. </p>
<p>Wei Wuxian ended up carrying them both, leaving Meng Yao to handle the basket. He grinned ear to ear the entire time, waving away offers to switch as Jingyi clung to his back while A-Yuan remained nestled happily in his arms, the two of them chattering happily over Wei Wuxian's shoulder. The obviously well-loved path took them from the Unclean Realm into the wild hurst, the tight foliage above their heads instantly offering some much-needed shade. </p>
<p>“I haven’t had much chance to explore the area outside of the Unclean Realm,” Meng Yao admitted. The path was littered with rocks and raised roots, making for easy footholds but difficult navigation when one was carrying two small children. Wei Wuxian managed with remarkable dexterity. </p>
<p>“Ah, it’s all mountains and scrub in every direction,” Wei Wuxian said. His face twisted. “And Koi Tower to the south, and you got the scenic route on the way here.” He paused a moment to boost A-Yuan further up his chest and tuck one arm back behind Jingyi’s bottom. “Qinghe’s nothing on Yunmeng, I have to say. I miss the lakes, and all the green. This is about as close as we get, and it doesn’t compare.</p>
<p>“Still,” he continued as they reached their destination—a sizable pond just shy of being called a lake, where a generous number of the surrounding trees had been cleared away to provide places to sit. “It has its merits, I suppose. Don’t tell Da-ge or Huaisang I said so, though, or I’ll never stop hearing about it.” Ringed by trees, and with the water so near, the heat dwindled to almost pleasant levels, though it still sat heavy in Meng Yao’s lungs. </p>
<p>Wei Wuxian set the boys down and shooed them towards the water to cool off, then slumped to the ground without any obvious thoughts to his respectable robes. Meng Yao hesitantly took a seat beside him, though he remained upright in a proper seat instead of a boneless slouch, and was rewarded with a broad grin. </p>
<p>“You’ve been with us a month, now,” Wei Wuxian said, eyes carefully on the boys as Jingyi kicked off his boots and ran into the pond with a pleased scream. A-Yuan removed his shoes carefully, and set them down neatly. He took a moment to straighten Jingyi’s as well before taking a few, much more sedate steps into the clear water. His sensibilities were completely overcome when Jingyi belly flopped directly in front of him and completely soaked his robes to the chin. “Are you settled?” </p>
<p>“The boys are excellent students,” Meng Yao reported. “Especially A-Yuan, who I think will have a remarkable gift for calligraphy.” </p>
<p>“Aiya, Meng Yao, I wasn’t asking about the boys,” Wei Wuxian’s tone was chiding, but he smiled. “I want to know about you.”</p>
<p>“Me?” Meng Yao repeated. “I am happy to be of service of course…” </p>
<p>“You are an incredibly frustrating person,” Wei Wuxian told him. </p>
<p>Meng Yao’s chin drooped towards his chest, mostly to hide the sudden twist of his lips. “It has been said before.” </p>
<p>Wei Wuxian smacked his own forehead. “You…” He huffed. “You remind me of Lan Zhan, when we first met.” </p>
<p>“I sincerely doubt it.” </p>
<p>“No, no, listen: he didn’t like being teased by me. Or anyone. Because when he was younger, the only people to tease him were cruel. He spent a life building up an icy face to prevent people from seeing how he felt, or from trying to get to know him better. Your face isn’t icy, but it’s the same as his. Hiding everything away, because you don’t want people to know how you’re feeling in case they use it to hurt you.” </p>
<p>Dangerous, as Meng Yao had always thought. That he had some sour pear. Thank <em>fuck</em> he had the practice of maintaing neutrality. “Quite the assessment, Young Master Wei.” </p>
<p>“I am going to make you call me Wuxian if it’s the last thing I do.” </p>
<p>“If you keep trying to find all my soft spots, it will be.” </p>
<p>“Ah ha! Jiang Cheng told me you had a sense of humour!” Wei Wuxian poked Meng Yao’s side, and allowed Meng Yao to slap his hand away instead of dodging the mostly ineffectual smack. “Anyway, Lan Zhan opens up around people he trusts, but even then it’s hard for him to do it. A-Yuan has been good for him, I think. He wants to set good examples to counter all my bad ones.”</p>
<p>“I think you’re an excellent father,” Meng Yao told him. He found himself surprised to realize it was true. </p>
<p>“And I think that once you trust us, all those many smiles you have might be a bit more real.” Having dropped that heavy load into the air between them, he sat up and clapped his hands together. “Now, those buns have tormented me since we left.” </p>
<p>The promise of food tempted the boys back to the shore, and A-Yuan sat neatly between Meng Yao and Wei Wuxian even as Jingyi—taking his cue from Wei Wuxian—dropped down and leaned his full weight against Meng Yao.</p>
<p>After Meng Yao packed away the last crumbs of their lunch, enjoying the delighted smiles the small sweets earned the boys, Wei Wuxian took his dizi from his belt and began to play, watching as the boys returned to the water. </p>
<p>Meng Yao found himself… quite content. </p>
<p>Or he did, until Wei Wuxian paused his playing, brow drawn in concern, and the alarming sound of heavy branches snapping tore through the peace. Wei Wuxian jumped to his feet and Meng Yao shouted for the boys. </p>
<p>They obeyed, but barely had time to reach the shore before a beast broke through the treeline in front of the path back to the Unclean Realm. Meng Yao couldn’t tell what it had been before the resentful energy corrupted it entirely; it’s enormous body and broad horns looked bovine in appearance, but serrated tusks stretched down from its mouth—a horrible, gaping maw already bloodied with the meaty dregs of its last meal still hanging from its jowls. Bony plates covered its sides that ground against each other with each twitch of muscle. </p>
<p>“The boys,” Wei Wuxian shouted. He produced a talisman from his sleeve and threw it forward, a golden shield springing into place in the all-too-short distance between them. As soon as it fell into place, Wei Wuxian calmly lifted his dizi to his lips and played a single note. The white jade sword token hanging from the end glowed with brilliant ephemeral light, there and gone in a heartbeat. </p>
<p>Meng Yao got his arms around them, but the creature blocked their only retreat. The forest would hinder them more than it would the beast. It heaved with the force of its breath and pawed at the ground with knife-sharp hooves, as though waiting. </p>
<p>“It’s too big, baba,” A-Yuan whispered. </p>
<p>The beast charged and Wei Wuxian whipped out his sword. Meng Yao cringed; even a spiritual weapon would be hard-pressed to put so much as a mark on the heavily armoured flank.</p>
<p>The beast tore through the barrier as though it were paper, howling with a deafening crash of a house being shattered beneath a rockslide. Wei Wuxian darted towards it, the tip of his sword sliding into the space between two of the plates near its eyes. The beast howled and spun to tear after him. Meng Yao quickly considered the distance between himself, the beast and the path, and shook his head. </p>
<p>The space for Wei Wuxian to maneuver was dangerously small, and he was forced to leap into the air to dodge as great horns bucked towards him when the beast whipped its head. He was fast, but the angle of his ascent brought him too close to the creature’s lengthy fangs, and the tip dug into his left leg, opening it from knee to ankle. It tried to spin, momentarily captured by the thick vegetation around it. </p>
<p>Wei Wuxian landed in front of Meng Yao and stumbled, blood running freely down his legs. </p>
<p>Panic stuck in his lungs, Meng Yao said, “I cannot make it to the path.” He wasn’t fast enough when he had the boys tucked into his arms, and he wouldn’t abandon them. Not for anything. </p>
<p>Wei Wuxian considered this in silence. </p>
<p>“Help is coming,” he said confidently. “I can distract it until it arrives.” </p>
<p>“Until wh— <em>Wei Wuxian</em>!” Wei Wuxian dove back towards the creature as it freed itself, powering a talisman with one hand as he brought his sword to bear with the other. He jammed the point in between two of the plates and tossed the talisman inside, then danced away as the creature loosed a scream, smoke pouring out from the new opening. It lumbered forward, but its target was no longer Wei Wuxian. Pain and rage drove it forward, directly towards Meng Yao and the children. </p>
<p>Meng Yao whipped about and ran for the trees, boys tucked in his arms and Wei Wuxian screaming wordlessly behind him. The cover wouldn’t help. The beast could easily pick up the momentum it needed to catch up to them, and it had felled who knew how many trees in its initial charge. But if Meng Yao could just get to the treeline and hide the boys, maybe he could find a way to distract it long enough for Wei Wuxian to find an opening. </p>
<p>He practically felt the hot breath against the back of his neck as they reached the trees, he dropped to the ground, the boys tight to his chest and eyes squeezed shut. </p>
<p>Meng Yao missed his mother. </p>
<p>He supposed he wouldn’t have to much longer. </p>
<p>And then something warm and solid draped across his back and he was being born away, moved out of the path of the creature and deposited safely near the path. Meng Yao swung around, and all the breath left his lungs as he beheld the dragon. </p>
<p>Artwork, even the most exquisite examples he’d seen in his time in the Unclean Realm, did not do the majesty and power of the dragon justice. Scales shone in the sunlight with white opalescence that beggared description, covering a broadly muscled body easily longer than five men placed head to toe, the finest silver mane following along the long stretch of its back to the tip of its tail, the vaguest touch of cyan run through the individual strands. He would not dare call its shape serpentine, no. This was no snake, though superficially the long stretch of it might make the ignorant scramble for any potential comparison. It’s maw stretched back over a frightening row of diamond-sharp teeth, as the beast before it sailed through where Meng Yao and the boys had stood only a moment before. </p>
<p>Wei Wuxian wasted no time. He jumped forward, and the dragon caught him with the tip of its tail and slingshotted him further, to the top of the beast. Wei Wuxian stabbed his sword down between the beast’s plates below the shoulder, twisting it viciously and earning himself another roar. The beast jerked around, but the dragon pulled Wei Wuxian back and away before it could do so much as twitch to throw him off. Wei Wuxian ran up the dragon’s body and, upon reaching its head, used its horn as a handhold as the dragon whipped forward, snatching his sword back and away. </p>
<p>In all the stories Meng Yao heard, nothing indicated the dragons willingly fought alongside anyone except the Two Lords. Dimly, he decided it to be a promising development for his father; and yet the obvious trust between them seemed so profound he could not imagine forcing such a connection. </p>
<p>The dragon and Wei Wuxian moved together seamlessly, taking the beast apart piece by piece until Wei Wuxian managed to drive his sword deep into its neck and it toppled over without another whisper of sound or breath. They stilled, waiting, Wei Wuxian balanced on one of the dragon’s impressively muscled forelegs, until satisfied it would not rise again. </p>
<p>He yanked his sword out of the beast and cleaned it with a flick and flare of spiritual energy. The dragon, obviously less sanguine though Meng Yao couldn’t confidently say how he could tell, lowered its head and accepted Wei Wuxian’s hand upon its brow. He leaned his entire weight forward until half-balanced on the dragon’s snout, carefully avoiding the horn-tipped muzzle, and rested his forehead against the space between two very intelligent eyes. </p>
<p>And with that small intimacy, he jumped straight and turned towards Meng Yao and the boys. “Anyone injured?” </p>
<p>“No, Young Master Wei,” Meng Yao reported honestly, if hoarsely. The boys, taking the question as permission, both darted forward to grab onto Wei Wuxian’s legs. A-Yuan reached up until the dragon lowered its head to allow him to press a small palm against his face. </p>
<p>With a broad grin, Wei Wuxian coaxed him forward. “Meng Yao, come meet Hanguang-jun.” </p>
<p>Meng Yao stepped forward cautiously, eyes trained on the dragon. The dragon itself turned its attention towards him and Meng Yao froze in place under the intense scrutiny of impossibly vibrant eyes. </p>
<p>“They have names,” he said quietly. </p>
<p>Wei Wuxian shrugged guilelessly. “Most things do. Say hello properly.” </p>
<p>“Forgive me,” Meng Yao gasped. He bowed lower than he had even to Jiang Wanyin, when he still thought of him as Sect Leader Jiang. “This one is humbled and honoured to behold your greatness, Hanguang-jun.” </p>
<p>“No one ever says shit like that to me,” Wei Wuxian muttered. Meng Yao couldn’t help glaring. “Come, come.” </p>
<p>“Can… can dragons speak?” He took a few more steps forward, until he stood only a few feet away. He couldn’t bring himself to move any further. </p>
<p>“In their own way,” Wei Wuxian said with a fond smile. He trailed his fingers gently along the crest above Hanguang-jun’s eye, and the dragon seemed to sigh into the touch, huffing a breath that smelled of wet stone and petrichor. “We’ll find you at home, yeah?” </p>
<p>Hanguang-jun, alarmingly, nudged A-Yuan’s stomach with its snout and then jumped into the air with a gust of wind so powerful the boys were knocked onto their bottoms. Both children laughed in delight, popping up again almost as quickly and waving enthusiastically after the receding form. </p>
<p>“Meng Yao, you look like you need a drink,” Wei Wuxian stated after Hanguang-jun disappeared over the treetops. </p>
<p>Meng Yao mustered up a weak version of one of his more pleasant smiles. “Well, appearances can’t always be deceiving.” </p>
<p>Wei Wuxian laughed and gathered the boys up for the return walk home.</p><hr/>
<p>Over dinner that evening, during which Meng Yao did not see the bottom of his cup, Wei Wuxian regaled the table with the completely exaggerated and mostly fictitious story of Meng Yao's bravery, egged on by the boys who seemed to think it a faithful recounting of events.</p>
<p>"And then he threw himself right in front of the thing to shield the boys with his own body," Wei Wuxian claimed, oblivious to Lan Wangji slipping another sesame ball onto his plate. He and the boys had been doted on all night by Lan Wangji, albeit in a very subtle yet genuine way that made Meng Yao ache for reasons he did not care to examine. </p>
<p>Meng Yao finally felt confident to protest. "Young Master Wei not being fair. He and… Hanguang-jun dispatched the beast too quickly for this one to be of any use at all."</p>
<p>"Of course then he almost pissed in his robes in front of Hanguang-jun," Wei Wuxian snorted.</p>
<p>"Wuxian!" Meng Yao snapped, cheeks flaming with embarrassment.</p>
<p>The man grinned and dug his elbow into Jiang Wanyin's side. "See! I told you! Not even a month before he broke."</p>
<p>"So what? You annoying someone to distraction is nothing new!" Jiang Wanyin shouted before regarding Meng Yao with the longest-suffering look Meng Yao had ever seen. “I’m sure you did just fine. The first time this idiot met Hanguang-jun he acted so shamelessly I almost threw myself off the nearest cliff out of sheer secondhand embarrassment.”</p>
<p>“Unfair. We were nowhere near a cliff!” Wei Wuxian protested over Lan Wangji’s huff.</p>
<p>“<em>I would have found one</em>!”</p>
<p>“We’re very grateful to you for protecting the boys, Young Master Meng,” Jiang Yanli said with a kind smile. It effectively cut off any and all other teasing, for which he was exceedingly grateful. </p>
<p>Later, tucked into his room, he wrote a missive to his father describing the dragon, and tried to capture Hanguang-jun’s effortless strength. The words were innocent enough, but he tried to identify the appropriate tone to imply the difficulty of taming a being of such overwhelming power. He could not say he was successful, but without making potentially compromising direct statements regarding his father’s directive, it would have to do. </p>
<p>When he finished, he sat back on his heels. </p>
<p><em>I have seen a dragon,</em> he thought. In retrospect, he could barely count the single, fleeting glimpse he'd caught when Jingyi came to them. It could not compare. Something deep within his chest twisted at the idea of Hanguang-jun beholden to anyone and tramped it mercilessly down. This all had a purpose, and he needed to stay true.</p>
<p>Leaving the letter to dry, he rose and left the room for his nightly exploration. He knew the Unclean Realm almost as well as he knew Koi Tower by now. The corridors unfurled to him with welcome familiarity, the occupants all abed or tucked comfortably into their quarters for the evening. He made his way towards the main reception hall for nothing else than the chance to enjoy his solitude and examine his thoughts. </p>
<p>His time here proved dangerous. He’d become… attached to the people who he knew would surely have to be dealt with if his father’s plans were to succeed. Even from the short time he’d witnessed Wei Wuxian’s interaction with Hanguang-jun, he knew there to be not the meagrest amount of a chance that the man would allow harm to come to the dragons while he still drew breath. One way or another, the problem of Wei Wuxian would have to be addressed. </p>
<p>And this obviously did not take into consideration the Two Lords, unknown factors he could not account for until he’d met them in person and evaluated them as potential threats to his father’s machinations. </p>
<p>Of course, the night after he reached this conclusion, the Two Lords made their return to the Unclean Realm.</p><hr/>
<p>Once or twice during his evening walks, he made it as far as the very limits of the living areas, finding himself trailing along a surprisingly well-kept path leading to the edge of the treeline and into what appeared to be a deliberately cleared at the edge of a deep valley. He found himself appreciating the wild beauty of the mountains; a small footbridge had been erected over a quick-running stream that careened over a nearby cliffside into an expansive lake filling the valley below. On the other end of the bridge, the pathway disappeared, leaving only untended land trailing towards the mountains. It had been where he’d witnessed Lan Wangji collect Jingyi, and he found himself often trailing back to the spot for its peaceful air as much as its promise of solitude. The grass, he noted, was completely trampled into the dirt to leave a bare stretch of mostly-smooth land stretching towards the nearest of the mountains. </p>
<p>That night, his solitude was interrupted when rain-scented fog descended upon him seconds before the dragon. </p>
<p>The earth beneath his feet shook with the power of its landing and Meng Yao stumbled back, eyes wide. This was not Huangang-jun. The bare glow of the crescent moon revealed only dark scales and a head crowned with wicked spiralled horns and a broader expanse of fur, very different from Hanguang-jun’s clean lines and effortless elegance. Enormous in size, this dragon must have been at least another half size larger than its counterpart, and blazing eyes fixed upon Meng Yao immediately. </p>
<p>It took him a long moment to realize it bore a man upon its back, and longer to react when the man slumped forward and slid to the ground. The dragon’s eyes widened, its attention snapping towards its fallen rider. </p>
<p>Meng Yao moved forward, though he froze a precious second later when the dragon swang back to him and bared its teeth. </p>
<p>Meng Yao bowed. “Great and honourable dragon, please let this unworthy one see if he can assist,” Meng Yao said. “Even at a run, help will be a few minutes off.” </p>
<p>The dragon, still as a statue, regarded him with eyes piercing as a sword through his chest, threatening to cleave him in twain. Finally, it raised its head and loosed a bellow into the air. Had a tempest been trapped within a box and the lid lifted for only a moment, it could not have made a sound to rival that call of the dragon. Yet, when it lowered its head once more it moved to allow Meng Yao closer. </p>
<p>The man on the ground bled freely through a mighty gash across his abdomen, and even with a pallid face twisted in pain he remained the most beautiful man Meng Yao had beheld in all his life. He cried out when Meng Yao placed his hands upon the wound, transferring what meagre amount of spiritual energy he could to stem the bleeding and placing enough pressure to slow the steady flow. The dragon… hovered. Not literally, but it remained close enough to remind Meng Yao of a worried party waiting outside a healer’s room. </p>
<p>Meng Yao was no healer, and his efforts felt futile, but he was determined. After all, the white ribbon resting tight across his forehead, though stained with blood, all but confirmed the man whose guts were currently being held in place solely through Meng Yao’s efforts was the Lord of Jade. </p>
<p>It took long minutes before the sounds of help arriving filled the air. Wei Wuxian and Lan Wangji spilled from the treeline, swords drawn and in the complete disarray of the recently awakened. They wore simple sleep robes, hair unbound, a wild look about them both. For all that, the truly shocking sight was the absence of Lan Wangji's forehead ribbon, until Meng Yao realized it to be lovingly tied around Wei Wuxian's wrist.</p>
<p>Wei Wuxian stumbled to a halt. “Chifeng-zun?” </p>
<p>“Brother,” Lan Wangji breathed in the same moment. He darted ahead of Wei Wuxian, dropping next to Meng Yao to begin pressing his own, much more substantial spiritual power into the wound. Broad hands rested alongside Meng Yao’s, and sharp tingles ran up his arms at the close proximity to the sheer volume of power Lan Wangji passed along. </p>
<p>“What happened?” Wei Wuxian demanded. </p>
<p>It took Meng Yao an embarrassingly long moment to realize the question to be aimed at him. “I was out walking and happened to be here when the… when Chifeng-zun landed. The Lord of Jade was already injured.” </p>
<p>“It’s after midnight,” Wei Wuxian pointed out.</p>
<p>“I am not an easy sleeper,” Meng Yao replied.</p>
<p>“Not the time,” Lan Wangji hissed. The bleeding slowed enough for him to gesture Wei Wuxian forward. “Let’s bring him to his rooms.” He paused and looked at Meng Yao from across his brother’s body. “Thank you.” </p>
<p>Breathless with shock, Meng Yao sat back on his heels as they collected the Lord of Jade carefully between them and carried him back towards the family quarters. He stared after them, heart twisting peculiarly in his chest. He… had he ever been thanked before? For anything? Surely, once in his life, he must have been. Yet he failed to call to mind a single instance. </p>
<p>His hands were slippery with blood and he stared down at them, gaze trailing up along the ruined sleeves of his robes. </p>
<p>No, no, no. The blood needed to come off before it flung him all the way back to his mother’s side. The phantom sense of her heaving ragged coughs in his arms and gagging on blood with every breath threatened to overwhelm him. He darted to the stream and desperately plunged his hands into the water, smashing his hands together to clean them. He could not have blood on his hands again. He could not. </p>
<p>The dragon waited nearby. In all the blistering panic of the situation, he’d almost forgotten the dragon to even be present, though he could not conceive of such a thing now. It watched as he stuck his hands into the water, the bank yielding to elbow-deep water and stinging with the frigidity of a glacier-fed stream. </p>
<p>“This unworthy one apologizes,” he whispered, wishing he might’ve waited until he had the chance to bow, but the sudden desire to rid himself of the gore could not be ignored. “I could not do more.” </p>
<p>The dragon considered him closely, then huffed and launched itself into the sky. </p>
<p>It didn’t occur to Meng Yao until much, much later how significantly easier acquiring a dragon might have proven if he’d applied pressure in a slightly different fashion, and let the Lord of Jade die beneath his hands.</p><hr/>
<p>Unlike the evening meal, to which everyone connected to the Household of the Two Lords was quite obviously expected to attend, mornings were significantly less organized. Those who didn’t request a meal brought to their rooms drifted in and out of the main hall, attended to by servants accustomed to the disparate habits of an eclectic mix of persons. Sometimes Meng Yao found himself alone breaking his fast, though rarely. His own habits overlapped with Jin Zixuan’s enough that they frequently ate together in polite silence, slightly strained by the fact that neither of them seemed to have a single clue as to what they could say to one another, even despite Jin Zixuan’s decision to call him brother. They often exhausted safe topics of conversation within a few minutes, and while Jin Zixuan often looked like he wanted to speak more, he erred on the side of caution. </p>
<p>Walking through the doors that morning, Meng Yao was shocked to see Nie Huaisang seated at the table. To the best of his knowledge, the other man shared Wei Wuxian’s habit of sleeping late and staying up later, and Meng Yao certainly hadn’t seen him at breakfast before. </p>
<p>The surprise faded when he realized that one of the two grand seats at the front of the room to now be occupied. </p>
<p>It was not the Lord of Jade. Indeed, considering the depth and extent of his injury Meng Yao would have been surprised to see him up and about so quickly. Thus, the man before him had to be the Lord of Blades, Nie Mingjue. He wore the heavy robes of the Nie, practically armour in their own right, and his face reminded Meng Yao of the crust atop a pool of lava. Meng Yao’s steps faltered, which only served to draw their attention to him. </p>
<p>He bowed as deeply to the Lord of Blades as he had to Chifeng-zun the night before. </p>
<p>“Da-ge,” Huaisang said, snapping his fan shut with far too much art. “This is Young Master Meng Yao.”</p>
<p>Nie Mingjue’s attention came upon him as a lodestone pressed against his back. Waiting for acknowledgement, he barely noticed the man himself rising and approaching until he stood before Meng Yao to tuck hands under his arms and draw him upwards. </p>
<p>The Lord of Jade remained the most beautiful man Meng Yao ever beheld. The softening of the hard features of the Lord of Blades made his breath catch nonetheless. </p>
<p>“I owe you a debt, Meng Yao,” he stated. Nie Huaisang made a noise behind him, though Meng Yao would’ve been hard pressed to describe it. “I’ve been apprised of your actions last night, which will contribute to a swifter recovery for Xichen. I pay my debts.” </p>
<p>A hard lump sat in Meng Yao’s throat, a steel spike driven through flesh and sticking into his spine until he found himself immobilized by the weight of the words and the presence of the man before him. </p>
<p>Before he could reveal too much of himself, he bowed again. “It is my honour to be of service.” </p>
<p>A shift, and then Nie Huaisang’s voice: “Yes, every time.” </p>
<p>Once again, Nie Mingjue lifted him to stand straight. “Join us for our meal, Meng Yao. I would like to know more about you.”</p>
<p>More intimidated than he’d been since the first, cautious step onto the Koi Tower stairs, Meng Yao crossed to share the table with Nie Huaisang.</p><hr/>
<p>Lan Xichen woke up feeling as though consciousness was unwise. </p>
<p>This assessment was quickly confirmed by both the pain in his abdomen and the glowering presence of his husband sat at his bedside. </p>
<p>“How are you feeling?” Mingjue demanded gruffly. </p>
<p>Lan Xichen took a moment to consider before replying, “Tender.” </p>
<p>This proved to not be the answer Mingjue was looking for. “If you ever do that to me again…” </p>
<p>When they’d first met, doubtless Mingjue would have found a very vicious, if not creative, way to finish the sentence. Now he just looked tired. Lan Xichen reached out a hand, relieved when Mingjue immediately grabbed it up in his own. Nothing irreparable, then. A relief, to be sure. There were few things he could weather with poorer grace than Mingjue’s temper when aimed in his direction. </p>
<p>He squeezed the fingers trapped against his own and Mingjue heaved out a frustrated breath. He tucked his free hand beneath Xichen’s robe to examine the mostly-closed injury, allowing Lan Xichen a moment to mentally focus himself. The familiar sense of his brother’s spiritual energy sat heavy in his veins, replenishing his own and fortifying his strength as his body worked to heal. And beneath that, almost an aftertaste after a small sip of sweet wine, something else. Weak, perhaps, but present. </p>
<p>“What happened?” he asked, eyes opening even as his brow drew in confusion. </p>
<p>“After that Wen-dog tried to gut you? Or do you need a refresher on that as well?” </p>
<p>Lan Xichen winced. Mingjue was obviously furious, and he frankly couldn’t blame him. They’d agreed, when they decided to deal with the lingering threat of Wen Xu and his ilk, no unnecessary risks now the war was over. That had been before Wen Xu had made another move on Cloud Recesses.</p>
<p>“I remember that part,” he said with a gentle incline of his chin, the best he could manage while lying down. He shifted to try and sit up, only for Mingjue to release his hand and push him back down. "It gave you and Uncle the opening required."</p>
<p>"Lan Xichen, if you're telling me you deliberately let yourself be eviscerated, I will be very, very angry." Baxia twitched from her place in the sword stand beside the door, Shouyue a pale shadow as the sabre quaked with Mingjue's rage.</p>
<p>"I didn't expect him to be able to land the blow," Lan Xichen replied honestly. Since when had either of Wen Ruohan's sons posed a significant threat beyond what they could do to the helpless? Their strength always came from the forces they commanded. Wen Xu may have been more martially competent than his younger brother, but Lan Xichen had only ever seen him as an extension of his father. An extension, Lan Xichen mused angrily, that had perpetrated terrible deeds when he had no fear of repercussions. </p>
<p>"Never underestimate your opponent. Isn't that written on your wall?"</p>
<p>"'Be respectful of the skills of others, both known and unknown,'" he quoted. "'Never take for granted your superiority.'"</p>
<p>"I should tell your uncle, but I'd prefer you recover under my hands than his."</p>
<p>Mn. Uncle could be a bit of a mother hen. "I have always loved being under your hands."</p>
<p>Mingjue smirked, though it faded quickly. "At least Wen Xu is dead.”</p>
<p>Xichen took in a grateful breath. When Wen Xu had struck at him, it gave Uncle the opening to land a blow and disable his arm long enough for Mingjue to finish him, separating head from shoulders. Finally. Two years after the Sunshot Campaign officially ended, perhaps now he and Mingjue could find some peace.</p>
<p>When Wex Xu escaped, shortly before his father's death, Lan Xichen had been so eager to return home he'd been willing to overlook potential consequences. Wen Xu’s proclivities towards cruelty were well-known, but without his father's support he occurred as nothing more than a child looking for validation through negative behaviour.</p>
<p>They hadn't expected him to blood dozens of men in the two years since his father's death and launch an offensive against Cloud Recesses. Thank goodness for the improved strength of the wards, or else he might have seen his home burn once again.</p>
<p>“Of course, you might have mentioned to me the wound was so grievous before deciding to fly home and then falling out of the sky when your intestines decided they were sick of being confined.” The acerbicy of the tone made Lan Xichen wince, but he supposed he deserved it. </p>
<p>“I had no idea it was as bad as it was, Mingjue. I wouldn’t have risked my life unnecessarily.” If anything, the flight had simply aggravated it more than he’d expected. </p>
<p>“You’re lucky we were close to the Unclean Realm when you finally passed out. Had we been of any real distance… <em>A-Huan</em>...” His grip tightened to the point of breaking Lan Xichen’s fingers, but he couldn’t fault his husband the concern. He longed to sit up and wrap his arms around Mingjue’s shoulders, but knowing Mingjue would not thank him for the efforts kept him in place. </p>
<p>“And then…?”</p>
<p>Mingjue took a moment to calm himself, fixing his gaze out the nearby window with gritted teeth until he breathed out and the tension eased incrementally from his shoulders. “Then you were attended by our new friend, Meng Yao.” </p>
<p>Meng Yao. Yes. Wangji had mentioned him when Lan Xichen had escaped the field to deliver Lan Jingyi into the care of his brother. The assessment hadn’t been particularly flattering, though Lan Xichen was willing to chalk such things up to Wangji’s natural recalcitrance. Apparently Nie Huaisang had concerns about his trustworthiness, though he couldn’t yet offer an explanation to merit it beyond something regarding a painted fan. Lan Xichen had decided to follow up with Huaisang directly, supposing he’d missed something essential in the secondhand message from his brother, but obviously the abrupt nature of his homecoming changed things. </p>
<p>"I shall need to thank him."</p>
<p>"I took the liberty on your behalf yesterday morning.” Mingjue huffed. “After he found his voice he made a point of asking after you, and then a number of pointed questions about where our dragons were kept and how they fared."</p>
<p>Lan Xichen frowned in confusion. "What?"</p>
<p>"If no one else has decided to enlighten him, I'll follow their lead. Wuxian and Zixuan want to talk to us about it once you’re feeling better. They apparently half-abducted him from Jin Guangshan, and we both know what sort of man he is." </p>
<p>"Indeed," Lan Xichen winced. "I do wish Yanli-jie had found someone else to give her heart to, even though Jin Zixuan hasn't proved the same odious scum as his sire."</p>
<p>"Strong words, husband. You must still be in pain."</p>
<p>"I speak as I say."</p>
<p>Mingjue snorted. "Like hell."</p>
<p>Lan Xichen mustered up a small smile and shifted on the bed. "Join me?"</p>
<p>"Only for a minute. Jiang Cheng is waiting on me to review the business we missed."</p><hr/>
<p>Within three days of waking, irritation at the spousal-enforced bedrest stung at Lan Xichen like a hornet aiming for a sensitive place. While their extended family offered a constant parade of faces eager to see and entertain him, he ached to walk the halls of the Unclean Realm and enjoy a view other than the same four walls. </p>
<p>Wangji and Mingjue, his most regular companions, remained unsympathetic, both being of the opinion that he'd brought the convalescence upon himself. Yanli-jie brought him food and gentle smiles and, on one notable occasion, her betrothed who agreed Lan Xichen had conducted himself well but declined to repeat the sentiment to Mingjue, which either showed good judgement or a lack of backbone depending on the generosity of interpretation. </p>
<p>Jiang Cheng, as was his wont, yelled. "What would I have done if you'd died, hmm? Dealt with all the Gusu bullshit on top of everything in Yunmeng? Am I supposed to be the one to tell Lan Qiren there's no budget for another wing on the library? You think I want that?"</p>
<p>He and Mingjue really did share some remarkable similarities. Mingjue's anger burned no less hot, but Jiang Cheng's ran quicker to the surface. The only reason his appendages remained unthreatened was, presumably, because Jiang Cheng knew it wouldn't truly hinder him.</p>
<p>"I am very relieved you were here to keep things in such good order, A-Cheng," Lan Xichen told him.</p>
<p>Flustered by the compliment, but still outraged, Jiang Cheng very deliberately did not ask if he needed anything for his comfort when he left. A small meal was brought in within minutes of his departure however, and Lan Xichen smiled softly into the bowl.</p>
<p>Huaisang, the most reliable visitor after Wangji and Mingjue, bored him with the pettiest, most frivolous gossip he could find as punishment for allowing himself to be hurt. The point was well-made, and Lan Xichen would have to work very, very hard in order to avoid allowing some of the choicer morsels to impact his behaviour towards certain other residents of the Unclean Realm. A long-lasting torture, and doubtless A-Sang’s intention.</p>
<p>Far and away, though, his favourite visitor quickly became Wei Wuxian. Not for the boisterous nature of his concern, though that was refreshingly uncomplicated, but in that he was often accompanied by his two young charges. They played well off each other; Jingyi more temperate, A-Yuan more willing to speak up. In both cases, Wei Wuxian beamed with sheer delight.</p>
<p>A great weight lifted off his mind to see Jingyi bouncing back so quickly. When he'd brought the boy to the Unclean Realm and left him again almost immediately, he'd also left his fears that the boy would not recover from the wounds left behind by Wen Xu's attack. He’d given half a mind to adopting Jingyi himself, had Mingjue been onboard with the idea, but doing it now seemed cruel, when the small family already seemed content. Wuxian and Wangji had managed to hold off on adopting a small maelstrom of children already to ensure A-Yuan settled properly; he could only imagine the encroaching storm now the floodgates were open. </p>
<p>Even with the steady stream of visitors, bedrest did not agree with him, and after Yanli-jie left him the morning of his fourth day conscious, Lan Xichen quickly dressed and escaped the room before another well-meaning family member showed up to entertain him. He’d managed a simple topknot and his usual hairpiece, and while he felt naked without the Nie plaits he’d started wearing shortly after binding himself to Mingjue, he couldn’t risk seeking his husband out and being bullied back to bed while replacing them. </p>
<p>Sneaking through his own home felt undignified, but still preferable to another moment trapped in his own room. He held no illusions he'd be found out sooner rather than later. Hopefully his destination—his favourite garden, tucked away deep in the recesses of the Unclean Realm and often overlooked by the other inhabitants—would be considered restful enough to let him avoid any overly concerned objections.</p>
<p>Shock bolted through him when he entered the garden and saw someone already seated on the lone bench within. </p>
<p>It had to be Meng Yao, of course. No other stranger would be permitted this deep into the family area of the Unclean Realm. Mingjue had described him well; a handsome face, though currently set with deep grooves of concern. What burdened him? </p>
<p>It took only a moment for him to notice Lan Xichen standing at the garden entrance. He leapt to his feet and bowed.</p>
<p>"Lord of Jade." His voice sounded familiar, probably from when Lan Xichen bled all over him. "This one is sorry for his intrusion on your peace."</p>
<p>"If anything, I am intruding on yours." Had Lan Xichen been closer, he would have pulled the other man straight. Then again, as he closed the distance between them, there seemed no immediate inclination to rise anyway. Lan Xichen pulled him up to find a pleasant smile had replaced the worry hanging on his brow. This, he had prepared himself for as well. Huaisang complained about it at length. "I'm not accustomed to others being here."</p>
<p>"I will leave you, then," Meng Yao offered. "Or fetch more pleasant company?"</p>
<p>"I have yet to find <em>un</em>pleasant company," Lan Xichen assured him. He gestured towards the bench. "Shall we sit? I understand I owe you my improved health, if not my life, and I should like to know you better."</p>
<p>Meng Yao's cheeks flushed prettily, but he acquiesced and sat next to Lan Xichen. “I hope it’s not an inconvenience for me to be here. Only, I’m usually with the boys at this time, but they’ve both expressed an interest in learning musical cultivation and it was determined Lan Wangji would be the best teacher. They’re with him now practicing the guqin.” </p>
<p>“You had no desire to learn?” A slight disappointment, quickly dismissed by Meng Yao’s pursed lips and fleeting look of longing.</p>
<p>“It is a gentleman’s instrument, Lord of Jade, and I am but a servant.”</p>
<p>“I have always believed courtesy and an earnest desire for learning are the truest measures of a gentleman, regardless of station. If you did desire to learn, I’m sure Wangji would be happy to accommodate you.” Or, hopefully more likely to be received, “Even myself if you would prefer a more… adult environment.” </p>
<p>A smile stole across Meng Yao’s face, though he maintained his strict ground-bound gaze. “I will consider your offer, Lord of Jade. Thank you.”</p>
<p>Their conversation drifted towards the boys and Meng Yao’s experience with the Unclean Realm since his arrival. As Mingjue had alluded to, more than one question seemed rather pointedly aimed towards the subject of dragons, though none of them struck him as inherently inappropriate. He answered gamely, if shallowly, and Meng Yao offered no sign of frustration or irritation. </p>
<p>Engrossing as their conversation was, it took both of them longer than it should have to notice Mingjue hovering beneath the garden entrance. To all appearances deeply irritated, though Lan Xichen fancied he knew his husband well enough by now to detect the fond understanding beneath.</p>
<p>“Your brother is unhappy with you,” Mingjue stated once they noticed him, crossing the garden towards them. Meng Yao jumped up to bow, but Mingjue waved him off. </p>
<p>“Which one?” Lan Xichen asked placidly. </p>
<p>“The loud one.” Ah, it had been Jiang Cheng’s turn to check on him, then. Little wonder they hadn’t heard him hollering from across the Unclean Realm. Mingjue moved to stand behind them and began fixing his hair. Lan Xichen eased back into the touch. Meng Yao refocused his attention on the garden path before them, obviously unaccustomed to such open and easy intimacies. It spoke more of the situation at Koi Tower than anything, Lan Xichen thought as Mingjue redressed his complicated plaits and reset his guan. </p>
<p>“Will I stop embarrassing you now?” Lan Xichen asked once Mingjue reseated his guan. </p>
<p>Mingjue snorted. “Doubtful.” </p>
<p>Meng Yao paled, but Lan Xichen laughed which seemed to put him at ease. </p>
<p>Very curious, their new resident.</p><hr/>
<p>Meng Yao walked the boys through the hallways to the room kept by Lan Wangji during the day. All of them had their own spaces outside their rooms to sit and occupy themselves with that they would. Even Meng Yao, though he’d quickly transformed his into the utilitarian space used for conducting lessons. </p>
<p>Next to him, Jingyi sang under his breath. “Gonna learn some more guqin, gonna be the best that’s ever played.”</p>
<p>Alas for Jingyi’s musical ambitions, the poor boy invariably dropped every note he attempted to carry, and would likely have to find his passions elsewhere.</p>
<p>Meng Yao knocked and waited for the three of them to be summoned inside. There was a momentary sound of scuffling before a very familiar voice issued a sunny command to enter, quite unlike Lan Wangji’s more soft spoken entreatments.</p>
<p>Sure enough, when Meng Yao opened the door, Wei Wuxian stood next to Lan Wangji’s desk, robes slightly askew and with a healthy flush to his cheeks. </p>
<p>“Wei Wuxian, Lan Wangji.” Meng Yao bowed, at which Wei Wuxian offered an exaggerated roll of the eyes. “I’ve brought your charges. Jingyi sang a very clever song today about calligraphy and was eager to come to his lessons and share it with you.” </p>
<p>“Mn.” Lan Wangji waved the boys to the two guqins set up in front of him, and the boys hastened to take their seats. “Thank you, Meng Yao. I will return them to you at the usual time.” </p>
<p>“Lan Zhan, can I stay?” </p>
<p>Lan Wangji levelled Wei Wuxian with a sly look, a flicker of expression that the unobservant may have missed. “If you are willing to participate in the lesson.” </p>
<p>Wei Wuxian took his dizi and twirled it around his fingers. “I’ll just see Meng Yao out.” </p>
<p>Meng Yao allowed Wei Wuxian to usher him out the door. In the hallway, checking to make sure the door was closed, he turned his blinding grin on Meng Yao. “Jingyi did the same with us at bedtime last night. Sat there singing 'need to get to sleep, need to get to sleep, why am I still up, it's no fair A-Yuan isn't talking to me.' And then sang 'it's not fair' in refrain about fifty times before finally conking out. Got pretty catchy after a while. Lan Zhan wont let me put it to music, but I think I can wear him down if you help me.”</p>
<p>“You are a menace, Wei Wuxian.” </p>
<p>Wei Wuxian grinned. “I am at that. And I thought we’d decided I was Wuxian, finally.” </p>
<p>“I have no memory of this decision.”</p>
<p>“Ah, Meng Yao, you’re so cruel to this poor man.” </p>
<p>Meng Yao rolled his eyes and dismissed himself. He didn’t get far—he was still close enough to hear the door open and close behind him and Wei Wuxian’s admonishments that the class had started without him—but paused in step when the sound of music caught his attention. It was beautiful, the player an obvious master of his or her craft. Meng Yao followed the sound until he came to an open door and found himself looking into the private room of Lan Xichen. The man in question noticed him almost immediately and his fingers fell still on his guqin. </p>
<p>Meng Yao dropped into a bow. “Forgive me, I heard the music, and—”</p>
<p>“There is no need to apologize, Young Master Meng,” Lan Xichen assured him. Meng Yao rose from his bow. “You’re here to take the boys to Wangji.” </p>
<p>“Yes. I’m sorry to have disturbed you.” </p>
<p>His smile gentled. “You did not. Would you like to come in? It’s been many weeks since I’ve had the chance to play and I found the need to reacquaint myself with my instrument.” </p>
<p>Meng Yao slipped into the room and allowed himself to be waved into the seat opposite Lan Xichen. The Lord of Jade tugged his sleeves up and began to play once more. The music was soothing, and Meng Yao allowed himself to drift into it, cares all easily forgotten in the easy calm of the sound. </p>
<p>He opened his eyes when the last note drifted through the air and offered Lan Xichen a sincere smile. “Thank you, Lord of Jade.”</p>
<p>“I believe A-Cheng convinced you to call him Lan Wanyin. May I be extended the same courtesy?” </p>
<p>“I have no desire to be discourteous,” Meng Yao said. His desires were much worse, of course, but there was never a call for discourtesy. “Lan Xichen.” </p>
<p>It earned him a smile, and reconfirmed his belief in the other man’s objective beauty. “Have you considered my offer of teaching you to play?" </p>
<p>“I could not impose upon your time,” Meng Yao protested.</p>
<p>“It’s not an imposition, I assure you. While I prefer the xiao as an instrument, I do love playing the guqin, and teaching another person will greatly enhance my enjoyment of it.” Lan Xichen met his eyes. “In which case, it would be a personal favour to allow me to teach you.” </p>
<p>It had to be an exaggeration, but it was certainly a kind one. </p>
<p>The next day, after he’d brought the boys to Lan Wangji, he once again made his way to Lan Xichen’s room. Inside, a second guqin had been set up across from Lan Xichen’s, and the man himself waved to Meng Yao with a smile. </p>
<p>“Let’s begin.”</p><hr/>
<p>Lessons continued abreast; Lan Xichen was an excellent teacher, and Meng Yao dedicated himself to learning. As Jin Zixuan had said, he’d rarely had the opportunity for purely recreational activities. Sitting across from Lan Xichen, more than occasionally shifting his eyes up to watch the serenity of his countenance while he played, became a daily occurrence, moments of peace Meng Yao had never expected nor looked for. </p>
<p>Nie Mingjue joined them occasionally, though his interest apparently less in the music and more in the company, reviewing records and muttering to himself as he read through whatever business crossed his desk. He was first and foremost Sect Leader Nie, after all, and Lord of Blades second. While his Head Disciple took care of training his cadre of cultivators, there was still work to be done on the daily, and the crease in his brow seemed to grow deeper every hour. </p>
<p>One afternoon, he interrupted Meng Yao’s lessons with a frustrated growl. </p>
<p>“Mingjue?” Lan Xichen asked, his fingers pausing on the strings. </p>
<p>“This doesn’t work,” he stated, glaring down at the documents before him. </p>
<p>Meng Yao ventured a curious glance at the records. Some sort of inventory manifest; something that should have been shuffled off into hands with less important matters to attend to, rather than the Sect Leader himself. “May I ask?” </p>
<p>“The administrator who usually looks over this has given birth, and is spending time with wife and child. I can’t pull her away from them, but this entire business...” </p>
<p>He waved at the papers, and Meng Yao took it as an invitation, which it probably was not. Meng Yao shifted around, guqin temporarily forgotten. He twisted the papers around to look at them properly and took a few moments to review the information. </p>
<p>“I think I understand the problem,” he said. The deceptively simple details hid implications more far-reaching than suggested on paper. He picked up Nie Mingjue’s brush and began to jot down notes, losing himself in the simple joys of administrative competence—his usual escape from the realities of Koi Tower, though he’d had little opportunity in the Unclean Realm. </p>
<p>At some point, a cup of tea appeared at his elbow and he drank it absently, his other hand continuing to scribble down plentiful remarks. He barely grimaced over the taste of it.</p>
<p>He looked up only seconds later to find the sun had set. Lan Xichen had disappeared, though Nie Mingjue remained seated across from him, apparently meditating as he awaited Meng Yao’s attention. </p>
<p>“I’m so sorry,” Meng Yao said, abashed.</p>
<p>Nie Mingjue’s eyes opened to slits. “Why? You’ve probably saved me days of frustration.”</p>
<p>“It’s not my place.” If he were exposed to too many of the Unclean Realm’s records, it would give him even more information to feed his father, and he already found himself hesitating to report on what he’d learned. </p>
<p>Nie Mingjue regarded him carefully. “It could be. I’m not saying your talents are wasted on the boys—you do them good service, and I know that Wangji and Wuxian find you invaluable—but it can’t be enough to fully occupy you.”</p>
<p>Meng Yao’s lips pressed into a thin line. “If… it would help.”</p>
<p>“It would.” Nie Mingjue tilted his chin towards the instruments behind them. “I won’t take you away from your lessons again, but perhaps you won’t mind me stealing some of your time in the late afternoon tomorrow?”</p>
<p>He couldn’t refuse; it was, after all, the entire reason Wei Wuxian thought to bring him to the Unclean Realm in the first place. “If you have faith in my abilities, it would be my honour to assist.” </p>
<p>Nie Mingjue looked at him—really looked—and for a horrifying second Meng Yao worried he betrayed more than he meant to. It only lasted a moment, but it left Meng Yao feeling vulnerable and Seen. “Thank you.”</p>
<p>Aflush, and with a wrench in his chest, Meng Yao stood, bowed, and wished the other man a pleasant evening.</p><hr/>
<p>‘Some of his time’ quickly turned into a regular occurence. Despite misgivings, Meng Yao found the work fulfilling. Nie Mingjue surpassed basic proficiency when it came to such business, but lacked the patience for it, and Lan Xichen admitted his uncle tended to most of the Lan Sect concerns and thus he was not intimately acquainted with the necessary skillset. Meng Yao doubted the truth of the statement, but saw it for the kindness it was. Finding a use for him beyond his tutelage of A-Yuan and Jingyi tied him even closer to the Unclean Realm, and in any other situation it would have a way of embracing him as a member of the household. </p>
<p>As such, his gut cradled the truth of it like a rock trapped inside his stomach. </p>
<p>He wrote to his father, insisting that there was no regular sign of the dragons. He suspected they kept themselves to the mountains save when called. How else could Hanguang-jun have reached them so quickly when they’d been attacked? There was certainly nowhere in the Unclean Realm they could be occupying without his knowledge. He knew every corner, now. </p>
<p>Jin Guangshan rarely replied, but the admonishments when he did rarely varied in severity, coached within pleasantries. How <em>pleased</em> he was that Meng Yao had found such a prestigious place in the household. How <em>valued</em> Meng Yao must feel. Perhaps if he focused his efforts on proving himself to them, he might sincerely win their trust instead of being morseled out crumbs of faith easily swept away. </p>
<p>Jin Zixuan caught him unawares after receiving one such letter, coming upon him in one of the sprawling gardens Meng Yao sought out for some quiet. </p>
<p>“Meng Yao?” He looked up and quickly shoved the letter up his sleeve. There was nothing inherently condemning in it, but surely Jin Zixuan knew their father well enough to read between the lines. Before Meng Yao could stand, he held up a hand. “I…” He frowned, consternated. “You need not feel obligated to reply to him, you know.” </p>
<p>“What do you mean?” Meng Yao asked. “Sect Leader Jin honours me by continuing correspondence after I’ve left the service of his household.” The words sat bitter in his mouth.</p>
<p>Jin Zixuan tilted his head and pursed his lips—a tell with which Meng Yao had long familiarity; it meant he wanted to say something but struggled to express himself. He imagined Jiang Yanli had passing familiarity with it as well. “Do as you will. Only,” he blinked rapidly, as though shocked at himself, “If he’s unwilling to pay you the respects he might pay a son, do not concern yourself with paying him the respects you might pay a father.” </p>
<p> </p>
<p>Meng Yao’s eyes widened, and Jin Zixuan turned on his heel and strode off across the garden, shoulders hunched almost to his ears. </p>
<p>He did eventually reply, of course, urging his father to be patient. It had only been a few months, after all, and the Two Lords hoarded their secrets closely. He paused and added a point to tell his father he would only write further if he had something worth mentioning. </p>
<p>Satisfied, he set his attention to the upcoming talks with the Zhu, a minor sect looking for an advantageous agreement with the Unclean Realm.</p><hr/>
<p>Showing up earlier than an agreed-upon hour when conducting negotiations was an underhanded trick used to catch a potential trade partner wrong-footed and give yourself an advantage. It forced the other party to rush through preparations for hospitality, and once negotiations began the lack of preparedness tended to sit in the room like a third party, waiting for acknowledgement and eyeing the host with disdain. Meng Yao encouraged his father towards such tactics on more than one occasion and it always led to him coming out with a greater result than expected.</p>
<p>He’d never known how terrible it felt to be on the other side. </p>
<p>“Wei Wuxian!” he half-yelled, walking far faster than one should in polite society. The man in question looked up from where he stood in the main hall, entertaining Jingyi and A-Yuan with a broad smile. </p>
<p>“Meng Yao, come. We’re just practicing sword forms!” With chopsticks, it seemed. </p>
<p>“Thank you, but I cannot. The Zhu delegation is here earlier than expected, and I can’t find Nie Mingjue or Lan Xichen. Jiang Wanyin is conducting the greetings, but they’ll be needed right away to commence proceedings.”</p>
<p>Wei Wuxian stroked his chin. “I think they’re up at the landing.” Near the footbridge, then, at the vast space near the cliff.</p>
<p>“Thank you again.” </p>
<p>Meng Yao took off, this time at a dead run. He’d already sent word to the kitchens and Jiang Yanli to host for the time being, but too much of a delay would put them at an even greater disadvantage than he wanted to imagine. The Zhu’s home bordered one of the greatest river markets anywhere, and having them as friends meant easier access and fewer tariffs of any number of goods which could not be found naturally in the Unclean Realm. These discussions were essential to the welfare of Qinghe and Meng Yao was determined to ensure they went as smoothly as possible. Now every effort would be undermined with their untimely arrival. </p>
<p>Perhaps it was because he had taken the lead on arranging the reception for the delegation. The pressing need to do well, to prove himself as more than a competent tutor for the boys and casual aid for Nie Mingjue, consumed him for reasons which didn’t bear thinking about. He could tell himself all he wanted it was to ingratiate himself to the Two Lords, but that stopped holding water weeks ago, when he’d first sat down with Lan Xichen to strum out those careful first notes on the guqin for no other reason than his personal pleasure. </p>
<p>He broke away from the trees and stumbled to a halt, eyes widening when he beheld not only Nie Mingjue, but the dragon with him. It was, perhaps, less of a shock this time (lies, it would never stop robbing the breath from his lungs) and Meng Yao credited his other two experiences with the dragons with how he was able to recover himself so quickly. </p>
<p>At first he thought it to be Hanguang-jun. Obviously it couldn’t be Chifeng-zun, with the magnificent white of its scales, but a few steps closer and he realized himself to be mistaken. This dragon had some superficial similarities to Hanguang-jun; their colouring looked quite close. But this dragon was larger, and when it turned its head Meng Yao’s way, he could see the subtle differences in the face and arrangements of its magnificent horns, as well as the shape of the impressive silver-blue mane running along the length of its back. </p>
<p>There were more than two dragons. </p>
<p>Meng Yao would examine this fact later, when the Zhu weren’t waiting on them. </p>
<p>Nie Mingjue stood on the ground near the dragon’s shoulder, a broad wire brush in hand. “What’s the matter?” </p>
<p>Meng Yao bowed. “I’m sorry to intrude, but the Zhu have arrived half a day earlier than expected, and you and Lan Xichen are needed.” </p>
<p>Nie Mingjue huffed. “Xichen isn’t available at the moment, so they’ll have to settle for me.” Meng Yao very carefully did not wince. Perhaps it was the lack of wincing that put a small smirk on the side of Nie Mingjue’s mouth. “I’ll go change. Here, you can help Zewu-jun.” </p>
<p>“I…” Meng Yao blanked. “Pardon?” </p>
<p>“There’s something caught beneath one of his scales,” Meng Yao mentally adjusted the pronouns he’d assigned the dragons. ‘It’ likely wasn’t flattering anyway. “I haven’t been able to find it.” </p>
<p>Zewu-jun’s head twisted around and rubbed against the ground in what Meng Yao imagined to be either agreement or irritation. </p>
<p>“Aren’t I needed for the negotiations?” Meng Yao asked. </p>
<p>“Obviously. I don’t want to have to deal with them. But we need to feed them first, which gives us time to help Zewu-jun.” He paused and frowned. “Have you eaten?” </p>
<p>“Yes, but—”</p>
<p>“Then here.” He shoved the brush into Meng Yao’s hand. It was unlike any brush Meng Yao had seen before; the bristles might as well have been nails with how long and sharp they were. “You’ll want to lift the scale slightly and slide two or three bristles underneath.”</p>
<p>“And it won’t injure him?”</p>
<p>“Nothing short of diamond can pierce dragonhide.” They needed to stop telling him things of such a confidential nature. Nie Mingjue gestured to a broad expanse of Zewu-jun’s back. “It’s somewhere in this area. Don’t worry, Meng Yao. I won’t commence talks until you’ve arrived.”</p>
<p>As though <em>that</em> were the issue. Before Meng Yao could protest again, Nie Mingjue disappeared back down the path. </p>
<p>“That is the most frustrating man I have ever met.” Zewu-jun huffed, a gust of breath smelling of fresh lakewater. Meng Yao bowed. “This one apologizes most sincerely, Zew-jun. I spoke out of turn.” </p>
<p>Zewu-jun shifted again, reminding Meng Yao of the task at hand. He bit back yet another apology and carefully examined the area in question. When he looked closer he could see small crystalline formations embedded all along thumbnail-sized scales, all tightly knit together. He almost doubted he could lift them at all, until he pressed a hand against Zewu-jun’s side. Pins and needles ran up his arm, the fine hairs on his forearm lifting of their own accord. Not unpleasant, he noted. He used his fingernail to ease one of the scales up and gently brushed the area beneath. </p>
<p>Zewu-jun rumbled and Meng Yao snapped backwards. “I’m sorry.” </p>
<p>Zewu-jun tilted his head and regarded him with a surprisingly gentle eye. Breathing through the uncertainty, Meng Yao continued, laboriously checking each scale and brushing underneath the area to clear out any debris. He shifted his gaze between the scales and Zewu-jun’s face, and allowed himself a small, private smile of satisfaction when he noticed the dragon’s eyes half-closed in apparent bliss. </p>
<p>Wei Wuxian proved right once again: they did speak, in their own way. </p>
<p>He finally found the offender, a thumb-sized pebble, trapped near the shoulder joint of Zew-jun’s left leg. Meng Yao daringly tucked it away in his sleeve as a keepsake. </p>
<p>Zewu-jun stood and turned about, regarding Meng Yao with what he could only imagine to be gratitude. It was a humbling thing. The dragon lowered his head and pressed it against Meng Yao’s chest. He stumbled a bit before catching himself, and laid his palm against the crest between Zewu-jun’s eyes. He’d gotten used to the tingling sensation while working, but it returned full force. The rumble returned as well. </p>
<p>Meng Yao bowed. “This one was honoured to be of assistance, Zewu-jun.” </p>
<p>Zewu-jun took off into the air, leaving behind a gentle breeze Meng Yao breathed in for only a moment before turning to head back to his room. He changed quickly and then pulled out his writing utensils to start a missive to his father. </p>
<p>More than two dragons. He hadn’t imagined there were more than two in the entire world, and yet in the Unclean Realm he’d already encountered three. More? Had the dragon he’d seen the night Jingyi arrived been another specimen entirely? </p>
<p>Obviously his father needed to know. Three—or more—dragons put them in a position where they didn’t even need those ridden by the Two Lords. Zewu-jun and Chifeng-zun could remain in the Unclean Realm, outside of his father’s influence, and they could find other ways… </p>
<p>But if there were only the three, it meant Hanguang-jun would be the one to fall into his father’s thrall. </p>
<p>His hand uncharacteristically shook as he imparted the news. Once he completed the letter, he stared at it a moment. </p>
<p>Perhaps he needed to err on the side of caution, and gather more information first. After all, his father relied on him for this. He took the letter and crumpled it in his hand. </p>
<p>On his way to the reception hall, he tossed it into one of the standing braziers lining the hallways. </p>
<p>Nie Mingjue and Lan Xichen, both present and dressed appropriately to their station as the Two Lords of Jade and Blades, remained true to Nie Mingjue’s word. They waited for him to arrive before commencing the discussion.</p><hr/>
<p>The Zhu, as it turned out, were not the cut-throated master negotiators Meng Yao feared. They had, in fact, arrived early due to favourable weather, and brought with them generous gifts for their hosts. Gifts, as it turned out, which included a number of jars of liquor which smelled of over-ripened fruit, yet tasted sweet and nutty and perfectly lovely. </p>
<p>At the celebration that evening to cheer their mutually satisfactory agreement, the Zhu were free with their pours—apparently they valued quick wits and had nothing but compliments for Meng Yao for having outmaneuvered them on more than one point. He had barely finished one cup when another was shoved into his hand, and cheers went up every time he drank. Surrounded by well-meaning men and women, Meng Yao found it hard to refuse, and his belly and cheeks both grew excessively warm. </p>
<p>Eventually, when the last of the Zhu admitted defeat and allowed Meng Yao to escort her to her room, he stumbled back down the corridor towards his own bedroom. The rest of the household had long seen themselves to bed, leaving him to make his way back to his room alone, a precarious wobble in each step. He crossed out into the courtyard separating the guest quarters from the family spaces, and paused when he heard a friendly ‘Yao-ge!’ from somewhere nearby. He twisted around, confused and nearly stumbling over his robes, until he looked up and saw Wei Wuxian happily seated on a nearby roof. </p>
<p>“Is that comfortable?” </p>
<p>“Come up and find out,” Wei Wuxian called. </p>
<p>Meng Yao held a hand to his lips to shush him. “You’ll wake the household.”</p>
<p> </p>
<p>Wei Wuxian grinned and jumped down. He had another jar of liquor in his hand, and waggled it Meng Yao’s way. </p>
<p>“Your constitution is stronger than mine, Wuxian,” Meng Yao told him. He was proud of how his words absolutely did not slur. “I shouldn’t.”</p>
<p>“Hmm.” Wei Wuxian rubbed his nose thoughtfully, then grinned. “Shouldn’t isn’t ‘cannot.’” </p>
<p>Well, no point arguing with that flawless bit of logic. </p>
<p>Somehow, Wei Wuxian managed to maneuver them both up to the roof without cracking anyone’s head open. He helped Meng Yao settle on a surprisingly comfortable spot and passed him the open jar for a long sip. It was even better now, under the open autumn sky, next to Wei Wuxian than it had been in the reception hall surrounded by congratulatory gladhanding. </p>
<p>“You know,” Wei Wuxian said in a voice full of speculation, “I was certain that you’d taken us for a ride during shijie’s wedding negotiations, but you went easy on us, didn’t you?” </p>
<p>Meng Yao took another long sip and laughed. “Jin Guangshan was furious with me.” Wei Wuxian took a drink, spilling liquor down his chin. </p>
<p>“Is that why he let you go so easy?” </p>
<p>Meng Yao scoffed. “I am only a chicken, Young Master Wei.” </p>
<p>“Hey, hey, hey, what happened to ‘Wuxian?’ I worked hard for that.”</p>
<p>“You cannot annoy people into intimacy.” </p>
<p>“That’s what Lan Zhan thought. He was wrong, too.” Meng Yao held out his hand for the liquor and Wei Wuxian gamely passed it over. “What do you mean, you’re a chicken?” </p>
<p>“In terms of the contract, I am a thing of non-importance. An afterthought. Something you see on your way out the door and point to and say ‘that, there. I want that too’ out of spite. Such as a chicken.” </p>
<p>Wei Wuxian frowned, though in his state of inebriation it looked more like a pout. Then again, Meng Yao wasn’t one to throw stones; he was feeling swimming warmth in his belly and a lovely relaxation to his tongue. “That’s not really what you think, is it?” </p>
<p>Another drink, though this one stuck in his throat with a pleasant burn. “It’s in the contract. You signed it.” </p>
<p>“It didn’t say anything about you being a chicken.” </p>
<p>“I am contractually bound to be a chicken, Wei Wuxian. Do not take this from me. I have never been anything this official before.”</p>
<p>The jar, when passed back to him, had only a small sip left at the very bottom and Meng Yao had to shake it free. How disappointing. </p>
<p>“Do you like it here, Yao-ge?” </p>
<p>“I do.
