An unfortunate amount.” The thought of the burnt letter sitting in ashes in the brazier certainly had helped along the smooth slide of liquor down his throat, and now the jar was empty he was left with nothing else to occupy his mind save the exceptionally irritating man sitting beside him. </p>
<p>“Why unfortunate? The Unclean Realm cannot possibly be worse than Koi Tower. And the family is here.” </p>
<p>Once again, he wondered how they all managed to take such a liberal view of the word. Sworn brothership and marriage ties aside, there existed a real quality of relationship between the members of the Household of the Two Lords; one that did not arise merely from official bonds. Sworn brothers could hate each other as easily as blood brothers, afterall. </p>
<p>His eyes drifted shut as Wei Wuxian began extolling the virtues of his would-be home, only snapping awake when his arm shifted and he realized that he really was rather higher off the ground than he usually liked. </p>
<p>“Wuxian, I want to get down now.” Before he fell asleep and rolled over to his untimely end. </p>
<p>“Yeah, Lan Zhan probably isn’t going to be very happy with me. He’d be up here too if he didn’t have to put the boys to bed.” </p>
<p>“Hmm. I wouldn’t have wanted to intrude on a romantic moment.” Not without purpose, anyway. </p>
<p>“Yao-ge, you are so drunk that you wouldn’t have noticed me if I hadn’t called your name.” </p>
<p>Well. That was certainly true. </p>
<p>His foot slipped on the way down, but fortunately he was only a few feet from the ground. He landed on a patch of comfortably soft grass instead of the rock garden lining the sides of the building, for which he was grateful, and rolled over laughing as Wei Wuxian squawked and scrambled down to make sure he hadn’t broken any limbs. To their joint relief, everything seemed to be in working order. </p>
<p>Wei Wuxian helped him up and made sure he was capable of balancing on his own feet—had he been this drunk when he’d scaled the side of the building? It suddenly looked very high—and then tucked himself up against Meng Yao’s side to help him navigate his way back towards his room. </p>
<p>It was sheer confounded luck they ran into Nie Mingjue on the way back. </p>
<p>“Da-ge!” Wei Wuxian called, far too loudly considering the hour. “You’ll help Yao-ge back to his room, yes? It’s so far from mine.”</p>
<p>Nie Mingjue looked back and forth between them. “Should I help you back first?”</p>
<p>“Da-ge, I am hurt by the insinuation I cannot find my own way back to my own room on my own.”</p>
<p>“Wuxian—”</p>
<p>The other man waved a hand and took off down the hall, far steadier than Meng Yao believed was fair, considering how much they’d had to drink. Without Wei Wuxian present to assist, he began listing sideways until Nie Mingjue caught the edge of his robe and pulled him upright. </p>
<p>“This humble chicken apologizes,” he said, fighting to keep his eyes open. </p>
<p>“Chicken?” Nie Mingjue repeated. </p>
<p>Meng Yao stepped forward, and Nie Mingjue gamely stepped up to his side, a silent support beside him as they trod familiar steps through the family quarters. Three months later and it never stopped surprising him to be allowed to live here. </p>
<p>“I’m sorry for this,” he said after a moment’s thought. “You don’t… you probably don’t like it, do you?” </p>
<p>“I share close quarters with my brother and Wei Wuxian. If I really minded escorting drunk men to bed I’d have A-Huan do the rounds at night.” A-Huan. It was so nice they had each other. So nice, their love. It made Meng Yao feel like scum. </p>
<p>“Drunk chickens,” he corrected instead. </p>
<p>“You’re going to need to explain the chicken thing to me.” </p>
<p>They reached his room and Nie Mingjue escorted him inside to put him to bed. It was nice. Meng Yao hadn’t been put to bed since his dubiously unorthodox childhood. He kept it simple: took off the outer robes, removed his simple hairpiece and took off his boots, then tucked him under the covers. </p>
<p>“Mmm. Thank you Da-ge,” Meng Yao whispered before letting his eyes finally close for good. </p>
<p>He heard a very gruff, “You’re welcome, A-Yao,” before succumbing to sleep.</p><hr/>
<p>Two days after the Zhu departed, a letter arrived for Jin Zixuan announcing his father’s imminent arrival. Mang Yao found himself woefully underprepared for the news, and had to plaster the most neutral of smiles on his face as Jin Zixuan turned concerned eyes his way. </p>
<p>Undaunted, his half-brother continued reading the letter, “He sends his best wishes to his son’s honourable hosts, and hopes they will not deny him the chance of seeing his son in person for a short while before the winter comes and makes travel inconvenient. He has matters to discuss both with his son and,” he stumbled, and his eyes flickered upwards towards Meng Yao, “former page.” No surprises there, though he grit his teeth at being dismissed as a mere page considering all the work he’d shouldered in Lanling. “And looks forward to a warm greeting.” </p>
<p>“Like fuck,” Wei Wuxian snapped. </p>
<p>“Wuxian,” Lan Xichen said, though his tone was not nearly as chiding as it probably should have been. </p>
<p>“No, I agree,” Jiang Wanyin said. </p>
<p>“He is my father,” Jin Zixuan murmured, a regretful cast to his face. Jiang Yanli placed her hand atop his. “At least it implies a short visit.” </p>
<p>Meng Yao turned studious attention to his meal, ignoring the weight of the attention placed upon him. He had little doubt as to <em>why</em> the sudden interest in visiting had arisen, and he doubted it had anything to do with missing his son. Meng Yao’s specific inclusion in the letter was doubtless meant to be a warning; he had until his father’s arrival to produce quality information about the dragons, or there would be consequences. </p>
<p>At least there were fewer stairs in the Unclean Realm. </p>
<p>Distraction hounded him during his lessons with the boys and into his afternoon with Lan Xichen and Nie Mingjue. Once or twice, he could tell they were on the verge of saying something, but he rededicated himself to the task before him—both guqin and accounts payable—and after a moment the urge seemed to leave them. </p>
<p>That evening, he sought out the solitude offered by the landing, looking out over the cliff into the distant peaks. His thoughts took on a traitorous tone. </p>
<p><em>Stay away,</em> he thought very hard at Zewu-jun, Chifeng-zun and Hanguang-jun. <em>I know I must betray you, but give me more time.</em> The very request was selfish perfidy, knowing the inevitability of what he had to do. Asking anything of them felt loathsome, and while Meng Yao long understood himself to be a contemptible man, he’d thought there to be limits to what he was willing to do to accomplish his goals. Obviously not. His nature was too set, carved in stone and unbending no matter the price.</p>
<p>He breathed in the mountain air and reminded himself of what all this was for. </p>
<p>He skipped the family meal that evening, ostensibly to ensure the servants were properly prepared for the arrival of Jin Guangshan and his retinue. Unlike those at Koi Tower, who only reluctantly listened to his directives when he proved the efficiency of them, those in the Unclean Realm seemed happy for the input. He provided strict orders as to who could personally attend his father, making it a matter of seniority—all the senior members of the staff in the Unclean Realm happened to be men, save for a few of the aunties working in the kitchen, for which he was prestigiously grateful—and preferences for meals. He could have been quicker about the self-imposed tasks, but he wasn’t sure he could stand the overbearing silent concern everyone projected his way. </p>
<p>It proved fruitless, of course. Both Lan Xichen and Nie Mingjue caught up with him shortly before he made his way back to his room. Lan Xichen carried a tray laden with food, and Nie Mingjue the weight of the world, judging from the set of his shoulders. </p>
<p>He’d been prepared to put his mask away for the day, and felt it straining around his eyes. “Thank you.” He bit any number of other responses back, though he wasn’t sure how successful he was in covering them up entirely. “Everything is prepared for the arrival of our distinguished guest.” </p>
<p>“Meng Yao—” Nie Mingjue began. He froze in the act of opening his door, preparing himself. For what, he had no idea, but his entire body braced as though readying for a physical blow. “You…”</p>
<p>Lan Xichen picked up his husband’s aborted words. “You don’t need to see him. We can find something for you to do. In Gusu, perhaps. You’ve told us you want to see the library. You could leave early in the morning, before he arrives.”</p>
<p>Ah. Not a physical blow, then. Just an emotional one. “Sect Leader Jin has specifically mentioned a desire for my presence. I’m sure he has important matters to discuss with me.” He bit down on his tongue and swallowed back the shaking of his jaw. “Only.” They waited patiently for him to continue and he forced another smile. “I believe that Sect Leader Jin’s constitution is not what it once was, and the sight of anything out of the ordinary might overwhelm him. Perhaps another occupation could be found for the dragons while he is here?” </p>
<p>He didn’t look up to see how the words were received, but the damning silence which followed told him all he needed to know. </p>
<p>“Of course,” Lan Xichen finally agreed, voice strained. </p>
<p>Meng Yao nodded and accepted the plate of food, though the nausea roiling in his stomach suggested it would go to waste. “Good night, Lan Xichen, Nie Mingjue.” </p>
<p>He waited exactly as long as proper for them to return the sentiment before closing the door behind him.</p><hr/>
<p>Early the next morning—earlier than should have been believable, unless his father force-marched his people through the night, which he supposed answered the question itself—Jin Guangshan and his retinue of a dozen cultivators arrived. Nie Mingjue and Lan Xichen met him outside the gates, and did not repeat the formal words Meng Yao remembered from his own arrival. They bowed, and offered every evidence of civility, but there was no request to acknowledge the duties and expectations requested or offered. He’d thought it a tradition of the Unclean Realm to which even the Zhu had been treated, but had no time to ruminate on the difference before his father was stepping forward out of his all-too-shallow bow. </p>
<p>“Sect Leader Nie, Sect Leader Lan, how good to see you. I’m sure you’ve been nothing but considerate hosts to my son and heir.” </p>
<p>“Sect Heir Jin has been an exemplary guest. We of course look forward to hosting yourself, knowing it will be more of the same,” Lan Xichen offered in return. “May we show you to your rooms, and allow you to take a moment to recover from your travels.” </p>
<p>“Ah, no need to stand on ceremony, we’ll all be family soon enough,” Jin Guanshan chuckled. “I’m sure Zixuan can do me the favour of escorting me wherever I need to go.”</p>
<p>Meng Yao had never been so thankful to be completely ignored. Not a single look passed his way as Jin Zixuan escorted their father through the gates, and he managed a few quick moments to breathe before turning to attend Nie Mingjue and Lan Xichen as they made their way back to the reception hall. There would be a banquet tonight—simple, elegantly arranged with dishes both favoured in Qinghe and Lanling, though with no shortage of items which Lan Wangji and Lan Xichen would find appealing—but for all intents and purposes, Jin Guangshan was Jin Zixuan’s guest, and everyone else could hopefully go about the next few days in peace. </p>
<p>The hope lasted less than an hour, when one of the servants nervously approached and told him that Jin Guangshan had requested his presence. “Also,” the man said nervously, “He requested a more delicate touch from the servants assigned to his needs.”</p>
<p>“I’ll speak with him. Please maintain the current arrangements for now.” </p>
<p>Meng Yao’s face ached with the force of keeping his smile in place as he made his way to the guest rooms his father had been assigned. </p>
<p><em>Smile,</em> his mother once told him. <em>Smile throughout all of it. Every moment you want to scream or cry, just smile. It won’t make you feel better. It won’t help you at all. But it will make them think you are weak and happy to receive whatever they wish to dole out, and from that moment on they will underestimate you.</em></p>
<p>These words in mind, he knocked on his father’s door and allowed himself inside. </p>
<p>“Sect Leader Jin,” he greeted, bowing. “This unworthy one is happy to see you well and hale.” </p>
<p>His father waited an awkwardly long time before turning from the window looking out upon a craggy mountainside before replying, his voice strapped of the good cheer he’d presented to Lan Xichen and Nie Mingjue. “I am <em>not</em> well or hale, Meng Yao,” his father stated. Meng Yao cast a furtive look about the room, but it seemed they were on their own. “Do you know why that might be?” </p>
<p>“I… can only imagine it is because of some trespass of mine.” </p>
<p>“Oh, you imagine it to be so? I would think that a whore’s bastard aspiring to be considered my son would know when he has trespassed upon my very limited patience.” </p>
<p><em>Oh, you imagine it to be so?</em> had been the words Jin Guangshan had spoken immediately before grabbing Meng Yao by the throat and throwing him down the steps of Koi Tower. Meng Yao hid shaking hands within his sleeves. </p>
<p><em>Smile, smile, smile.</em> “I’m sorry I have not succeeded in delivering the information you want, Sect Leader Jin. Secrets in the Unclean Realm are preciously guarded, and it wasn’t until I had been here more than a month before I even saw a dragon with my own eyes.” His heart beat simultaneously in both his stomach and throat, having fled his chest in fear of the tone in his father’s voice. </p>
<p>“Did I fail to make myself clear when I sent you here?” Ah, of course, as he had been the one to request Meng Yao’s presence. Wei Wuxian had nothing at all to do with it. “If you ever want to aspire to be more than a blight on my legacy then you will do as you’re told.” </p>
<p>The blow came from nowhere, and caught Meng Yao across the shoulder blades, his father’s ostentatiously heavy golden belt biting through his robes and into his skin. A half-shout escaped Meng Yao’s lips before he clamped them shut, and he held himself still through the next, and the next. Four all together—one for each month he’d failed to deliver his father up the dragons, and each strike imbued with spiritual energy to make sure he felt them a hundred times worse than his father’s otherwise weak arm would allow for. </p>
<p>Considering how he meant to betray the Household of the Two Lords, he took it as his due. </p>
<p>When he was certain his father had finished, Meng Yao straightened. His robes burned against his skin, but the pain paled in comparison to the damage his father had done to him in the past. </p>
<p>“Meng Yao,” Jin Guangshan said with the same oily smile he’d offered Nie Mingjue and Lan Xichen upon arrival. “I would <em>never</em> think to strike my own son, no matter the colour of his eyes.” </p>
<p>Meng Yao, still smiling, nodded in understanding. “Is there anything you need at the moment?” </p>
<p>“No. Zixuan has gone to retrieve Lady Jiang for us to have a family chat. You’re unnecessary.”</p>
<p>He bowed and showed himself out. </p>
<p>Despite the encroaching autumnal cold, it was still warm out and his robes relatively light. They’d done nothing at all to protect his back from the blows, and every step pulled at the injured area until he wanted to fall over. Four blows should have been nothing. Would have been, if his father hadn’t wanted him half-crippled in the name of his failure.</p>
<p>The boys were expecting him, but he had just enough time for a very brief detour to the healer’s, though not to use the salve he furtively collected.</p><hr/>
<p>Dinner that evening proved nearly insufferable in the pall Jin Guangshan’s presence cast on the usually cheerful proceedings. He considered requesting his meal in his room, but decided he needed to be there. If Jin Guangshan thought him to be deliberately missing opportunities to ingratiate himself to the House, there’d be more than four lashes across his back. Unlike the robes he’d acquired during his stay in the Unclean Realm, all subtly embroidered with the heraldry of the Two Lords and conspicuously left in his rooms at random points until they mostly replaced his usual wardrobe, he dressed yet again in the simple attire he’d brought with him. He met Jiang Wanyin outside the reception hall, who frowned at the sight but thankfully declined to speak. </p>
<p>Inside, the tables were all rearranged to suit a more formal setting, though Nie Mingjue and Lan Xichen remained in place as was their due. He kept his eyes averted, slipping into a seat behind Jin Zixuan and Jiang Yanli. Across from them, the Jin cultivators looked on with varying levels of distaste. At least Jin Zixun had been left in Koi Tower; Meng Yao didn’t want to imagine how he’d behave himself even in such dignified company. </p>
<p>“Ah, the Two Lords are too good,” Jin Guangshan laughed boisterously from his seat. “Of course, of course you’re both such attentive hosts as to invite former servants from my household to join us at mealtimes, but I assure you it’s unnecessary.” </p>
<p>As the most prominent members of the household, Jin Zixuan, Jiang Wanyin, Nie Huaisang and Lan Wangji had the dubious honour of sitting in the first row. If he imagined them a wall, he could suffer through a single meal alongside Jiang Yanli and Wei Wuxian. Now that Jin Guangshan had made his sentiments regarding Meng Yao’s presence clear, he could likely get away with missing the shared meals until their guests left the Unclean Realm. </p>
<p>“You’re mistaken, Sect Leader Jin,” Nie Mingjue stated. Baxia trembled beside him. Meng Yao focused his attention on the table before him. “The only ones here besides yourself and your cultivators are honourable members of our Household.” </p>
<p>Another laugh, this one considerably stilted though no more fake. “I suppose the Two Lords organize their house and family much differently than the rest of us, considering the very distinguished collection of persons they’ve brought under their protection.” He grabbed his cup. “Allow me to drink to the health of the Household of the Two Lords, as well as those who are here merely at their forbearance.” </p>
<p>Wei Wuxian, just to Meng Yao’s left, started to reply. Meng Yao snapped a hand out to catch his arm, and while he did not look towards him, hoped that drinking from his own cup got the point across as succinctly as possible. </p>
<p>Still, everyone drank, which was the best Meng Yao could hope for. </p>
<p>Unlike Lan Wangji and Wei Wuxian, who had a brilliant built in excuse of two young children needing their attention and escaped early on, the rest of them were expected to be in the banquet hall late into the night. Jin Guangshan pronounced the meal as ‘an excellent attempt to recreate his favourite dishes’ and his cultivators drank a reasonable amount; nothing to excess, unlike they might have done at Koi Tower, getting too deep into their cups while following the example of their Sect Leader and a certain absent cousin. Perhaps it was the presence of the Two Lords themselves that forced them to temperance.</p>
<p>Meng Yao waited exactly five minutes longer than manners demanded before excusing himself for the evening. His back was on fire after a day full of his usual routine, and he had salve waiting for him in his room he desperately needed to apply. </p>
<p>“Ah, now that it’s only respectable company we can discuss some particulars I’ve been meaning to address…” Followed him out the door. </p>
<p>Let them discuss whatever they wished. Meng Yao took vicious pleasure in noting that no matter what came up, Nie Mingjue would consult him on everything before putting any decisions into effect. He’d proven himself enough to merit such considerations. </p>
<p>He’d finally tucked himself away in his rooms, salve in hand and robes half-undone, when a knock sounded at his door. Beyond irritated, Meng Yao nonetheless answered, ready with a polite dismissal for whoever needed his help so late into the evening and frantically praying it wasn’t his father come to call. </p>
<p>Nie Huaisang swept in without waiting for an invitation. “Well, let’s see then.” </p>
<p>Meng Yao frowned. “Young Master Nie?”</p>
<p>Nie Huaisang snapped his fan shut. “Whatever he’s done to you to send you scurrying off to the healers.”</p>
<p>No point denying it, but hopefully he could scare Nie Huaisang off with formality; as a whole, the family seemed to be allergic to it. “It’s not proper for you to be here, Young Master Nie.”</p>
<p>“Will you stop? I think you’re forgetting you’re in the Unclean Realm instead of Koi Tower. Show me, or I tell Da-ge and then we have to deal with whatever political fallout comes out of him breaking the bastard’s nose.” </p>
<p>Meng Yao winced. “If we might find another insult, it would be appreciated.”</p>
<p>Nie Huaisang’s face fell into something altogether more sombre, an expression which should have been alien on the other man’s face but fit him surprisingly well. “Of course. Yao-ge, please. Let me help.”</p>
<p>If the choice came to Nie Huaisang or his elder brother, at least the former could keep his temper. Meng Yao reluctantly allowed his robes down to expose his back. Nie Huaisang hissed through his teeth. </p>
<p>“What did he want?” </p>
<p>“What he always wants. To remind me of my place.” He trembled at the first touch of salve-coated fingers to his back. “It’s nothing he hasn’t done before.” </p>
<p>“I’ve never been beaten a day in my life.” </p>
<p>Meng Yao cast a droll look over his shoulder. “That much is obvious.” </p>
<p>“Vicious, Yao-ge,” Nie Huaisang barked out with a surprised laugh. Still, his touch remained gentle and the salve worked quickly, easing away the hurt and making his movements significantly easier. When he finished, Meng Yao pulled his under robe back into place. When he turned, Nie Huaisang had a speculative look on his face. “I know what I said, but you absolutely cannot mention this to Da-ge. He values you so much this would drive him to rage.” </p>
<p>Meng Yao swallowed back the bitter taste the sentiment left in his mouth. “I value him too, Nie Huaisang.” Just not enough to keep faith with him and Lan Xichen over his father. </p>
<p>“Once the wedding is over, you will never have to see him again. I give you my word as Sect Heir.” </p>
<p>Meng Yao inclined his head. “Very kind.” </p>
<p>Obviously dissatisfied with the response, but at otherwise loose ends, Nie Huaisang opened his fan again. “Be kind to yourself, Meng Yao. I hear from Da-ge that Jin Guangshan plans to leave the day after tomorrow. If he’s done torturing you, I can make sure you’re busy until then.” </p>
<p>Meng Yao took a breath and nodded. “Yes, please.” He reluctantly met Nie Huaisang’s eyes. “Thank you.” </p>
<p>Nie Huaisang nodded behind his fan and left Meng Yao to his own devices. </p>
<p>He slept on his stomach the next two nights, but by the time his father was ready to leave the wounds were mostly healed thanks to the salve. Nie Huaisang showed up several more times to help him apply it, in and out quick enough to avoid observation. </p>
<p>Still, on the last day, Meng Yao could not avoid the last summons from his father. </p>
<p>The skin on his back pulled uncomfortably under his robes, though it was fortunately much improved from the original injury. From the dissatisfied glance Jin Guangshan leveled his way when Meng Yao arrived to escort him to the gates with more speed than intended, he had expected the pain to last significantly longer. </p>
<p>“It does seem you’ve managed to carve out a place for yourself here,” he said as they made their way along the paths towards the main gate where the members of the household waited to bid their farewells. “You’re in an excellent position, if you’d actually manage to do something with it.” </p>
<p>“I will mark your words during the coming winter,” Meng Yao assured him. </p>
<p>Jin Guangshan paused in step, and Meng Yao fell still beside him. “I know your mother must have taught you some of her arts.” Meng Yao’s fist clenched at his side. “Do whatever you must to ensure I get my due.” </p>
<p>“I think you underestimate the power of the Two Lords and their devotion to one another.” </p>
<p>“Well, whatever you think is best.” He paused and placed a hand on Meng Yao’s shoulders, one of his fingers straying down to press against the topmost stripe of bruising on his back. “I am counting on you.” </p>
<p>Breadcrumbs of affection thus scattered for the picking, he continued on his way. Meng Yao followed in his wake, eventually falling into place next to Wei Wuxian to bid the official farewell. </p>
<p>Once the Jin retinue went on its way, Wei Wuxian slumped beside him. “Can we avoid any more guests until the springtime? That was exhausting.”</p>
<p>“You spent most of your time drunk on rooftops and avoiding conversations,” Jiang Wanyin reminded him. “What do you have to complain about?” </p>
<p>“A-Cheng, I think what you meant to say was ‘thank you, Wei Wuxian, for spending all your time on rooftops and preventing the ruination of shijie’s wedding by avoiding conversations during which you would surely end up punching our honourable visitor or his honourable attendees.’”</p>
<p>“That does sound more accurate,” Nie Huaisang agreed. “Unfortunately, we still have Sect Leader Yao’s visit to look forward to next month.”</p>
<p>They filtered back through the gates, though Jin Zixuan hung back to fall into step with Meng Yao, allowing Jiang Yanli to catch up to her brothers. </p>
<p>“I haven’t seen you much in the past few days,” he said. “Can I tempt you to a game of weiqi now he’s gone?” </p>
<p>Meng Yao sniffed, though a real smile stole across his face. “You’re terrible at weiqi.” </p>
<p>“Admittedly. I thought you might enjoy not having to actively think about anything for a while.” </p>
<p>Despite himself, Meng Yao smiled. “Well, if you insist. I suppose some humility would be good for you.”</p>
<p>Pained, Jin Zixuan replied, “Between you and A-Li’s brothers, I would say you all have that adequately covered.”</p><hr/>
<p>Autumn quickly trailed towards winter, the colourful finery of the great forests surrounding the Unclean Realm drifting to the ground and settling in preparation of the coming snows. Everyone warned Meng Yao about the brutal Qinghe winters, though he still wasn’t sure what to expect. </p>
<p>He quickly came to understand. Autumn in Lanling lasted for months, awash with bright colours and cool winds. In Qinghe, it barely seemed to last a week before snow descended with the bone-chilling and unassailable cold, burying the entirety of the Unclean Realm under deep drifts and icy winds. </p>
<p>Jin Zixuan showed up at his door the morning after the first major snowfall, a sizable bundle of clothing in his arms. The blizzard still raged outside, howling winds throwing sharp snowflakes at the windows.</p>
<p>“A-Li and I wanted to make sure you were prepared,” his brother offered, shoving them unceremoniously towards Meng Yao. The bundle proved to be well-tailored robes made of thicker material than Meng Yao’s current wardrobe, and carefully lined with extra cloth. Meng Yao noted, with some interest, they were also styled in the way of the Two Lords, with dark embroidered clouds and dragon scales. He admitted himself to be touched every time they thought to gift him such attire, as though trying to call him family. </p>
<p>He wore them to lessons with the boys that morning, both of them also bedecked in warmer robes, similarly patterned. It made his chest ache, though not for want of gold fabric, as he might have suspected when he’d first come to stay. </p>
<p>They started with history, and A-Yuan immediately began fidgeting. Meng Yao first attributed it to the stiffness of the new robes. And then, when he began itching the skin of his forearms almost to the point of blood, he decided they must have been quite itchy—he had half a mind to send to the healer for something to ease the discomfort if the boy didn’t soon settle. A-Yuan usually sat much better than Jingyi and paid close attention to his lessons, but his unrest carried through for most of the lesson and well into the late morning. </p>
<p>A-Yuan jumped to his feet in the middle of one of Meng Yao’s sentences, a wild look in his eyes, dancing back and forth with so much nervous energy Meng Yao worried he’d rip up the matting beneath his feet.</p>
<p>“A-Yuan? Are you—”</p>
<p>Before Meng Yao could finish, A-Yuan heaved a great sneeze. Reality seemed to twist around them, and a piercing feeling of vertigo stabbed at Meng Yao through his inner ear. His face twisted in pain, eyes snapping shut against it. The feeling left him again within seconds, and when he opened his eyes.</p>
<p>Oh. </p>
<p>A number of things slid into place, replacing reality as Meng Yao understood it, as A-Yuan turned into a dragon.</p>
<p>
  <em>A-Yuan turned into a dragon.</em>
</p>
<p>Where A-Yuan had stood, a petite dragon remained in place. Lessons promptly forgotten, Jingyi crowed in excitement and tackled the dragon—tackled A-Yuan?—wrapping his arms around a shorter neck than Meng Yao had seen before and avoiding the delicately feathered wings protruding from his sides. None of the other dragons had wings. And also unlike those Meng Yao had seen, gold scales covered A-Yuan’s body save for the burnished copper mane. </p>
<p>Jingyi’s enthusiastic embrace knocked them into the sunlight cast by the nearby window. The dragon was still shorter than Meng Yao and seemed as surprised as he did, whipping his head around to look at himself.</p>
<p>How many others? </p>
<p>All this time he’d suspected more dragons than the ones he’d encountered to be ensconced within the Unclean Realm and surrounding territory, but this went beyond the pale. His mind scrolled through countless possibilities before coming to an abrupt halt when A-Yuan’s tail brushed against his hand. The familiar pinprick sensation proved to be exactly what he needed.</p>
<p>“Jingyi,” Meng Yao said with calm he certainly did not feel. “Please make sure you and A-Yuan don’t leave this room.”</p>
<p>“Yes, teacher,” Jingyi said absently, even as A-Yuan flailed and knocked over the table, spilling ink, paper and brushes across the floor. </p>
<p>Meng Yao stood and exited the room to place a rudimentary locking talisman upon the door. It wouldn’t keep out anyone truly determined to get inside—Meng Yao’s weak cultivation failing him yet again—but hopefully it would deter any curious eyes for long enough for Meng Yao to go in search of help. </p>
<p>After a brief panic attack.</p>
<p>He allowed himself exactly ninety seconds of hyperventilation before a crash from within the room pulled him back to himself. For good measure he added a silencing charm, abruptly cutting out the sounds of Jingyi’s delighted laughter, and took off. </p>
<p>This, of course, had to occur on the day when Wei Wuxian and Lan Wangji were unavailable. The latter had dropped the boys off that morning with a polite nod and a request for Meng Yao to watch them throughout the period in which they all usually enjoyed their guqin lessons. Some sort of disturbance in the higher peaks had been brought to the attention of Lan Xichen and Nie Mingjue, and he and Wei Wuxian had been tasked with its investigation. </p>
<p>In the absence of A-Yuan’s parents, Meng Yao sought out the next most viable option. </p>
<p>The Two Lords tucked themselves away early in the morning with a delegation from the Yao sect, looking to fight against Meng Yao’s recommended adjustments to their trading agreements, and interrupting them would prove a necessary evil. He loathed the idea of interrupting anything to do with the business of the Two Lords, but Lan Xichen and Nie Mingjue were the only ones he felt confident in speaking with. Doubtless everyone save him was in on this secret—the enormity of it and the inherent repercussions near-stupefied him in their scope and scale—but he couldn’t take the speculation for granted. </p>
<p>Every eye in the room turned his way when he entered with a low bow. “Pardon this one for intruding, but there is an urgent matter I must ask the Lord of Jade accompany me to address.” </p>
<p>Sect Leader Yao scoffed. “Are we so unimportant that Jin Guangshan’s bastard can interrupt whenever he pleases?” The sting of the words washed through him in deference to other, much more pressing, considerations. The Sect Leader’s attitude towards him was part of why Meng Yao had excused himself from the meetings, after all.</p>
<p>Nie Mingjue, who had been regarding Meng Yao with some confusion, now leveled a hard glare towards Sect Leader Yao. “If a valued member of our Household declares something is urgent, then we choose to believe them. Just because yours pester you with nonsense doesn’t mean ours aren’t competent enough to deal with minor emergencies on their  own.” </p>
<p>Lan Xichen used the ensuing uproar to escape without further remark. </p>
<p>“What’s the matter?” he asked with a creased brow. </p>
<p>Meng Yao opened his mouth to speak and found his words had fled him. In a show of uproarious impropriety, he grabbed Lan Xichen’s wrist and pulled him along through the corridors back to the room in which he’d left the boys. Inappropriate, perhaps. Indecorous, definitely. But needs must. </p>
<p>All too quickly they reached the classroom and Meng Yao banished the locking talisman with a wave of his hand. He felt it pertinent to leave the silencing talisman in place, and slid open the door to reveal A-Yuan hovering a full five feet off the floor, Jingyi holding onto his tail as though flying a particularly elaborate kite. </p>
<p>“Ah.” Lan Xichen stepped inside and, after a moment’s consideration, Meng Yao opted to join him. He slid the door shut behind them. “A-Yuan.” </p>
<p>The boys both froze, and whatever power kept A-Yuan aloft failed, sending him toppling to the ground. He landed on top of Jingyi, a flurry of limbs both skin and scale. Impressively, the boys managed to disentangle themselves again almost immediately and hopped up. </p>
<p>“Zewu-jun!” Jingyi called. “A-Yuan is born true!” </p>
<p>The awful twisting in Meng Yao’s gut solidified into a mass of cold metal, an anxious press against his sternum until he could barely breathe. It battered against every inch of his self-control in a hard ramming motion coming in waves; he would find himself capable of taking a breath only to lose it again in the next moment. He noted Lan Xichen—Zewu-jun, another dragon, of course he was—eyeing him with concern, even as he smiled encouragingly at the boys. </p>
<p>“How many?” Meng Yao finally asked. </p>
<p>Lan Xichen did him the courtesy of not feigning ignorance. “In total, or in our House?” </p>
<p>Answer enough, he supposed. </p>
<p>“I believe this would be your area of expertise, Lord of Jade, if you would pardon me.” Lan Xichen had the unmitigated gall to look hurt that Meng Yao had reverted to his title, when all Meng Yao wanted to do, truly, was scream. His mask was firm. His smile in place. And when he bowed it was the picture perfect example of the deference due to one so much higher in station that he might as well have been crawling with belly on the ground. </p>
<p>“A-Yao.”</p>
<p>He walked out of the room. Through the corridors. At some point, he thought he heard someone calling his name, but what he needed was his room and solitude and <em>a single fucking moment to process the fact he’d been living among who knew how many legendary magical creatures who had obviously known him to be an duplicitous snake in their midst and justifiably decided not to trust him.</em> </p>
<p>The thing of it was, he could acknowledge with the part of his brain still capable of higher thought, this solved a number of problems. His father could have a dragon, just not one of the Household of the Two Lords. Surely if, as Lan Xichen implied, there were others out there then there had to be some self-serving enough to want the privilege and advancement which could come with serving Koi Tower. He could write the missive immediately informing his father that no, taking possession of the dragons ‘belonging to’ the Two Lords (oh, fuck, Nie Mingjue had to be Chifeng-zun) was an untenable solution to his request and he could begin making inquiries further abroad. </p>
<p>But then, it never had truly been about the dragons themselves. Oh, certainly, Jin Guangshan wanted the power and prestige enjoyed by the Two Lords, but he wanted it at the expense of the Two Lords themselves. To be equal to them by taking what was theirs and twisting it to his own advantage. His father loathed the thought of being beneath anyone, no matter how meritorious their claims to power. </p>
<p>Once, in Koi Tower, there had been a merchant who’d come to sup with his father, very early on in the days of Meng Yao’s position. His wife had been very beautiful, and they’d obviously been in love. No matter his father had every woman in Koi Tower at his disposal. No matter he’d married one of the foremost female cultivators of the Yu. No matter he already enjoyed mistresses aplenty. No matter, no matter, no matter. </p>
<p>The dragons were the same. </p>
<p>“A-Yao?” </p>
<p>He turned, realizing he’d left his door ajar, and found Zixuan hovering, eyes full of gentle concern. “You’re upset.” </p>
<p>Brilliant observation, all things considered. No need to hit him over the head with the obvious any longer, now Jiang Yanli helpfully coached him to civility.</p>
<p>“I have a headache,” he lied. </p>
<p>Zixuan frowned. “Did someone say something to you?” </p>
<p>“Not at all,” Meng Yao said. “It’s nothing, truly.” </p>
<p>He did not like the look on Zixuan’s face. Not one bit. He’d oftentimes considered his half-brother an idiot, with an intentional and deliberate lack of charity. Jin Zixuan was not an idiot. He was an arrogant, over-privileged child who happened to luck into the love of one of the foremost empathetic women in the entire world and had been moulded and shifted until he resembled something human. Meng Yao consciously misjudged him because it was <em>safer</em> to believe him an idiot. Once he became something more, he became dangerous and Meng Yao could not slot him into that category in his mind without beginning to make plans to do something about him. </p>
<p>“Xichen-ge finally told you, then,” Zixuan finally decided. </p>
<p>Wonderful. Another person right not to trust him. Then again, he wasn’t even supposed to be here, was he? He was only the fucking chicken. </p>
<p>“It’s a shock, I know.” Now he was trying to be kind. Meng Yao wanted to hang himself from the rafters. “They’re still the people we know, Meng Yao. The people we love.” </p>
<p>“The people we.” Meng Yao’s last vestige of self-control slipped away from him completely and he snapped. “<em>The people we love?!</em> What do I know about love, Jin Zixuan? What could I possibly, possibly know about it at all?” </p>
<p>Zixuan frowned. “I thought—” </p>
<p>The connection between his brain and his mouth severed under the weight of revelation, as though it were a blade cleanly slicing through every defense and self-protective measure he’d ever put in place. </p>
<p>“No. No you didn’t think. Because if you’d had one reasonable thought in your vapid brain, you and Wei Wuxian would have killed me on the way here and told your father it was an unavoidable accident.”</p>
<p>“I’d never—” </p>
<p>“That’s the problem! You’d never. You’d never lower yourself to spying on the people who welcomed you into their home. You’d never kowtow to your father because you’d never have to. You’d never allow yourself to be used as some ridiculous pawn in a power grab because you are the one with the power. You’d never kill someone in cold blood to protect the people who matter to you. </p>
<p>“You know why he sent me here. All of you must know. And you were right not to trust me and you were justified in keeping every secret locked away for fear of him finding out.” Ah, here came the anger, rising up out of the shock as though the untended pot of emotions inside finally boiled over. “At any moment, I could have stumbled upon the secret and betrayed all of you, and you unbelievably naive idiots had the chance to stop it from happening and you couldn’t.” </p>
<p>Zixuan frowned. “I’m sorry, am I to understand that you are angry at me for <em>not</em> murdering you?” </p>
<p>“I am so far beyond angry I can barely see,” Meng Yao stated with admirable calm. His eyes felt wide and wild even to him, but at least he’d stopped shouting. “If I had allowed myself to put the pieces together any sooner, everything here would be compromised. I have spent months memorizing this place and moving about undetected to gather information on his behalf. A single moment of incaution would have been all that was necessary. There would be a letter in his hands describing everything from the layout of the Unclean Realm to the secrets of the Household. Everything I’ve unearthed since arriving would be his to peruse in such pornographic self-congratulation the entirety of Koi Tower would be left blushing. I still, in this very second, find myself composing it in my head. Or stealing out of here undetected and telling him in person.” </p>
<p>“Why?” </p>
<p>Meng Yao staggered at the simplicity of the question.</p>
<p>Zixuan continued, “Why does his approval matter so much? You might have desired legitimization before, but surely this House—”</p>
<p>“<em>Because I want him dead!</em>” </p>
<p>Zixuan staggered back. “What?” </p>
<p>Meng Yao’s entire body shook. “My mother died waiting for him to free her. For him to sweep in and find us and legitimize me and make every day of the years they spent apart mean something. She <em>begged</em> me to go to him. She saved every coin she could for <em>years</em> that I might have enough to travel to Koi Tower and find him. Money she might have used for medicine when she fell ill, and refused to reveal to me when it became obvious she was dying. I helped her when she vomited blood for months on end as her strength failed her, and the sores stole away her beauty and even then when men still wanted her she wouldn’t allow me to send them away because it might yield just a bit more for me to go. </p>
<p>“I wouldn't leave her. I stayed with her two more years through to the very end, and she died in my arms still insisting that I leave.” There had been so much blood. “That my father would take care of me.” His face twisted, and his mouth shook as tears began streaming down his cheeks. His hands clenched, and for a moment he remembered what it felt like when she finally passed, her body slackening in his arms. “And, oh, you <em>saw</em> the way he took care of me. The reason I came to Koi Tower was to get into his good graces to allow me close enough to kill him. I owe him my mother’s life, and I will repay the debt.” Being a servant never afforded him the chance, no matter how diligently he performed or how many duties he assumed. Jin Guangshan was too seasoned a leader to allow for anyone save his family to come close enough to do him harm.</p>
<p>Finally, <em>finally</em> Zixuan had no response.</p>
<p>“So there you have it. I'm not some misguided little wretch blindly desperate for my father's approval. I am a would-be patricide. And,” his breath caught in his chest. “I can’t be here.” Not among the best people he’d ever known, with their wonderful flaws and loving lives. Dragons, probably, the whole lot of them, and he was as tumorous as the illness which had stolen his mother away. He shoved his way past Zixuan, frozen in the middle of the room, and stalked his way blindly towards the closest door. </p>
<p>The air snapped the breath from his lungs as a knife stuck through his chest, yet he barely noticed through the rest of the pain scoring his flesh. This late into the afternoon, the sun already disappeared behind the mountains, casting the entire Unclean Realm in shadow though the sky overhead remained the light grey of the cloud cover, the blizzard finally passed. He pushed his way through the snow, trusting the loose-packed powder to cover his steps if Zixuan cared to look for him. Not that he thought it likely. Their father was an unworthy, power-hungry lech and rapist, but Zixuan was still filial. </p>
<p>Hopefully this time, he would actually understand the incomparable importance of letting someone die to protect his family. </p>
<p>Meng Yao didn’t want to die. Not frozen to death on the side of a mountain some embarrassingly short distance from the Unclean Realm. But his continued life placed everyone in danger. At some point, he’d unconsciously sworn to himself he would protect Lan Xichen and Nie Mingjue and A-Yuan and Jingyi and all the people they loved from his father as best he could, and the discovery did not change anything. This was the only way to guarantee their safety from Meng Yao’s own, terrible nature. </p>
<p>He forced himself forward, further and further away, fuelled by anger and desperate grief until he could barely feel his limbs and then he forced himself further still. Away from the living quarters. Across the frozen stream where he’d first beheld Lan Xichen and Chifeng-zun and into the wilderness beyond. This was not suicide. This was sacrifice. His mother had sacrificed everything for him—her dignity, her beauty, her life—how could he do any less with what he had for those who had truly seen him as a poisonous blight and treated him with kindness and respect anyway? </p>
<p>Fools, all of them. They’d invited their own demise through their front gate and treated it (him) with kindness he never deserved and could never hope to repay. Doing this for them might cede some of the debt. Hopefully the rest could be worked off in his next life. </p>
<p>The sky dimmed quickly to black as the sun set and the clouds remained. </p>
<p>His foot caught a rock beneath the snow and he stumbled. His hands burned as they shot out to catch himself, the snow biting into his skin with the same pain as having shoved them into an inferno. He tried to clench his fingers into fists and found them unwilling to respond. He grit his teeth and attempted to rise anyway, only for his legs to buckle beneath him. </p>
<p>Better to die this way than with a sword through the heart, he supposed. Gentler, if colder. Or perhaps everyone facing death felt this cold beforehand. </p>
<p>He knew the dragon to be above him before it landed, though there was no obvious sound to announce them. </p>
<p>Chifeng-zun landed before him, alighting atop the snow as though merely another flake falling onto the drift. The same reality-piercing shift filled Meng Yao’s perception, and then Nie Mingjue crouched before him.</p>
<p>“You should go,” Meng Yao whispered. </p>
<p>“A-Yao.” Nie Mingjue never called him that. Or did he? A hallucination, perhaps? No, worse: pity. Meng Yao despised pity. It had been such a relief to become an adult and be subjected to contempt instead. “If you really wanted to die, there’s a perfectly good cliff two miles back you could have thrown yourself from.” </p>
<p>“And pollute your lake?” </p>
<p>Nie Mingjue’s forehead furrowed. “I’m going to bring you back, A-Yao.” </p>
<p>“I’ve betrayed all of you.” </p>
<p>“Have you? Because from what I understand, you spilled your guts to your brother at the slightest provocation, and I’m fairly confident from the lack of messages being sent to Koi Tower that you stopped replying to your father’s letters before his visit.” He watched as Nie Mingjue mentally put the pieces together. “It was why he came, wasn’t it?” </p>
<p>Meng Yao frowned at him. “I can’t be trusted, Da-ge.” If he was going to die hearing ‘A-Yao’ on Nie Mingjue’s lips, he’d damn well claim some of the intimacy for his own. </p>
<p>“Not with yourself, obviously.” Another shift, and Chifeng-zun rested before him. Careful claw-tipped feet wrapped around him and lifted him into the air, winging him back to the Unclean Realm. </p>
<p>Darkness claimed him before they got very far.</p><hr/>
<p>As a child, his mother made every effort to keep him well, usually at her own expense, and Meng Yao rarely fell ill. When he did, she showed him the kindness she never showed herself and spent her carefully-hoarded coins on the best medicines to be found from the greatest doctors in Yunping.</p>
<p>“This is the son of Sect Leader Jin,” she told anyone who would listen. No one cared. Her money bought less for more because of her profession, but at least they were willing to sell to her. “He must be treated with the dignity of a proper young master.” </p>
<p>As shudders wracked his body, every nerve ending alight with painful tremors, Meng Yao could hear her voice whispering in his ear, <em>A gentleman does not sweat, A-Yao. He glows with his inner light.</em></p>
<p>He turned his head into the cloth dabbing at his forehead. It felt cool against his skin and he relished the gentle touch until it pulled away from him. Only proper for them to pull away; everyone needed to pull away or they’d get sick as well. Meng Yao bled poison. </p>
<p>Music broke through his fogged up mind, beautiful and sad and soothing. Sometimes the guqin, sometimes the dizi, sometimes the xiao. He preferred the xiao. It spoke to him in ways the others did not, as though the musician composed songs for his ears alone. Whenever he tried to open his eyes sweat spilled into them and he ended up crying at the sting. </p>
<p>“He’ll recover,” he heard once. The feminine voice held no familiarity. “His core is weak, and the fever is strong, but Chifeng-zun reached him in time to prevent anything serious. He’ll even keep all his fingers.” </p>
<p>Meng Yao liked his fingers; his fingers could hold his brush and play the guqin.</p>
<p>Once he woke with a heavy weight pressed down on his chest, warm and electric, the air filled with the scent of petrichor. He saw nubby antlers and golden scales for only a moment before sleeping again. </p>
<p>When he woke, truly woke, Zixuan was sat beside him. The other man eased him upright and helped him drink a cup of lukewarm tea, a strong arm behind his back to support him. Breathing was hard; his lungs struggled with even shallow breaths, and deep ones felt nigh impossible. When he tried more than a shallow inhale, painful coughs wracked his body and left his mouth tasting like metal. </p>
<p>“Please never do this again,” Zixuan said, settling him back to sit up in the bed. Meng Yao frowned, realizing after a long moment’s consideration he’d been set up in a different room. The healer’s, probably, judging from the nearby shelves stocked with carefully organized jars and drawers. </p>
<p>Meng Yao’s throat still hurt too much to talk, and Zixuan held another cup of tea to his lips. Its medicinal taste lingered long after he’d finished. </p>
<p>He took stock. Alive, recovering from the stupidity of his actions—he really needed to remember acting in anger served little to no purpose—and too weak to escape the conversation looming on his horizon. Judging from the look on Zixuan’s face, he’d rather have died on the mountain. </p>
<p>He said as much. </p>
<p>“Don’t joke about that,” Zixuan told him with a hard glower. “Do you understand how ill you were?”</p>
<p>“I’m sure you’re about to tell me,” Meng Yao replied in a hoarse whisper. </p>
<p>“I am. And you are going to sit through to every word I have to say and <em>listen</em> to them.” He took a fortifying breath. “I killed many men during the Sunshot Campaign. And I'm not sure if any of them deserved to die the way our father does. He spent my entire life shaming and dishonouring my mother. And, you know, I'm glad. Because it gave me principles to hold onto. As long as I'm not like him, I must be righteous. And for all those principles, you are right. I am stupid. Stupid enough to believe that shared blood and a little charity makes us brothers instead of everything else that actually matters. I brought you into Koi Tower and essentially abandoned you to the pernicious sycophants that reside there. I regret three things in my life, and that is one of them.” </p>
<p>“What are the other two?” </p>
<p>“<em>The other two are not relevant to this conversation, Meng Yao, I told you to listen.</em>”</p>
<p>Meng Yao managed a weak smile. “You do have a temper.” </p>
<p>“Yes.” He breathed in and continued, “For all that, I can't imagine killing him. Well, I can imagine it, but probably not to the extent you’ve done.”</p>
<p>“Are you going to stop me?” Meng Yao asked, as good a confession of intent. </p>
<p>“Not by force. By finding you a reason not to throw your life away.”</p>
<p>Should he be insulted? “I'm very sneaky. I could get away with it without risking execution.” Or imprisonment, depending on who caught him afterwards. He imagined Lan Xichen would insist on some sort of enforced seclusion as atonement.</p>
<p>“Of that I have no doubt, but what would you do afterwards? You could come back here, of course, but I think after all this time I know you well enough to know that after killing him, all those pretty masks you like to wear would become real. And you would hate everyone here for believing them. Or you would wonder if they did, and look for shadows in every corner, doubting all of us until it drove you to madness. I don't want that for you, A-Yao. So I am going to find a way to make your life here better than what you think you'll have if you kill him.”</p>
<p>Meng Yao stared. And… stared. And stared. “Your plan, in discovering that I intend to murder our father, is to redeem me through <em>affection</em>?” Another coughing fit punctuated his words, and robbed him of the ability to further list the ways his brother’s plan was completely asinine. </p>
<p>Zixuan’s mouth tightened into a thin line. “It worked for me.” Meng Yao’s brow furrowed in confusion and Jin Zixuan sighed, as he always did when preparing himself to say something he really did not want to. “I made an error in judgement during the war. It resulted in A-Li being very badly hurt, and the two of us trapped in a warded cave for a significant amount of time before we were found.”</p>
<p><em>A coward who spent a month of the war hiding ,</em> the cultivators had said. Meng Yao had wondered, especially after spending more time with him. Of all his flaws, cowardice was not among them. </p>
<p>“It ended up being to my advantage, fortunately. Not in how I conducted myself as a warrior, but how I was able to conduct myself as a man.” He reached out and took Meng Yao’s hand, and Meng Yao tried not to tremble in shock. “Everyone here has an invested interest in you.” He winced. “Some more than others.”</p>
<p>Meng Yao needed to return to that later. “It’s certainly a strategy I never considered employing against anyone. May I ask how you decided it to be the best course of action?” </p>
<p>“You’ve been unconscious for a week, A-Yao.” A-Yao again. “I had plenty of time to talk it over with A-Li.” </p>
<p>Meng Yao pondered the words through another cup of tea and soon after found himself drifting towards unconsciousness. Zixuan helped him settle back down into the bed and pulled the covers up. </p>
<p>“Zixuan,” Meng Yao whispered. </p>
<p>“Hmm?” </p>
<p>“I never really thought you were stupid.”</p>
<p>“I wouldn’t blame you if you had. And you’d certainly have been in good company.” </p>
<p>Meng Yao smiled and almost immediately nodded off.</p><hr/>
<p>There wasn’t someone present the next time he woke up, though an incense burner wafted delicate smelling scents his way, which relaxed the ache in his lungs with each breath. He still struggled to breathe deeply, and coughs wracked his body when he tried, leaving him half-paralyzed and exhausted on the bed. </p>
<p>The sound summoned a new arrival to his room. It was not the healer he knew, and at this point Meng Yao fancied he knew all the household staff in the Unclean Realm. This woman struck him as being much harder to manipulate than the older man who Meng Yao had come to know, which likely meant him to be stuck in bed for quite a bit longer than he’d prefer.</p>
<p>"Lean forward, I want to check your breathing."</p>
<p>He did as he was told; it didn't occur to him until his body had already moved to refuse.</p>
<p>"Your lungs suffered from the exposure, not necessarily permanent, unless you ignore my instructions." She checked the incense burner and nodded at whatever she saw within. </p>
<p>"May I ask who you are?"</p>
<p>"Wen Qing," she said without ceremony. </p>
<p><em>Wen Qing</em>, Meng Yao silently repeated to himself. It remained a bleeding sore in his father’s side that remnants of the Wen still existed when he had advocated so strongly for their elimination. While he’d publicly backed the Nie-Lan offers of clemency for the non-cultivators who survived the war, he privately seethed over what he considered to be disrespect of his wishes. By the time he’d arrived at Nightless City, to hear tell, the decision to spare the civilians had already been made, and he’d been denied the opportunity to have his say in the matter. Those who remained gathered in their home on Dafan Mountain. </p>
<p>"I was sent for after Chifeng-zun found you half frozen to death."</p>
<p>Somehow, despite Zixuan's words earlier, he'd doubted the severity of his condition (though he'd gone into the snow with no intention of returning). From Wen Qing, he believed it, though he still wasn't sure how he felt about having failed. Failed them again. Failed to be honest. Failed to redeem himself. Failed to keep the one secret he'd hoarded against his heart since burying his mother among all the other dead prostitutes of Yunping. </p>
<p>"I'm going to loosen some of your muscles to ease your breathing," she told him, retrieving a sleeve of acupuncture needles from across the room. "Move forward and lay on your stomach."</p>
<p>She efficiently adjusted his body with brusque hands and then took a place at his side to begin easing needles into his back. The tension slowly eased away, and the laborious heaving of his lungs eased with each inhale.</p>
<p>He must have looked truly pathetic when Nie Mingjue and Lan Xichen walked in a short time later.</p>
<p>"Chifeng-zun, Zewu-jun." There was an odd tone to Wen Qing’s voice Meng Yao could not immediately parse. </p>
<p>"Lady Wen," Lan Xichen answered. Nie Mingjue said nothing. "We are interrupting."</p>
<p>"Yes," she agreed. She slid another needle into Meng Yao’s back. </p>
<p>Heavy silence pervaded the room, and Meng Yao lacked the strength to break it. After all, what could he say that they'd care to hear? Perhaps his hesitancy to speak drove the sad sigh he heard drawn up through Lan Xichen's chest, and the dissatisfied rumble from Nie Mingjue. For a moment, Wen Qing placed a hand against Meng Yao's back, sans needle, and he wondered if she understood.</p>
<p>"Would you like me to summon you when I've finished?"</p>
<p>"'Summon' us?" Nie Mingjue growled.</p>
<p>"Mingjue, please." Meng Yao could imagine the look on Lan Xichen's face. The strain he got around his eyes when trying to play peacemaker. "Yes, Lady Wen. If you could."</p>
<p>They left together.</p>
<p>"I didn't realize the remnants of the Wen were so close to the Two Lords,” Meng Yao murmured. For all they’d defied Jin Guangshan’s wishes around their annihilation, no reports existed to indicate they held any further ties.</p>
<p>Wen Qing did not reply until she finished the course of treatment, and when she did she made no mention of his remark.</p>
<p>"I don't have to call them back," she told him, tidying up the remainder of her workspace.</p>
<p>"You don't like them," Meng Yao surmised, mystified. He couldn't fathom anyone with good judgement disliking Lan Xichen, and Nie Mingjie for all his gruffness, tended to command respect if not admiration. </p>
<p>"I came at Wei Wuxian's request," she said. It spoke volumes. “None of us would still live, if it weren’t for him." Wen Qing briskly changed the subject, "You know about us, but are not blooded." Us? The Wen? No. There was a certain weight behind the proclamation he’d come to associate with dragons. </p>
<p>"Blooded?" he repeated.</p>
<p>Wen Qing explained, "A child of dragons who was not born true or a human gifted with blood by one of our kind." He could guess from context what born true meant; hadn't Jingyi said it of A-Yuan when he'd first turned?</p>
<p>"I am not. What does that mean for me?"</p>
<p>Wen Qing paused. "There have been very few humans who know our secret without being blooded. If you look for them now, you will not find them." She turned back to him to check his back. "When I draw these out, you will be very relaxed and tempted to sleep. I can find ways to keep you awake if you wish to speak to them."</p>
<p>Meng Yao thought of the gentle disappointment in Lan Xichen's tone, and what look Nie Mingjue must have had in his eyes when he'd been fully apprised of Meng Yao's treachery, certainly hidden away when he’d come to retrieve Meng Yao from the mountains.</p>
<p>"Sleep sounds like a safer option," he whispered.</p>
<p>Perhaps he let slip more than he realized, as Wen Qing followed up with, "It is not cowardice for an injured animal to retreat and hide until its wounds are fully healed." </p>
<p>He was asleep before she'd removed the third needle.</p><hr/>
<p>The cycle of waking-treatment-sleeping continued far longer than Meng Yao felt comfortable with. On the one hand, he was pleased they hadn’t sent him away (thrown him down the stairs) from the Unclean Realm (yet). On the other, waiting for repercussions became a painful anticipation which made his muscles clench and resulted in Wen Qing’s ongoing annoyance when it undid her hard work. Zixuan outright stated Meng Yao would be permitted to stay, but while it could be attributed to his brother’s optimism, and quite possibly true, he could not imagine what he’d done would be so easily overlooked. He counted his sins on every needle pushed into his skin, and dreamt about them when they were removed. </p>
<p>Lan Xichen and Nie Mingjue did not return. </p>
<p>That being said, once Wen Qing announced him capable of staying awake for longer periods of time without exacerbating his illness, every other member of the household decided to trod their way through his door in a relatively steady stream of company. </p>
<p>Jiang Yanli came first and was, perhaps, the only one he expected to join him besides Zixuan. He had been uncharitable towards her when he’d first seen her; her beauty really shone through when one came to appreciate her kindness. </p>
<p>“Whenever A-Xian was trapped in bed when we were children, I made him soup,” she announced, gracing both Meng Yao and Wen Qing with a warm smile. </p>
<p>Meng Yao’s brow furrowed. “Not Jiang Wanyin?”</p>
<p>“Dragons don’t fall sick very often, and when we do it is generally nothing soup can cure.” ‘We’ he whispered to himself. He could only imagine Jin Guangshan’s reaction to the statement; little wonder Wei Wuxian had been so insistent on them living out of the Unclean Realm. She ladled out a steaming bowl of something that somehow managed to smell of home and love, underlain with beef and ginger. “It’s not as fine as I could manage in Lotus Pier, of course, and my brothers would both be upset if I made their favourite for you and wouldn’t share.” </p>
<p>He almost offered to share, then took a bite and realized that, no, he had no plans to do so at all. </p>
<p>Jiang Yanli sat back and watched him carefully. “A-Xuan tells me he’s spoken with you.” Meng Yao reluctantly nodded, though he kept his eyes fixed on his bowl. “Did you understand what he said?”</p>
<p>“I believe so, Lady Jiang.” </p>
<p>“Yanli-jie,” she corrected. </p>
<p>He frowned at his bowl. “I’m afraid you are all trying to foist intimacies upon me I do not deserve and have not earned.”</p>
<p>“Perhaps, but they are ours to offer.” She reached out and touched his hair, and his heart ached for his mother. “And in case no one tells you otherwise, you are free to decline them.”</p>
<p>His spoon froze halfway to his mouth. “Why would I?” Not rhetorical, he wanted her insight. He had his own reasons for reluctance, of course, but what did Jiang Yanli see when she looked at him? </p>
<p>“For fear of giving yourself power over us, perhaps. Power you would be afraid of abusing,” she replied, as though she had not succinctly summarized his true nature and not trembled at the grotesquerie of it. </p>
<p>The spoon trembled in his hand. “You see quite a bit, don’t you, Yanli-jie?”</p>
<p>Jiang Yanli inclined her head and refilled his bowl.</p><hr/>
<p>Jiang Yanli’s visit prompted more. Wei Wuxian swept into the room later that afternoon with an armful of loquats and dropped down next to Meng Yao, tumbling the fruit across the bed. Where had he even acquired loquats this time in the year? They looked suspiciously fresh. </p>
<p>“Here,” he said, passing the one over. “You’re about to be subjected to the typical parade, and I thought it might be good for you to keep up your strength.”</p>
<p>Meng Yao stared at the fruit. “Dare I ask?” </p>
<p>“Eh, whenever anyone gets injured we all end up in the recovery room eventually.” He looked at the loquat in Meng Yao’s hand expectantly until he took a bite. He detected the faintest whiff of spiritual energy, perhaps to keep it fresh. “I keep them around all year for Lan Zhan. I’m not sure if he likes them all that much, but I once threw one at his head and now they make him smile.</p>
<p>“Now then.” Wei Wuxian placed his hands on his needs and regarded Meng Yao very seriously. “I think shijie gave you the soft talk, yes?” </p>
<p>“Is this where you threaten me?” He’d been expecting it, after all. If not from Wei Wuxian, then from Nie Mingjue.</p>
<p>“That’s going to come whenever Jiang Cheng stops making eyes at Wen Qing and drags himself in here.” We Wuxian leaned forward. “You’ve only been with us for half a year. I knew, when Jin Zixuan asked me to get you out of Koi Tower—” </p>
<p><em>What?!</em> “What.”</p>
<p>Wei Wuxian sighed. “You were never a chicken, Meng Yao. Your brother wanted you out of Koi Tower and I agreed to it, even knowing what Jin Guangshan would ask of you. I saw it in his eyes after you left the meeting. We didn’t not trust you, but hoped that you’d be able to create ties with us strong enough to keep you from actually doing it.”</p>
<p>Meng Yao chewed over this a moment, now that time had distanced him from his rage when Zixuan had admitted as much the first time. “Why take the risk?” It made no sense. Only one wrong move or moment would have resulted in Jin Guangshan knowing everything about all of them, and Meng Yao considered himself clever enough to easily orchestrate it. “You don’t know me.” </p>
<p>“The House—”</p>
<p>“You, Wei Wuxian, were the one to decide to bring me here. I can somewhat understand Zixuan’s desire to do so, but you were the one to ultimately make the call. Nothing can convince me you’d blindly do what Zixuan asked of you, and while you’re idealistic to the point of suicidal, you’re not an idiot. The benefit didn’t outweigh the potential loss.”</p>
<p>Wei Wuxian looked down at his hands, clenched into white-knuckled fists atop his legs, lips twitching. “Someone took a risk on me once.” He seemed determined to snap himself out of whatever maudlin thoughts possessed him, because a moment later he looked up with an obviously forced grin. “I like this version of you, by the way, saying what you mean.” </p>
<p>The sound of yelling from outside the door drew their attention and Wei Wuxian relaxed his fingers from where they were still clenched tight. “Well, here’s the loud part. Good luck. Remember, he usually doesn’t follow through on his threats, but don’t talk back just in case he’s in a mood.” </p>
<p>Like the consummate asshole he was, Wei Wuxian opted to open the window and creep out instead of facing his brother’s temper. Jiang Wanyin stormed in seconds later in a bluster of threats against Meng Yao’s extremities, barely pausing to take in a breath despite walking into a gust of winter air. </p>
<p>“...And why the fuck is this window open?”</p><hr/>
<p>“Teacher! We wrote a song for you to help you feel better."</p>
<p>Meng Yao snapped awake with a start; he hadn’t even noticed he’d nodded off. He ledger he’d been reviewing—snuck into him post-tantrum by Jiang Wanyin as a favour to stem off the boredom of the sick room, and conspicuously only detailing the records of Lotus Pier—sat open on his lap. He blinked the sleep out of his eyes and tucked the ledger to the side to grace Jingyi and A-Yuan with a smile. Lan Wangji stood behind them, A-Yuan’s guqin in hand. </p>
<p>"Did you?" Meng Yao cast a pleading look at Lan Wangji. The non-committal eye he received in return spoke worlds, and most of them unanimously chorusing, ‘you deserve this.’</p>
<p>Meng Yao sat through all twelve verses, which seemed to cover everything from a plea to avoid injury in the future to condemnation of Master Nie Liu’s teaching skills. It was actually quite sweet, he had to admit, especially when Jingyi went out of his way to freestyle his assurances that while Meng Yao was terribly bossy and being forced to learn the biographies of famous scholars the worst torture ever inflicted, they hoped he'd resume lessons with them soon.</p>
<p>It was very enthusiastically done. </p>
<p>At the end of the song, the boys settled in for a visit and to report on everything they’d learned since Meng Yao left them after A-Yuan’s first change to his dragon form. Apparently this ‘Master Nie Liu’ lacked some basic context regarding clan history outside that which involved the Nie, and Meng Yao resigned himself to having to reteach a number of incorrect assumptions about the formation of traditional borders. </p>
<p>Eventually, Lan Wangji herded the boys out—presumably into incompetent academic hands—but returned to Meng Yao's side moments later.</p>
<p>"I will play for you, if I may?"</p>
<p>"After I've already been so excellently serenaded?"</p>
<p>A small, almost invisible smile touched the corners of his mouth as he withdrew his guqin and began strumming a familiar melody. The spiritual energy suddenly pervading the room soaked into Meng Yao's very marrow, easing him towards rest. This, beyond anything else, impressed him with the oddity of how the household must view him; Lan Wangji never impressed him as the forgiving type. Between him and Lan Xichen, Meng Yao imagined the latter to be the one willing to play.</p>
<p>He had yet to see either him or Nie Mingjue since Wen Qing turned them away. </p>
<p>The last notes of the song drew to a close, and Lan Wangji turned to go. </p>
<p>“Second Young Master Lan,” Meng Yao said. Lan Wangji paused and regarded him closely. “I can understand the forgiveness of others. Jiang Yanli, Zixuan. Even Wei Wuxian and Jiang Wanyin. But I feel forgiveness without sign of proper repentance is not in your nature, and I have done nothing to show earnest regret for my actions.” </p>
<p>Lan Wangji’s lips pressed together. “The boys value you very highly. And trust you implicitly as their teacher.” Meng Yao nodded, though the words sat heavy in his gut. “It would have been very trivial of you to abuse this trust when you saw A-Yuan change, yet your first action was to seek out my brother.” </p>
<p>Meng Yao considered this. “I do not wish to see them harmed.”</p>
<p>“This is why you have no need of forgiveness from me.” He pressed his hands together and bowed deeply, as though Meng Yao was a person of greater standing. A man of worth. </p>
<p>“Thank you,” Meng Yao replied, and for good measure, “Hanguang-jun.” </p>
<p>The smallest sliver of a smile touched Lan Wangji’s mouth, and he showed himself from the room.</p><hr/>
<p>On the seventh day after he'd woken, Wen Qing finally declared him fit to leave her care, albeit with strict instructions not to overexert himself. Having spent such close quarters together in the meantime, she’d impressed him with her ruthless dedicationt to his welfare, if not her taste in men. </p>
<p>"If I have to spend another two weeks under the roof of the Nie, a little cold will be the least of your worries," she told him strictly.</p>
<p>"Understood," Meng Yao said quietly. "And may I compliment the fine new comb in your hair?"</p>
<p>Wen Qing glared at him. He stared back impassively until they both nodded in silent accord.</p>
<p>Zixuan arrived to help him back to his room, a strong presence at Meng Yao’s side as he slowly hobbled away from the healer’s. The hallways of the Unclean Realm bit with the winter cold, and when Meng Yao shivered Zixuan tugged him closer. </p>
<p>“May I ask you something?” Meng Yao questioned. Zixuan nodded. “The Two Lords…” He paused, not sure what he wanted to ask. He had been the one hesitant to see them, after all. Perhaps because, of all the forgiveness he’d received, it was theirs he wondered about the most. </p>
<p>“Whenever you’re ready.” </p>
<p>Might be a while, then. Still didn’t the avoidance make things easier, in some ways? Zixuan said he wanted to give Meng Yao something else to live for, but without the Two Lords supporting the idea, he’d be hard-pressed indeed. </p>
<p>Despite the words he wondered if they might be waiting for him at his door to help him settle for the evening. While there was someone standing amidst his things, it was the wrong Nie entirely.</p>
<p>"Leave him with me, Zixuan," Nie Huaisang said.</p>
<p>His brother hesitated, a brief tension that lasted all the way through what quickly became an uncomfortable silence. Finally, he looked to Meng Yao. "I can remove him, if you don't want him here."</p>
<p>Nie Huaisang whined in protest, but Meng Yao shook his head, though he was touched Zixuan offered to stand against the House on Meng Yao’s behalf. "It's fine." </p>
<p>Still unsure, and rather sweetly so, Zixuan finally nodded and left them together. Once the door closed behind him, Nie Huaisang’s demeanour changed entirely, from spoiled child to straight-faced adult. Meng Yao had seen glimpses of it before, notably when Nie Huaisang had helped him recover from his father’s beating, but this was far and away the most serious he’d ever seen the other man. It suited him surprisingly well, leaving Meng Yao to wonder at how easily he’d fallen for the deceptive, considering how many masks he employed on his own. </p>
<p>"Tea?" Nie Huaisang offered.</p>
<p>"Shouldn't I be the one offering?" Meng Yao asked.</p>
<p>Nie Huaisang hummed, but poured for them both anyway. After a week of the astringent medicines Wen Qing had dumped down his throat, Meng Yao was ready for a change, even if it meant the burnt tree branches stewed in water that passed for tea in the Unclean Realm. When Nie Huaisang offered him a cup of a pleasantly floral blend instead, he looked at the other man with surprise.</p>
<p>Sitting across from one another, they stared each other down, both taking occasional sips of tea.</p>
<p>"Tell me, Yao-ge, what do you think of my fan?" Nie Huaisang snapped it open to show off the same hideous specimen he'd showcased in their first meeting.</p>
<p>Meng Yao's lips pulled, though not in anything that might be called a smile. "It's an abomination of colour, poor line work and nonsensical arrangement of theme. Jingyi could do better while blindfolded with his own ribbon, and if it never assaults my senses again I'll die a happy man."</p>
<p>"Very good," Huaisang told him. He closed it and passed it over. "It's all yours. I'm sorry to say that all the others you had have been mysteriously destroyed, but this one should serve you well." He produced another, much more tasteful specimen from his sleeve for his own use.</p>
<p>"You're too kind," Meng Yao said. He angled for sarcasm and missed by a mile. “Are you…?” </p>
<p>“Blooded,” Nie Huaisang replied, a slightly regretful downturn to the corner of his mouth. “My father was born true, as well as Da-ge’s mother, but not mine. For a long time, he believed himself to be the last.” There was a wealth of meaning in there; out of habit, Meng Yao tucked it back to the recesses of his mind for review at a later time. "Zixuan says you're planning to kill your father." </p>
<p>Ah, so he’d made it common knowledge. How delightful everyone could now share in condemnation of Meng Yao’s debasement. He could not imagine either Nie Mingjue or Lan Xichen being willing to forgive such desires. ‘When you’re ready,’ indeed. Little wonder they were avoiding him. </p>
<p>"Yes."</p>
<p>"I assume you have a plan in place, if not yet in motion." Meng Yao nodded. "Tell me. I think between the two of us we can really make him suffer."</p>
<p>Meng Yao's eyebrow twitched up. "Would your brother approve?"</p>
<p>"Da-ge's approval means everything to me, but not at the expense of his safety. Do you think he'll continue to be safe once your father realizes that you're no longer of use to him, and sends someone without unreconciled trauma to spy on us? Someone who might do it for the money?" His face twisted in disgust.</p>
<p>"I am perfectly reconciled to my trauma, thank you," Meng Yao told him pertly.</p>
<p>Nie Huaisang fanned himself and waited patiently.</p>
<p>Well, a second opinion couldn't hurt. "Very well. Though I’m not sure why you’re interested in helping me.” </p>
<p>“Jin Guangshan sent a spy into my home to uncover secrets he has no right knowing, for the purpose of injuring my family.” Nie Huaisang’s eyes narrowed. “There are sins I do not forgive.” </p>
<p>“Zixuan seems to think if I follow through it will lead to my damnation.” </p>
<p>“Zixuan isn’t taking into account that you might do so with someone else’s help and support. Having someone who truly knows you goes a long way in maintaining one’s sanity, don’t you think?”</p>
<p>Meng Yao tilted his cup up in acknowledgment, and settled in to plot.</p><hr/>
<p>"He's back in his room, now," Xichen said that evening, brushing out his hair as they prepared for bed. "We should go to him."</p>
<p>Nie Mingjue held back a sigh. "We agreed to wait until he comes to us. We can't force it."</p>
<p>Xichen lowered his comb and bowed his head. He unreasonably shouldered most of the blame for Meng Yao's impromptu hike, despite Mingjue's reassurance that if anyone was to blame it was Jin Guangshan, the fucking toad. Two years separated them from the Sunshot Campaign, and Xichen had apparently forgotten the tremendous amount of work Yanli-jie had put in to turn Jin Zixuan into something even beginning to resemble a decent man. And for all he had come to respect his soon-to-be brother, he did not come with halfsomuch baggage as Meng Yao. </p>
<p>Fortunately, he and Xichen both had shoulders broad enough to help bear the burden.</p>
<p>"If I thought I had betrayed our family, I would do something worse than a poorly-planned walk into the snow."</p>
<p>Xichen turned a frown his way. "Please don't jest, Mingjue."</p>
<p>"I'm not." Their eyes met and held a few moments. Not bothering to withhold the sigh this time, Mingjue stood and crossed the room to take the comb from Xichen's hand. He continued the ministrations with a gentle touch. </p>
<p>"We should blood him," Mingjue decided.</p>
