<p>"Yes." Xichen tilted his head up, and accepted a not-entirely chaste kiss. "It will bind him tighter to us." </p>
<p>Not that blooding meant a guarantee of loyalty, as Wen Ruohan proved. Mingjue's jaw clenched as it always did when the blasphemies of the deceased Sect Leader came top of mind. Having Wen Qing in the Unclean Realm did nothing for his temper, even if the two of them had come to their grudging peace with one another. It was difficult for Mingjue to look at her without remembering that he'd almost cleaved Wuxian in twain, that there still existed a small scar sitting at Wuxian's hairline because Mingjue almost couldn't pull his blow when Wuxian had inserted himself between her and Baxia. Having her so close sat ugly in his stomach, because it reminded him that while Wuxian had forgiven him, joined his flight and called him Da-ge, Mingjue wasn't confident he'd forgiven himself.</p>
<p>Part of his reluctance to attempt another visit to Meng Yao's side was, perhaps, fuelled by her presence in their infirmary. He and Lady Wen would never be friends, for all he appreciated the assistance she offered them.</p>
<p>"After the wedding," Mingjue suggested.</p>
<p>"That won't be until the fall," Xichen said with disappointment.</p>
<p>"Give him some time to learn our ways, Xichen. He's clever, it won't take him long, but he should know what he's committing to before we force anything upon him."</p>
<p>"I would never!" Xichen insisted.</p>
<p>"A poor choice of words, husband. I beg your pardon." Mingjue pressed another kiss to his mouth apologetically. "I know you wouldn't."</p>
<p>Mingjue began running the comb through his thick hair again, and Xichen's eyes drifted shut in contentment after a few moments of care. He relaxed backwards into Mingjue's chest. The first time Mingjue had done this, fresh off the battlefield, blood matting Xichen’s beautiful tresses down to his scalp, he'd thought Xichen would look lovely in Nie braids. Satisfying, all these years later, to know he had been right.</p>
<p>When he finished, reluctant as he was to put down the comb, he undid Xichen's ribbon, and allowed his husband to bind it about his wrist. Mollified, Xichen rose and waved Mingjue into his abandoned seat, nipping the comb easily from his hands. Feeling indulgent, Mingjue acquiesced and allowed Xichen free reign of his hair. His braiding had come along, the artistry almost as fine as those born into the Nie. He finished with a simple sleeping plait and ran his fingers along the side of Mingjue’s neck, curling around to his jaw, cupping his face in his warm palm. </p>
<p>The first time he’d looked upon Xichen, his thoughts sang of frost. The Gusu Lan were only just recovering from Wen Ruohan’s first foray into domination, scouring the world for dragons to feed his desire to assume power to which he was not born and could only aspire. Cloud Recesses burnt to ashes. And there stood the Sect Heir, untouchable and ferocious and preparing to bring devastation upon those who had harmed his people. </p>
<p>Wangji had been sent away with the most precious of the books, leaving Xichen to protect those who remained. Holed up in a warded underground cave, they’d managed to withstand the assault of the Wen until Mingjue and his forces showed up to offer assistance. When he’d looked on Xichen and seen winter, the sort that brought devastation and death, he hadn’t known he was looking upon another dragon. He’d thought himself to be the last. Wen Ruohan must be furious in death that his aim of shaking free other dragons hidden within the human Clans for his own purposes would end up uniting them against him instead.</p>
<p>Discovering Xichen’s true nature hadn’t come until much later, with the taste of Xichen’s blood in his mouth as his own soaked the earth beneath him, the man himself staring down at him in a mix of astonishment and awe. </p>
<p>Before the Sunshot Campaign, Mingjue despaired of A-Sang’s love of irony. He’d since come to appreciate it.</p>
<p>(Another irony: the man Jin Guangshan sent to destroy them might end up being the man’s own death walked through their door.)</p>
<p>“Come to bed,” Xichen whispered. </p>
<p>Mingjue turned his head to kiss Xichen’s palm and stood to follow his husband.</p><hr/>
<p>Meng Yao slowly made his way on his own to the classroom the next morning, met by Master Nie Liu, who had the audacity to look surprised to see him. </p>
<p>“Thank you for your assistance these past weeks, Master Nie Liu,” Meng Yao said with a bow. “I am pleased to resume my lessons with the boys.” </p>
<p>Nie Liu appeared deeply unimpressed. “I have some concerns about the content of your lessons, Master Meng.” Meng Yao waited for him to continue. Flustered when he ventured no questions, Nie Liu continued, “The Nie have never felt it necessary to include philosophical discourse in our history teachers. We are objective in all things.” </p>
<p>Meng Yao highly doubted it. “Then how fortunate for them the boys are Lan.” </p>
<p>Nie Liu’s face twisted angrily. “While you are in the Unclean Realm, it would behoove you to follow our customs.”</p>
<p>“While I am in the Unclean Realm, I will strive to bring honour to the Nie Clan and the Unclean Realm, per the Clan motto. Were I derelict in my educational attempts with the boys, I would not be doing such words justice.” </p>
<p>“You think you understand our words better than I? You, the son of a wh—”</p>
<p>A quiet voice—not to be mistaken for a soft one—interrupted. “Your pardon.” </p>
<p>They both turned to the doorway, where Lan Wangji stood with the boys. A-Yuan and Jingyi were practically vibrating with excitement, wide-eyed and ready to jump to Meng Yao’s side. Meng Yao smiled softly in their direction, even as Nie Liu stiffened beside him. </p>
<p>“Good morning, young masters. Are we ready to continue our lessons?” Meng Yao asked.</p>
<p>It seemed all the permission they needed. A-Yuan, in a very familiar maneuver he’d never executed with Meng Yao as a target, leapt forward and wrapped himself around Meng Yao’s leg, pushing his face into Meng Yao’s thigh. Jingyi seemed more interested in attempting to jump high enough to meet Meng Yao’s gaze at eye level. Nie Liu appeared deeply unimpressed. </p>
<p>“May I speak with you, Nie Liu?” Lan Wangji asked, his voice ice-covered steel. Meng Yao was surprised to realize he’d learned the limited facial tells of the other man well enough to recognize that he was furious. How delightful.  </p>
<p>Nie Liu shifted uncomfortably, but nodded and followed him from the room. </p>
<p>“Both of you take your seats now,” Meng Yao told them, gently easing A-Yuan away from his leg so he could take his spot. As he did, he brushed the top of the boy’s head with his knuckles and earned an expansive smile. </p>
<p>Little over an hour later, A-Yuan sneezed, and once more there was a petite dragon hovering in the air before him. He seemed incapable of controlling how his body moved in the air. Jingyi jumped to his feet to try and tackle him again, but froze in place when Meng Yao turned a stern glance his way. He settled down with limited grumbling. </p>
<p>“A-Yuan,” Meng Yao said. The dragon twisted around to meet his eyes. “You can understand me when I speak to you in this manner, correct?” A-Yuan very deliberately nodded his head. “Excellent, then we shall wait until you are back to your human body before continuing with calligraphy, and instead turn to philosophy for the time being. I shall try to pose my questions to you in ‘yes’ or ‘no’ to allow you to participate.” </p>
<p>A-Yuan moved forward and slid over and around Meng Yao, sending full-body shivers running through Meng Yao’s veins. </p>
<p>“No fair he gets to hug you,” Jingyi grumbled. </p>
<p>“Let us talk of fairness for today’s lesson, then.” </p>
<p>Unappeased, Jingyi cast another somewhat irritated look towards A-Yuan before settling in for his own learning. </p>
<p>A-Yuan was back to human in time for their music lessons. Instead of a guqin, Jingyi had apparently decided to try his hand at drumming, which Meng Yao suspected to be both Wei Wuxian’s suggestion and an effort to conciliate some of his more exuberant tendencies. Despite the disparity of styles, he had little doubt Lan Wangji was up to the task of teaching both at once. </p>
<p>“Nie Liu will no longer be responsible for the teaching of children in the Unclean Realm,” Lan Wangji told him, settling behind his own guqin and pulling up his sleeves. </p>
<p>“Unnecessary,” Meng Yao said through the swell of his heart. Lan Wangji graced him with a sceptical eye. “But thank you.”</p>
<p>Lan Wangji nodded and turned his attention to the boys. </p>
<p>Meng Yao stood outside the door exactly long enough to hear Jingyi’s first attempts at rhythm before deciding to retreat. </p>
<p>He paused at the turn of the hallway which would take him to Lan Xichen’s room. Would he be waiting? </p>
<p>Uncertainty proved too tiresome for Meng Yao to deal with. Shoulders back, head up, he made his way to Lan Xichen’s receiving room. </p>
<p>After Nie Huaisang had left the night before, and indeed during much of his convalescence, he’d given thought to what to say to the Two Lords. Words tripped over one another as he’d ordered and reordered them to find a way to express himself. </p>
<p>Meng Yao had never been ‘good.’ Conducting oneself honourably had its benefits only in that it made one more palatable to society at large, and he’d long come to terms with the knowledge that there were few things he would not do to advance his place in life enough to avenge the death of his mother. The Unclean Realm hadn’t instilled any values in him, but he found himself wanting to remain. And perhaps behaving with goodness was an acceptable substitute when one could not be inherently good.</p>
<p><em>What is fair?</em> he had asked Jingyi and A-Yuan. In all fairness, Lan Xichen and Nie Mingjue should have cast him out, or left him to die on the mountain. He didn’t want to consider himself in their debt, but he felt he owed it to them to be, if not the ideal to which they all aspired, close enough to be acceptable. </p>
<p>Lan Xichen looked up at his arrival, and stood with a glowing smile stretched wide across his face. “A-Yao.”</p>
<p>“I would like to continue my lessons,” Meng Yao said. He started to bow, only for his elbows to be caught in Lan Xichen’s gentle hands. </p>
<p>“Please don’t. Please.” </p>
<p>Meng Yao straightened. “I feel I should speak with you and Nie Mingjue.”</p>
<p>“I’ll summon him. In the meantime, may I play for you? You still look quite pale.” </p>
<p>Nie Mingjue joined them only a few minutes later, and Meng Yao did not want to accuse him of hovering, but he did wonder where he must have been to have been retrieved so quickly. He settled in next to Meng Yao to listen to the remainder of Lan Xichen’s playing. Meng Yao did feel better afterwards, which bolstered his confidence enough to speak his mind. </p>
<p>“Undoubtedly Zixuan has told you everything said between us,” he began. Lan Xichen and Nie Mingjue did him the service of listening without interruption. “I understand now you welcomed me here not under false pretenses, as I had feared, but with full understanding as to what my purpose in coming was. I would like to confirm, here and now, that I have no plans to betray this  House in any capacity. You have given me—” Kindness, respect, a home, friends, family, “—more than was due to me considering the intentions I brought with me into the Unclean Realm. I wish to thank you for that.” He bowed low enough his forehead touched the floor, and while he heard Lan Xichen shift to stop him, he also trusted Nie Mingjue to understand why he could not. </p>
<p>He took his time rising. “I also understand Zixuan’s plan to...rehabilitate me may not be tenable with consideration to these prestenses and intentions. I understand that, as the Two Lords of Jade and Blades, you have made many difficult decisions. Should one of those decisions run counter to Zixuan’s plans, please believe my sincerity when I say I understand completely.” He couldn’t look at them, and chose to keep his eyes on the ground. </p>
<p>“And if we are in support of Zixuan’s plan?” Lan Xichen asked. </p>
<p>“I shall try to be worthy of it.” He paused. “Mostly. I am beginning to appreciate the value of speaking my mind.” </p>
<p>Nie Mingjue shifted in place. “I would rather you did, Meng Yao. I’ve never had patience for false faces.”</p>
<p>Meng Yao’s lips twitched, but he did not smile. “You must be mightily tired of me, then.”</p>
<p>“I think knowing to look for the mask stopped it from being the disguise you believed it to be,” Lan Xichen offered. Nie Mingjue nodded. “We will accept your service, Meng Yao. And, in time, should you wish to join us, we will accept you into the House.” The finality of the words sent a shiver down Meng Yao’s back. </p>
<p>“Thank you.” </p>
<p>Lan Xichen gestured to the waiting guqins. “Shall we?”</p><hr/>
<p>Bundled in their warmest clothing, they gathered to say goodbye to Wen Qing the next morning, Nie Mingjue conspicuous in his absence. Meng Yao gathered, from snippets of conversation he’d picked up while in the infirmary, bad blood existed between them though he had not discovered why. </p>
<p>“Thank you for your expertise, Lady Wen,” he said with a bow. </p>
<p>“You have proven one of my less challenging patients,” she told him. To his left, Jiang Wanyin huffed in annoyance and she turned to him. “Yes? Jiang Cheng? You wish to refute that? Certainly not with your own experiences under my needles.”</p>
<p>“I would think a doctor would be hard-pressed to rank her patients.”</p>
<p>“I found it very easy. You were the worst by far.” </p>
<p>They glared at each other, until Jiang Wanyin finally broke and managed a surprisingly soft smile. “Safe flight.” </p>
<p>Her eyes warmed. “Goodbye.” </p>
<p>She shifted into a beautiful gold-scaled dragon, close in appearance to A-Yuan with her brilliant feathered wings. Almost in sympathy the boy snapped into his dragon form as well, and Wei Wuxian had to grab a hold of him to stop him from floating up after her as she lifted into the sky and took wing. Jiang Wanyin watched her with longing eyes, confirming yet again to be the most unfortunately expressive man Meng Yao ever met. No wonder he shouted; anger had to be the only way he could convincingly hide whatever else he felt. </p>
<p>“You should probably just marry her,” Wei Wuxian said once she’d crossed over the nearby peak. </p>
<p>“You should probably just shut your fucking mouth,” Jiang Wanyin growled in return. </p>
<p>“A-Cheng, I have been happily married for longer than you’ve been alive—”</p>
<p>“Wei Wuxian, I swear—”</p>
<p>“—And I have a world of experience in convincing someone objectively better than you to take you on.” </p>
<p>Lan Wangji looked like he wanted to argue, but demurred when A-Yuan and Jingyi took off to play in the untouched snow around the landing. </p>
<p>At least Jiang Cheng looked thoughtful. Ah, brotherhood. </p>
<p>It wasn’t a teaching day for the boys, and Nie Mingjue had already sequestered himself with his administrative tasks, leaving Meng Yao somewhat at odds. </p>
<p>Momentarily, at least. The moment he started to start back, Wei Wuxian’s attention snapped to him and he left Jiang Cheng to muddle over whatever dubious advice he’d provided.</p>
<p>“Come along, then, Yao-ge,” Wei Wuxian said, slipping his arm through Meng Yao’s. He frowned sidelong. “Qing-jie gave us strict instructions for making sure you recover as quickly as possible, and that includes getting you to the training fields to help build up some more muscle.”</p>
<p>Meng Yao blinked. “...training fields. Wei Wuxian, the training fields are currently buried under five feet of snow.” </p>
<p>“They <em>were</em> buried under five feet of snow. You’re welcome.” </p>
<p>Once they reached the field, Meng Yao half-shaking with trepidation, Wei Wuxian took his measure. Literally. He made Meng Yao stretch out his arms and looked them over before darting into a nearby armoury and producing a serviceable practice sword.</p>
<p>"Have you used a blade before?" he asked.</p>
<p>Meng Yao pursed his lips. "A dagger only.” He slipped the concealed blade from his sleeve to a nod of approval. “Never a sword. My mother bought books on cultivation, and I used to practice the footwork exercises, but she always said my… said Jin Guangshan would provide a real sword for me when he legitimized me."</p>
<p>Wei Wuxian did him the honour of not offering up pity or soft words. "Those books are garbage. I once caught one of the authors peeking over the walls of Lotus Pier to get ideas for his 'manual.' I wouldn't be surprised if all of them came about the same way. Not a single one written by someone who held a sword." He grinned. "Fortunately for you, you have an embarrassment of choice for which form would suit you best."</p>
<p>"I am confident embarrassment will be playing a part in this."</p>
<p>Wei Wuxian laughed and then kicked at his feet until he repositioned them in a satisfactory manner.</p>
<p>Meng Yao wasn't all that confident, an hour later, that Wen Qing had deliberately prescribed a course of treatment that involved him sweating so profusely his robes half-froze to his body, but he had to admit it felt satisfying. Even without a spiritual weapon, the movements through which Wei Wuxian had guided him thrummed in his veins; his poorly-developed golden core sang to him in songs he'd never heard before, and he did feel better.</p>
<p>The bone-deep aches crept up on Meng Yao steadily over the rest of the day, and he barely managed to get himself back to his room after dinner. He believed Wei Wuxian’s insistence that the exercise had been at Wen Qing’s command, but surely he was meant to take a more measured approach?</p>
<p>“A-Yao.” He turned and nodded in greeting to Zixuan as his brother approached. “I have this for you.” He withdrew a small pot from his sleeve. “It should help with the muscle pain. Wuxian is an excellent teacher, and demands excellence in his students.” </p>
<p>Meng Yao noted the surprising lack of reluctance in the assessment, and accepted the pot with a small nod. “Thank you. I’m surprised to hear you speak so well of him. I thought you two often found yourselves at odds.” </p>
<p>“We do.” Zixuan opened his door and waved to invite Meng Yao inside. He entered the room with some small reluctance; it was the first time he’d seen the inside of his brother’s accommodations after all. The room looked well-appointed and lavishly decorated as befitted a man of his stature. Tucked in among the golden decor and comfortable furniture were touches of lotuses and purple fabrics, which Meng Yao regarded with quiet amusement. </p>
<p>They sat for tea, which Zixuan poured for them both. </p>
<p>“Wuxian has ideas about what is best for A-Li. And while I can appreciate the desire to protect her, he often overlooks the fact that she is perfectly capable.” Zixuan’s face twisted. “I have been guilty of overlooking these capabilities in the past, and he and Jiang Cheng were both reluctant to forgive my offenses. Are still, to a certain extent. Part of the reason I’m spending a year here is to prove I can manage more than five minutes in her presence without offending her, a feat I was incapable of accomplishing when we first met.” </p>
<p>“It must have made that month you spent together difficult,” Meng Yao commented. </p>
<p>“You have no idea,” Zixuan admitted with an uncharacteristically open scoff. “Despite this, though, I hope I am able to acknowledge his strengths. He very admirably managed to keep up with Jiang Cheng when they were children, despite Jiang Cheng’s natural advantages.” </p>
<p>“Another dragon,” Meng Yao said. </p>
<p>“Sandu Shenghou,” Zixuan told him. “Though more than that I cannot tell you without his blessing.” </p>
<p>“Why did it fall to Wei Wuxian to assist me?” Had Zixuan not wanted to? </p>
<p>Zixuan’s brow acquired the small line between his eyes that only ever appeared when he was annoyed. “It was determined I would be too gentle with you.” </p>
<p>Meng Yao smiled into his tea.</p><hr/>
<p>Winter clung to the walls of the Unclean Realm with vicious pleasure, hanging on with a seemingly unbreakable grip. </p>
<p>“Much longer and the farmers will be unable to get their spring planting in,” Meng Yao muttered to himself one morning, reviewing reports from the territory. </p>
<p>Lan Xichen and Nie Mingjue exchanged measured looks. “One more week,” Lan Xichen finally nodded. </p>
<p>“Until what?” Meng Yao asked.</p>
<p>“Until we intervene.” </p>
<p>The snow persisted, though the sun made regular appearances throughout the day. Meng Yao had mostly forgotten Lan Xichen’s words until he was roused from bed late one evening by Zixuan, who respected him enough, at least, to knock on his door to get him out of bed. They slid along the impacted ice leading to the landing, where Meng Yao found every adult dragon in the Unclean Realm awaiting them. Wei Wuxian turned and regarded them both with a smile as they fell into line beside him. </p>
<p>He was of course familiar with Zewu-jun, Chifeng-zun and Hanguang-jun, but this was his first opportunity to look his fill at the Jiang siblings. In the darkness, their scales were indiscernible from the velvety blue of a moonlit sky, and he could only imagine what they would look like in the sun. </p>
<p>“We thought you might want to be here,” Zixuan said, gripping Meng Yao’s shoulder and watching with wonder as the five dragons rose into the air together. They seemed to float upwards into the sky above, disappearing through the heavy cloud covering together. </p>
<p>“What are they going to do?” Meng Yao asked. </p>
<p>The distant rumble of thunder caught his attention, and only a few minutes later the first drop of rain splashed against his forehead. </p>
<p>“It takes a toll on them,” Wei Wuxian stated. “They’ll sleep all day tomorrow.” </p>
<p>The rain came quicker, light droplets that seemed to caress his cheeks before sluicing down to gather at the neck of his robes. It would melt the remaining snow, he realized. And hopefully start to thaw the ground. </p>
<p>True to Wei Wuxian’s words, not a single one of them was available the following day. Meng Yao took over for Nie Mingjue in an endless series of meetings with a small cadre of petitioners looking for aid; they’d all braved the torrential rain outside, and it was the least he could do to make sure their concerns were heard. Wei Wuxian released him from his relentless exercise regime, and even corralled the boys into something resembling a respectable day, though more than once Meng Yao found himself pausing in his speech to wait for the sounds of childish delight to quiet enough for his words to be heard. </p>
<p>“You must understand what you’re asking for is quite impossible,” he continued once the screaming had abated. </p>
<p>The merchant in front of him scowled. “Why?”</p>
<p>“I have already explained the reasoning,” Meng Yao replied evenly. “We have a mutual and exclusive agreement with one of your competitors which we are not at the liberty or, honestly, the inclination to break at this time.” </p>
<p>“I’m confident upon hearing the value I can bring, the Two Lords—”</p>
<p>“You will find the Two Lords trust my judgement, sir. You’re welcome to remain in the Unclean Realm until you’ve decided on your next destination, but I’m afraid your proposal is declined.” Meng Yao handed the sheaf of papers to the attendant standing at his left, who returned them to the merchant with a shallow bow. </p>
<p>The merchant’s mouth twitched into a dissatisfied moue, but stood and bowed. “Thank you for your time, Young Master.” </p>
<p>He turned, prepared to leave, when Meng Yao coughed to catch his attention. “If you are looking to broaden your trade, you might try the Han. The distance between their territory and this one is comparable, and you may find they have no similar trading agreements in place.” </p>
<p>The merchant blinked and bowed again, deeper. “Thank you sir.” </p>
<p>Once he was gone, Meng Yao looked to the attendant. “Any other appointments for the day?” </p>
<p>“No sir.”</p>
<p>“Thank you. Please see tea is sent to the Two Lords, Sect Leader Jiang and Lady Jiang, as well as a meal if they desire. I’m not confident they’ve been well enough to request anything for themselves. Once that’s completed you may retire for the evening.”</p>
<p>The man bowed and whisked himself out. Meng Yao, smiling with no small amount of satisfaction, rose to go in search of Wei Wuxian and his charges. </p>
<p>He found them near the stables, ignoring the harried looks of the stablehands and plying Wei Wuxian’s donkey with a shocking number of preserved apples. </p>
<p>“Keep it up and that donkey will be so fat you won’t be able to sit astride it,” he commented mildly. </p>
<p>“Teacher!” The boys chorusing was… gratifying and Meng Yao rewarded both of them with a smile. </p>
<p>“She’ll be fine!” Wei Wuxian protested, offering up the last sliver, which the donkey accepted with little grace. “She’s seen me through since the war.” He attempted to pet the donkey’s nose, to which the animal responded with a grunt and turned away, now apples were no longer luring him to the end of his stall. </p>
<p>“Perhaps now you can tell me why you choose to ride a donkey at all.”</p>
<p>“Once you’ve been a dragon’s rider, you can’t ever ride a horse again.” Wei Wuxian shrugged. “Dragons don’t like it.”</p>
<p>“Dragons… don’t like it? Horses?” Surely that wasn’t right. </p>
<p>“At all. It's a thing. As well as my mistress Lil Apple treats her unworthy rider, I would much rather be on horseback. But every horse I've ridden since the war has mysteriously vanished from the stables. And I <em>know</em> Hanguang-jun isn’t eating them, is the thing. They're just. Gone. Could be an entire herd of wild horses running amok in Qinghe somewhere right now and we'd never know.” Perhaps noting the way Meng Yao’s face twisted in response, Wei Wuxian frowned. “All right?” </p>
<p>“I had no idea dragons could be ridiculous. It’s a rather stunning realization.” </p>
<p>Wei Wuxian grinned and herded them all out to the evening meal. It was certainly quieter, with only the four of them and Zixuan in attendance. Meng Yao rather thought Wei Wuxian missed his usual sparring partner in Jiang Wanyin, not to mention the subtle affections of his spouse. </p>
<p>After dinner, Meng Yao paused before heading to his room, and instead made his way to the quarters shared by Lan Xichen and Nie Mingjue. If they were asleep, he vowed, he would leave them be. If they answered his gentle knock…</p>
<p>“Come in.” </p>
<p>He let himself inside. Both the Two Lords were awake, though dressed only in simple under robes. They looked exhausted, despite the day of rest. He was gratified to see, however, his instructions had been carried out and there were empty dishes next to the door awaiting collection. </p>
<p>“I thought I would see how you both fared,” he offered. “And perhaps you’d allow me to practice my middling guqin skills by playing for you.” </p>
<p>Lan Xichen smiled wanly. “You’ve gotten quite good, Meng Yao.”</p>
<p>“As you well know,” Nie Mingjue harrumphed. </p>
<p>“Any progress I’ve made has been because of your instruction,” Meng Yao said. Then, daringly, “Er-ge.” Lan Xichen looked pleased, and Meng Yao decided to forgive himself the presumption.</p>
<p>He took a seat at Lan Xichen’s guqin and set to playing. It lacked the spiritual power a performance by Lan Xichen himself might have produced, but he felt it a serviceable attempt. Nie Mingjue half passed out before the first movement was done, and Lan Xichen treated Meng Yao to a peek at their easy affection as he smiled adoringly at his spouse. </p>
<p>Meng Yao ached for it, though he couldn’t say if it was for Lan Xichen, Nie Mingjue, or the look in and of itself.</p><hr/>
<p>“You’re overextending,” Zixuan told him, watching from the side of the field as Meng Yao moved through the training exercise Wei Wuxian had left him with. </p>
<p>Meng Yao gritted his teeth and adjusted his stance. The sword still did not feel entirely natural in his hand, not the extension of his body suggested by Wei Wuxian, but he did feel as though he’d made progress. </p>
<p>“It’s not a problem during training, but it could result in someone getting up under your guard if you’re in a real battle.” </p>
<p>“No offense, da-ge, but if I’m ever in a real battle then I doubt my skills with a sword will be my saving grace,” Meng Yao pointed out. </p>
<p>“Don’t underestimate yourself.” Zixuan’s mouth twisted up unhappily. “You’ve come a long way since starting with Wuxian.” </p>
<p>Meng Yao eased out of the stance and bowed. “Thank you. But should I ever need to dispatch an enemy, I think I shall have to rely on treachery.” </p>
<p><em>Here are the places to strike, my love, if you need to cripple a man. And here to avoid the breastbone to drive a blade through their heart.</em> </p>
<p>Zixuan moved to join him, pulling Suihua from its scabbard. He took a place beside Meng Yao and slowly went through the same movements. It felt distinctly odd to see him working within the freedoms of the Jiang style, but he seemed unaffected by the vast differences. Meng Yao lined himself up alongside his brother and attempted the same easy grace. </p>
<p>Once Zixuan was satisfied, they faced each other to allow Meng Yao to mirror the movements. Zixuan was a competent teacher. More than once, when seeking him out in Koi Tower, Meng Yao had found him working with the Jin disciples, taking them through their paces with the senior disciple standing by to watch. Meng Yao suspected his brother preferred such activities to the actual governance necessities of leadership. </p>
<p>Perhaps he’d overestimated his familiarity with the Jiang style, however. When they returned to their starting position, Zixuan’s hand moved at the exact wrong angle and strayed into the path of Meng Yao’s blade. He jerked backwards with a small grimace of pain, quickly banished, though a small splatter of blood trickled down his robes. </p>
<p>He waved off Meng Yao’s apologies as his own fault, and was halfway through correcting himself by going through the motion when Yanli-jie burst onto the training fields. </p>
<p>“A-Xuan!” she called, eyes somewhat wild. She calmed at the sight of them, though there was still a quickness of step Meng Yao hadn’t seen from her before. “I…” She looked back and forth between them, at a loss.</p>
<p>“It was an accident, A-Li,” Zixuan assured her. He held up his hand, and she moved to inspect it. </p>
<p>“I. Oh. Just… the blood.” Her lips pursed unhappily. “I worried.” </p>
<p>Meng Yao regarded them blankly until Zixuan motioned to the white jade charm hanging from his waist. Meng Yao noted the blood marring the otherwise pristine carving, caught during the dribble down the length of his robes. </p>
<p>“If you would like to examine his wound, I would be happy to chaperone,” Meng Yao offered in lieu of another apology. They both turned fond eyes on him. “I understand these things are occasionally best viewed under open skies, and the walking paths to the west have been cleared.” </p>
<p>Yanli-jie patted the side of Meng Yao’s head, in a way very similar to that which she’d offered Jiang Wanyin and Wei Wuxian when they’d done something particularly endearing (to her). </p>
<p>“Thank you, A-Yao,” she said. </p>
<p>Zixuan tucked his sword away and offered her his arm.</p><hr/>
<p>Zixuan’s year in the Unclean Realm was almost up and, by all appearances, he would press his suit with Yanli-jie and officially join them. Xichen couldn’t pretend it wasn’t a relief, though an ugly part of him still hesitated to call Jin Guangshan kin. He saw the same reluctance reflected in Mingjue’s eyes as well, and the same guilt over the reservations. After all, keeping Zixuan also meant keeping A-Yao and despite the ugliness of their father, he and Mingjue did intend to keep A-Yao. </p>
<p>The year would end at sunset, and he’d gathered all the members of the Household of the Two Lords on the steps at the entrance to the Unclean Realm, Meng Yao and Zixuan facing them from the ground below. Someone, likely Yanli-jie, had made sure they were both bedecked in their finest robes. </p>
<p>Family greetings, after all, were much different than those of anyone else who might pass through their doors. </p>
<p>“Young Master Jin, if you are here it means you are a part of our House. It means you are prepared to love and protect the others within these walls, and live your life freely but in service to this commitment. You are free to stay as you will, and may leave at any time, but acknowledge that you will not leave our hearts even in parting. Do you remain in the Unclean Realm with a full understanding of this?” </p>
<p>“I acknowledge this to be true,” Zixuan said with a demure smile. Xichen noted, with a small smile of his own, that his eyes remained fixed on Yanli-jie as he spoke. Once he was finished, he stepped forward and joined them on the stairs.</p>
<p>Meng Yao looked directly at Xichen and Mingjue, unwavering. </p>
<p>“Young Master Meng, if you are here it means you are a part of our House. It means you are prepared to love and protect the others within these walls, and live your life freely but in service to this commitment. You are free to stay as you will, and may leave at any time, but acknowledge that you will not leave our hearts even in parting. Do you remain in the Unclean Realm with a full understanding of this?” Mingjue asked. </p>
<p>“I acknowledge this to be true,” Meng Yao agreed, chin lifted. </p>
<p>“We have something for you as well,” Xichen said. He nodded to Zixuan, who proudly stepped forward, producing a small box from his sleeve. “To recognize that your place is now with us.” </p>
<p>Zixuan opened it to present the white jade sword charm. Meng Yao stared at it as though afraid to accept, his shaking hands reaching out to brush across it. </p>
<p>“I.” He stopped, overcome. “I will try to be worthy of it.” The words echoed those he’d spoken to Xichen and Mingjue when recovering from his illness. He had lived up to them, as Xichen was confident he would also live up to the trust now being presented. “Thank you.” </p>
<p>“We’ve prepared a feast in honour of you both,” Yanli-jie said a moment later. </p>
<p>“And then, tomorrow, we start preparing for the wedding!” Wuxian grinned. </p>
<p>Meng Yao looked relieved as they all began to file back inside, towards the reception hall, likely because none of them mentioned the tears gathered in his eyes.</p><hr/>
<p>Zixuan and Yanli-jie agreed to move forward with things (not that there had been any doubt from any corner, perhaps save the small one inhabited by Wei Wuxian, and only then on a performative basis) the wedding preparations swept across the Unclean Realm. Jiang Wanyin and Wei Wuxian had lofty ideas for their sister’s wedding—emphasized and embellished moreso by Lan Xichen, who took an empathic interest the music—and between the three of them and a seemingly limitless budget, it was turning into a dramatic affair the likes of which probably wouldn’t be seen again for centuries. With so much focus on other aspects of the union the contract had not gone into nearly enough details and the oversight apparently allowed the bride’s family to run absolutely rampant. </p>
<p>Unfortunately, what the whole ridiculous cadre of overenthusiastic idiots enjoyed in ambitions, they lacked in organizational capacity. Except for Nie Huaisang, who shook his head and claimed to know nothing, but wasn't this particular silk merchant known for poor seams, and wouldn't this other one be better suited, not that he professed to be an expert, but perhaps someone should check? All commented upon from behind his fan as his eyes tilted upwards, having driven everyone into a frenzy of trying to verify the claims and make sure that necessary perfections were achieved. Meng Yao wasn’t sure why he even bothered anymore, other than keeping up appearances. </p>
<p>(Nie Mingjue washed his hands of the whole affair, and told everyone he would be busy with Nie Clan matters until the day of the wedding. When pressed as to which Clan matters could be so important, he recalled something very urgent he had to do and showed himself from the room).</p>
<p>Thus, with only the slightest twitch of the eye, Meng Yao put himself forward as the cornerstone for organization and planning. </p>
<p>“I appreciate it,” Nie Mingjue told him one evening, late into the night after Meng Yao harried Wei Wuxian and Jiang Wanyin away from his notes. </p>
<p>“As well you should,” Meng Yao replied. “But one more comment scribbled where it doesn’t belong and we’ll also be planning a funeral. Two funerals,” he corrected himself. “Three if Nie Huaisang says one more fucking thing about silk.” </p>
<p>Nie Mingjue pressed a broad palm to his back. “We all value your assistance, A-Yao.” </p>
<p>“Value it from another room. I have work to do.”</p>
<p>Nie Mingjue left with a chuckle, but a short time later one of the servants brought him a small jar of wine, so Men Yao considered the otherwise inexcusable levity forgiven.</p>
<p>Early the next morning, rousted from what he considered to be a well-earned nap (passed out across his desk amidst his papers, a involuntary reprieve of only a few minutes), Nie Huaisang hastily shoved Meng Yao into respectable robes and dragged to the main gates to stand and greet the new arrival. She arrived with a small cadre of cultivators and two imposing women at her back, both of whom wore identical expressions of diffidence, matched by the cunning neutrality of their mistress.</p>
<p>Yu Ziyuan. The Violet Spider. Regent of Yunmeng. The bride’s mother. </p>
<p>Both Lan Xichen and Nie Mingjue stood to welcome her, the former speaking the traditional words of greeting. He’d gotten to understand the greetings, now. Only dragons and blooded were offered the courtesy and protection the words provided. </p>
<p>“Madam Yu,” the Lord of Jade began, “You come here in celebration of your daughter’s wedding. You are welcome to stay for the entirety of the proceedings and as long as you please afterwards to share your joy in the celebration. You are to be accorded every respect, as we likewise expect you to respect the members of his household.” Now <em>that</em> was interesting. Meng Yao had not heard such an affixation to the greetings beforehand; respect for the House was always an inherent expectation, regardless of who walked through the gates. “Do you enter the Unclean Realm with a full understanding of this?” </p>
<p>“I acknowledge the truth of these words,” she said. While the members of her party all bowed, she remained standing, much like Wei Wuxian had that first day. What did it mean, she did not bow to the Two Lords? Meng Yao hated missing context, he always assumed it meant people knew more than he did and it was something he could not countenance. “A-Cheng, A-Li, come.” </p>
<p>Jiang Cheng and Jiang Yanli broke away from the gathered bodies and went to their mother. She looked them over with a critical eye, slightly narrowed, as her people streamed by her to be shown to the guest houses set aside for the visitors of Yunmeng, quite a bit closer to the family quarters than any other guests could boast. “They are keeping you well?” </p>
<p>“Yes, mother,” Jiang Cheng assured her. </p>
<p>Her chin tilted upwards. “And you are conducting yourselves with respectability and honour due to your hosts?” </p>
<p>“Our brothers, mother. And yes,” Jiang Yanli replied evenly. </p>
<p>“Hm. Brothers. As though they were hatched from my own nest.” She slit a glance towards the rest of the House and snapped out, whip-quick, “Wei Wuxian, is this how you greet me?” </p>
<p>Wei Wuxian broke away and half-stumbled down the stairs, skidding to a stop before her and bowing with far more reverence than even the regent of Yunmeng deserved, especially considering the manner in which he’d greeted his Sect Leader. “Madam Yu.” </p>
<p>“Let me look at you. Still embarrassing us? Your robes are a mess.”</p>
<p>Nie Huaisang leaned over, snapping his fan out to cover his mouth as he whispered to Meng Yao, “Believe it or not, this is worlds better than it used to be.” </p>
<p>“Really?” Meng Yao asked. The words didn’t shake him—he’d lived with similar, if not worse, every day he’d spent in Koi Tower—but he wondered at the fond look in Wei Wuxian’s eyes. </p>
<p>“Mm. After Lan Wangji blooded him and he technically belonged to the Gusu flight, it forgave some of his sins.” </p>
<p>“Where is your son?” Madam Yu continued. </p>
<p>“In lessons, Madam Yu,” Wei Wuxian reported truthfully. Others had taken on the boys’ education while Meng Yao lost himself in wedding planning. He had vetted the potential educators very carefully to ensure they could be trusted with such an important task. “He’ll see you at the ceremony tonight.” </p>
<p>Meng Yao blinked and looked at Nie Huaisang. “Ceremony?” </p>
<p>“Jin Zixuan’s blooding,” Nie Huaisang replied. “You were doing so much work with the human part, we didn’t want to tax you with the dragon half.” </p>
<p>Lan Wangji descended the stairs at a much slower pace and came to stand beside Wei Wuxian to offer his own greetings. Madam Yu greeted him with far more civility, though a cutting remark about his failure to make Wei Wuxian respectable snuck in regardless. He took it with far more grace than Meng Yao had expected, considering the subject matter. </p>
<p>“What’s involved in the blooding?” Meng Yao asked. It felt safer than unpacking the questionable dynamic of Madam Yu and her children. </p>
<p>“You’ll see tonight.” </p>
<p>Meng Yao blinked. “I’ll what?” </p>
<p>Once the sun had well and truly set that evening, Lan Xichen showed up at his door with a surprisingly plain black robe and waited for him to arrange it before leading him through the Unclean Realm to the landing. He stumbled, slightly, at the sight of all of the dragons of the House, Wen Qing, and a dragon he did not recognize, stood alongside one another, save Yanli who waited apart from the rest. Lan Xichen motioned him towards Nie Huaisang, Wei Wuxian, Jingyi, who spotted him and waved. Meng Yao gratefully slid in beside him and Wei Wuxian. </p>
<p>“I don’t understand why I’m here, Wuxian,” he admitted out of the side of his mouth. </p>
<p>“You’re the groom’s brother,” Wei Wuxian reminded him. </p>
<p>“I am honoured.”</p>
<p>“Make sure to tell him that,” Wei Wuxian said. He tilted his eyebrows and Meng Yao followed his gaze to where Zixuan had appeared on the path. He walked with dignity towards Jiang Yanli, though even in the dark Meng Yao could tell his neck was bright red. As he approached Jiang Yanli, she shifted back to her human form and smiled with quiet serenity. </p>
<p>“A-Xuan,” she said. “Thank you.” </p>
<p>He bowed low before her. “I am, and always will be, unworthy of you.”</p>
<p>“We finally agree on something,” Wei Wuxian muttered. Meng Yao elbowed him sharply in the side and he quieted. </p>
<p>Was his brother to drink a cup of blood? Meng Yao couldn’t guess how it worked, and waited in bated breath as the other dragons began to circle them. They curled around the two, hiding them completely from view by moving in concentric circles, Chifeng-zun on the outside as the largest among them. They spun faster with every turn, and Meng Yao gasped as thunder rumbled above them, turning his gaze to the sky at the massive stormhead rolling in through the mountains to obscure the moon and stars. </p>
<p>"Is it always this wonderful?" Meng Yao breathed.</p>
<p>Wei Wuxian didn't immediately answer, and when he looked over, the other man's eyes were clouded over with old pain, aging him far beyond his years. "No. Sometimes, on the battlefield, there's no time for ceremony if you want to save the life of the person you love." </p>
<p>Before he could offer a reply, Jingyi tugged on Meng Yao’s robes and he bent over. “What happens if A-Yuan can’t hold his form?” he asked. </p>
<p>“No one would ever let him come to harm, I promise you,” Meng Yao said. If he knew nothing else about this affair, he knew that with the utmost certainty.</p>
<p>Jingyi nodded, but grabbed Meng Yao’s hand and held on tightly as the odd dance before them continued. </p>
<p>Finally, with a crack of lightning threatening to tear the sky itself apart, everything seemed to freeze. The sky opened up and a torrent of rain broke upon them. Jingyi screamed in delighted surprise and Meng Yao had to shut his eyes against the sudden torrent, though he couldn’t help the smile crawling across his face. </p>
<p>Huaisang nodded. “The sky and storms bless them.” </p>
<p>“The sky and storms bless them,” Wei Wuxian echoed with enthusiasm, his voice only slightly choked. He laughed and pushed a handful of wet hair back out of his face. </p>
<p>“Should we go inside?” Meng Yao asked. </p>
<p>“Not yet,” Wei Wuxian replied, his voice at a yell to be heard over the pounding of the rain. Another rumble of thunder, though not nearly as violent, shook through the air as though the sky itself woke from slumber with a violent yawn. His new robe clung to Meng Yao, but he didn’t feel dragged down. Quite the opposite: more than anything, the fresh scent of the rain buoyed him in ways he’d never felt before. </p>
<p>The dragons slowly peeled off and away from the couple, leaving space enough for a small bundle of humans to approach. </p>
<p>“Come on!” Wei Wuxian grabbed Meng Yao’s hand and hauled him along, barely giving him time to pause to collect Jingyi before they were charging forward. True to Jingyi’s fear, A-Yuan was back to his human form, but clutching tightly enough to Jiang Yanli’s legs that he must have been well out of the way of the others. Wei Wuxian scooped him up as soon as they came within arm’s reach. </p>
<p>“Congratulations, shijie,” he said, hugging her tight. She was laughing and crying, and Meng Yao saw the same emotions dancing across Zixuan’s face. </p>
<p>He grabbed his brother’s arm. “Congratulations.” He wasn’t sure exactly what he was congratulating, but Meng Yao thought he could see the smallest trail of blood dotting the corner of Zixuan’s mouth, though much watered down from the rain.</p>
<p>“I’m glad you were here, A-Yao,” Zixuan told him with all appearances of honesty.  </p>
<p>“Time for your first flight, then,” Wei Wuxian said. “If Meng Yao doesn’t mind putting the boys to bed.” </p>
<p>“It would be my pleasure,” Meng Yao replied honestly. </p>
<p>Jiang Yanli shifted again—the air crackling with the changes, as well as the hair-raising feeling of the lightning overhead—and with minimal awkward scrambling on Zixuan's part, he managed to get himself onto their back before they took wing.</p>
<p>Hanguang-jun approached and lowered himself to allow Wei Wuxian to step onto his front leg and wrap an elbow around the greatest of his  horns. They lifted into the sky, followed by many of the others. An elegant dragon resplendent with indigo scales he suspected to be Madam Yu, if only by process of elimination, rose fast on Sandu Shengshou’s tail.</p>
<p>Before he joined them, Zewu-jun shifted back and came to Meng Yao’s side. “I’m sorry you can’t join us tonight, A-Yao.” </p>
<p>“Don’t be. I’m just happy to have been a part of this.” He blinked in shock, realizing the words to be sincere. </p>
<p>Lan Xichen seemed to understand as well. “We’ll see you in the morning.”</p>
<p>“Fly safe,” he replied. </p>
<p>Zewu-jun soon rose with the others, leaving only Meng Yao, Nie Huaisang, and the boys on the ground. A-Yuan looked after the others with longing, but submitted to Nie Huaisang scooping him up into his arms. </p>
<p>“Let’s get you both into some warm clothes, and maybe we can find something sweet from the kitchens if you promise not to tell your parents,” Meng Yao offered. </p>
<p>Slightly cheered, A-Yuan tucked his face into Nie Huaisang’s neck and they headed back to their rooms. </p>
<p>Later, once the boys were tucked into bed and curled around one another like cats, Nie Huaisang opened a jar of exceptionally good wine and poured them both a cup.</p>
<p>"I understand why I'm not up there," Meng Yao said. For all he understood himself to now be part of the House, there was a certain unspoken intimacy in riding a dragon, and the only dragons he could even speculate sharing such a thing with were already married to each other. "But why didn't you go along?"</p>
<p>Nie Huaisang snapped his fan open and adopted an officious air. "There is protocol and tradition to follow when it comes to dragons. A dragon, should they ever agree to take a rider, will only ever take one in their lifetime. And while I could have gone, being carried in their claws is, I can tell you right now, terribly uncomfortable."</p>
<p>"And heavens forbid you experience any discomfort," Meng Yao said, dry as dust.</p>
<p>Nie Huaisang refilled his cup, and offered a smug smile.</p><hr/>
<p>The sect delegations began to arrive two days later. Meng Yao's arrangement of the guest housing was a work of art, truly something to be proud of, and his seating plan for after the ceremony should have been held up as an example of political grandmastery.</p>
<p>Or it would have, if Nie Huaisang had not been sent by all the hells to torment him.</p>
<p>"Where, exactly, will you be sitting Yao-ge? Because it seems you've forgotten to assign yourself a seat."</p>
<p>Meng Yao blinked. "Ah. Huaisang, I—"</p>
<p>"I know it cannot <em>possibly</em> be that you're planning on missing your brother's wedding. Even if you're not included in the tea pouring—which everyone thinks is ridiculous, but is willing to overlook given that Jin Guangshan <em>must</em> be included—you cannot expect they'll let it slide for you to bow out of the rest."</p>
<p>"A-Sang," The House, to a one, could be directed by open shows of affection. It was how he has stopped Wei Wuxian and Jiang Wanyin from being assholes about the flower situation, "I have attended the ceremony that matters. I would be of much better use behind the scenes assisting the servants."</p>
<p>Nie Huaisang snapped his fan shut with far too much flare. "Are you suggesting the servants of the Unclean Realm are incapable?"</p>
<p>Meng Yao gritted his teeth. "No."</p>
<p>"Have you provided them with clear directions which are easily followed?"</p>
<p>"I know what you're doing," Meng Yao hissed.</p>
<p>"I am trying to make sure that the groom's brother, who he loves very much, is present to celebrate his marriage to his bride, who would be shockingly disappointed if that same brother did not attend." Nie Huaisang glared with such ferocity it suddenly reminded Meng Yao of the often overlooked fact that despite their differences, he and Nie Mingjue were indeed brothers. "If you think that Wei Wuxian and Jiang Cheng will suffer Yanli-jie being at all disappointed on her wedding day with anything resembling grace, you haven't been paying attention. I am preventing another war, Yao-ge. This is in service to my country, Yunmeng, and all the casualties that would surely result. Now, <em>where will you be sitting</em>?"</p>
<p>Meng Yao scowled at the seating plan. </p>
<p>At least it presented an interesting mental exercise, not unlike a game of weiqi with an accomplished opponent. He could not sit with the Jin; Jin Guangshan would never stand for it, and he'd prefer to be as far away from his father, Madam Jin, and Jin Zixun as possible.</p>
<p>The Lan might have been an option, but they would already be subject to scrutiny with the presence of Wei Wuxian within their ranks. For all he and Lan Wangji were married, Wei Wuxian still primarily honoured Jiang customs, and having a second outsider among them instead of the Lan senior disciples would make them look weak.</p>
<p>Sitting with the Nie could be a viable option, especially with the limited family numbers, but that would put him close to the Jin. As hosts, they were seated closest to the families of the bride and groom.</p>
<p>He set himself to pondering, and Nie Huaisang allowed him to stew over the question in silence for a single, precious minute before deciding to offer his own commentary.</p>
<p>"With Da-ge at the front of the hall, I of course have no one sitting beside me."</p>
<p>"If you want to avoid starting a war, you absolutely cannot insist Jin Guangshan's bastard son be seated beside you. It would be seen as a slap in the face of every respectable Clan member. And it would stain your own reputation."</p>
<p>"My reputation takes care of itself quite nicely. I'll just shake my head and tell everyone that I don't understand why a valued member of our House can't sit next to me."</p>
<p>"There are limits to what people will fall for, Huaisang. Pick your battles. Besides, as Senior Disciple, Nie Zonghui has more than earned the spot."</p>
<p>Nie Huaisang tapped his chin with the tip of his fan. "Behind me on the right, then. It will put you two seats over from Jin Zixun—far enough to keep him from speaking to you, unless he wants to shout—and close enough to make a statement. Nie Xiu has been angling for a way out of attending anyway."</p>
<p>Meng Yao frowned. "She's Second Disciple. She's earned the seat."</p>
<p>"I think she's more interested in attending the private party the rest of our cultivators are arranging. Apparently they will have better alcohol."</p>
<p>Alas, it was likely true. Jin Zixuan had been insistent on serving his favourite, a very delicate chrysanthemum wine that would be wasted on almost everyone in attendance as soon as they had more than one cup. Considering it was the only request he'd made the entire time, Meng Yao felt it important to oblige him. He and Wei Wuxian had already made arrangements for a significant quantity of their stores of excellent Zhu liquor to be placed strategically about the room for the more deserving of the guests anyway. He'd have to make sure the servants knew to place one on his table as well.</p>
<p>"Very well." He made the necessary change and Nie Huaisang grinned at a job well done. "But since I have to go and communicate these changes, I'm afraid you'll have to be the one to greet Sect Leader Yao when he arrives."</p>
<p>Nie Huaisang's face twisted in dismay. "No fair, Yao-ge, I've just prevented a war! I should be rewarded for my efforts."</p>
<p>"If you talk very slowly, Sect Leader Ouyang should arrive before you're finished. The two of them are more than capable of entertaining each other." Like gossiping old aunties. "They'll forget you're even there."</p>
<p>Nie Huaisang considered this a moment, then nodded decisively and took off to greet their impending guests.</p><hr/>
<p>The ceremony completed—Mingjue could reluctantly admit it had been lovely despite Wei Wuxian and Jiang Cheng making teary spectacles of themselves—which only left this endless meal and reception to slog through. While ecstatic for Yanli-jie and Zixuan, Mingjue privately vowed never to host such an affair out of the Unclean Realm ever again. Or Qinghe, for that matter. For all things were going smoothly, the number of people present in his home—significantly more than a typical discussion conference, which he could at least justify to himself as being a necessary evil—made him uneasy. Baxia was unsettled. He wanted nothing more than to change and take flight into uncomplicated skies, and thanks to the number of potential witnesses, he couldn't even do something as simple as a late night flight.</p>
<p>The next one of them to be married would have to go to Gusu, he decided. Let Lan Qiren deal with the headache of it all. The recalcitrant old bastard could glower even better than Mingjue himself, and was certainly better at keeping his temper.</p>
<p>(In truth, it was more likely to be out of Yunmeng, but that didn’t bear thinking about). </p>
<p>Thank the heavens Meng Yao secreted some of the good liquor onto his table. People were still filtering in, small bundles of conversation happening across the room as old friends greeted each other, and jars of wine were already being prodigiously refilled by servants who’d somehow managed to pick up Meng Yao’s trick of disappearing while in plain view. Xichen had drifted over to where Lan Wangji took the head seat of the Lan, Lan Qiren still tucked away in Cloud Recesses and wisely avoiding such frivolousness, as was his wont. Considering both Xichen and Wangji were present, as well as their respective spouses, there was no inherent insult in him declining to attend. </p>
<p>Oh, yes, Mingjue thought bitterly as Sect Leader Yao tried to catch his eye. Lan Qiren would definitely be hosting the next wedding. </p>
<p>The representatives of the Nie arrived just late enough to be polite while still drawing attention. Huaisang headed the group of four, alongside Zonghui, who admirably convincingly looked as though he wanted to be here. Meng Yao entered behind them, and Mingjue’s stomach curled in warm triumph at the sight of him in Nie colours. It had been a collective decision for members of the House to avoid their personal heraldry to satisfy both wagging tongues and the egos of their respective birth clans. This affair was already far too political to allow any of them to show off the deep roots of their alliance, but everyone looked very finely attired nonetheless. He found Meng Yao's new hairstyle especially interesting, as he could easily detect A-Sang’s hand in the braids, and he was relatively confident the hairpiece had belonged to A-Sang's mother. It was a statement, but not one anyone outside the Nie, or the House, would or could appreciate.</p>
<p>Meng Yao took the place Huaisang had helpfully picked out for him, and was immediately accosted by Wei Wuxian. Mingjue marked several eyes turning towards them and shoved down raised hackles. Meng Yao looked content enough, and after a full year of wearing him down it wasn’t as though Mingjue couldn’t tell when he was faking it. </p>
<p>Xichen took his hand, decorously hidden by their sleeves. "Our wedding was significantly calmer, wasn't it?"</p>
<p>"It was a political affair in the middle of a war. We couldn't have paused for all… this." Still, he didn't begrudge Yanli-jie, not in the face of her radiant joy.</p>
<p>Xichen's smile was fond and regretful all at once. "Do you wish it had been different? A love match?"</p>
<p>"I am allowed to have you in my arms every night, A-Huan. However you came to be there I am grateful." He boldly lifted Xichen's hand up and pressed his lips to the back of his knuckles. No one was watching them anyway.</p>
<p>Well, almost no one. </p>
<p>Madam Yu pointedly cleared her throat beside them. "Set a good example for my daughter if she's to continue living here," she scolded. </p>
<p>Xichen bowed his head to hide his smile. "Our pardon, Madam Yu."</p>
<p>A raucous laugh caught Mingjue's attention and he glanced at the Jin party. One of the cultivators had spilled wine across his lap, having obviously overindulged as the night went on. With eyes now aimed in his general direction, Jim Guangshan took the opportunity to stand. </p>
<p>And here they'd been having such a nice time.</p>
<p>"Allow me a moment to thank our esteemed hosts. I could not be more honoured to have the Jin united with such a prestigious collection of clans. My son was most wise to forge such an alliance.” </p>
<p>What an exceptional way to ignore the bride all together. From the set of Madam Yu’s mouth, it had not gone unnoticed. </p>
<p>“Through the Jiang’s connection to the Nie and Lan, this brings all four of the major Clans under one roof, and ensures our prosperity for years to come. I know Sect Leader Jiang will agree that this has been to the benefit of everyone.” Of course, before Jiang Cheng could say anything, Jin Guangshan muscled on. “It is my honour, as the father of a single son, to see him well situated and in the position to bring the Jin glory in the future.” </p>
<p>Mingjue cut a look towards Meng Yao, satisfied when he saw the other man was unaffected. Jin Guangshan’s eyes swept across the room, pausing on Meng Yao himself. He seemed momentarily disgruntled, but permitted himself a last boisterous chuckle before sitting back down. </p>
<p>“I am likewise happy for my cousin,” Jin Zixun stated, standing to pick up where his uncle left off. “But this time of separation has been difficult for us. Having been close since boyhood, we have been as brothers. And as the only brother he has, I’m sure he shares my sentiments.” </p>
<p>Xichen pressed his hand firmly against Mingjue’s, as though he couldn’t be trusted to control himself. His temper remained in check; what did it matter if the Jin made a show of dismissing or excluding A-Yao? He belonged to the House now. </p>
<p>“And with this in mind, I will ask to be allowed to trespass on the generosity of our hosts after the wedding to share in his joy and help celebrate properly.” </p>
<p>Meng Yao had failed, and so Jin Zixun was to be the replacement. They could not have been less subtle than if he’d put the words to song and dance. Putting it outwards so publicly obligated them to agree; with such statements of love and friendship, forbidding Jin Zixun from staying would make them look ill-mannered.</p>
<p>A-Sang, looked over his shoulder towards Meng Yao, and the two shared an unreadable look. While Mingjue trusted them to have things in hand, he wasn’t altogether sure how he felt about the two of them plotting.</p>
<p>“Thank you, cousin,” Jin Zixuan said, standing. Yanli-jie, visible only to Mingjue and Xichen from their position behind them, wrapped her hand around his ankle. “And we of course are happy to have you here. But I do need to correct an assertion. I do have a brother, and I am honoured by his presence here tonight, as without him I can safely say that this entire affair would not have been possible.” He lifted his cup. “Meng Yao, my greatest respects to you.” </p>
<p>The House, and most of the guests, lifted their cups to drink. Meng Yao’s faithful mask slipped back into place, cheerfully gracious in acceptance of the words, and barely covering the shock to those who knew him.</p>
<p>Mingjue emptied his cup and leaned over to Xichen to whisper, “Did you know he was going to do this?” </p>
<p>“I did not,” Xichen replied through the smile tilting up the corners of his mouth. “But I am proud of him.” </p>
<p>The Jin were the only ones not to lift their cups, even Sect Leader Yao reluctantly joining in the toast when Sect Leader Ouyang nudged his friend’s side, and Jin Zixun shot Meng Yao a look filled with so much venom Mingjue privately decided to walk Meng Yao back to his room that evening. </p>
<p>The banquet wore on until the early hours of the morning, and Mingjue suspected he saw the beginnings of dawn peeking over the mountaintops by the time they’d seen the last of their guests back to bed. Only him and Meng Yao remained—Xichen having given up later than the usual Lan bedtime, but early enough that Mingjue’s side felt colder in his absence. </p>
<p>“I think I shall sleep through the next wedding,” Meng Yao declared, finishing what little wine remained in his jar. He’d remained remarkably sober; the same couldn’t be said of most of their guests. </p>
<p>“Fortunately there aren’t any more on the horizon.” </p>
<p>Meng Yao smirked. “We shall see.” </p>
<p>Mingjue glowered, though there was little heat in it and the amused curl of his lips probably betrayed his good humour. “What are you plotting?” They made their way from the reception hall, the new shift of servants immediately rushing in to begin clearing away the mess left behind. </p>
<p>“Nothing, Da-ge. But I may have been asked to sit in on a certain conversation with Madam Yu, Jiang Cheng, and Weng Qing and her brother as a scribe.” </p>
<p>Mingjue’s upper lip twitched at his earlier thoughts. “Well at least that one can be out of Lotus Pier.” </p>
<p>He thought he caught sight of Jin Zixun hovering outside of the family quarters, but paid it no mind. Wei Wuxian had taken it upon himself to ward their rooms prior to the wedding, and the man was good enough at talisman work that Mingjue doubted anyone capable of bypassing them besides the immortals themselves. </p>
<p>“His first move will be much like mine,” Meng Yao whispered, apparently having made the same observation. “Searching the Unclean Realm for signs of where the dragons stay. He’ll know from my initial reports to my… to Jin Guangshan that they’re not within the walls, and will likely go further afield. Everyone should avoid the landing for now. He’s clever enough to realize the grass is tamped down.” </p>
<p>“We can pass along the message at the meal tonight.”</p>
<p>“No. He’ll insist on attending, and I believe Jin Guangshan will probably draw out his visit at least another few days to see him properly installed.” He took a steadying breath and turned to take Mingjue’s arm. “Da-ge, you should be prepared to hold your temper; my father is too aware of potential backlash if he offers you insult, so he’ll have Zixun do it in his place. He will look to get a rise out of Zixuan in punishment for his words towards me and both of you must remain calm, no matter what he says. </p>
<p>“And,” Meng Yao swallowed nervously, “Zixun will find a way to get me alone, one way or another. It won’t be as bad as when we were in Koi Tower, but he knows where and how to strike to leave no marks.”</p>
<p>Forget holding back his temper at dinner; Mingjue was already furious. “You cannot expect me to stay silent while you are abused in your own home.”</p>
<p>"We cannot give them excuses to take offense. Remember that while the House exists in the Unclean Realm, the only true alliance at the moment is between Jin and Jiang. For all his talk of alliances last night, Jin Guangshan knows that. Should something occur, he can place blame without offending his official allies, and insist on retribution. It could result in a war greater than the Sunshot Campaign."</p>
<p>"How? The Nie and the Lan would never…"</p>
<p>"No, but he could convince the smaller sects that you hold too much power, and are unafraid of offending or injuring your allies. You know many of the other sect leaders are envious of you, Xichen and your connection to the dragons. They covet that power. All it would take for that covetousness to turn to open hostility is a single excuse, and Jin Guangshan excels in finding those excuses and exploiting them. It's how he was able to avoid commitment to the Sunshot Campaign and still come ahead."</p>
<p>"I hate all this political bullshit."</p>
<p>"Fortunately you have Huaisang and I to take care of it for you." Meng Yao pressed a warm palm to Mingjue's bicep. "And we will."</p>
<p>Mingjue's upper lip twitched. "Fine. But if he does anything where I can see, Baxia and I will take exception."</p>
<p>"Of that I have no doubt," Meng Yao chuckled. "Just remember you can't actually beat a visiting member of the gentry who disciplines me for poor work as a servant of this household."</p>
<p>"A servant—!"</p>
<p>"A servant to all except those who matter." </p>
<p>Perhaps the wine, combined with exhaustion of the past few weeks and the forgone bedtime, emboldened him. "You matter, Meng Yao. To me."</p>
<p>With soft eyes and dimpled cheeks Meng Yao squeezed the arm against which his palm still rested and took himself into his room. </p>
<p>Mingjue waited outside the door for a long moment before double checking the wards Wei Wuxian had lovingly drawn into the frame, and heading to seek out his own bed.</p><hr/>
<p>Mingjue crawled in beside him shortly before Xichen gave thought to rising, sleep still pressing heavy against his eyelids and fighting the ingrained habits of a life of early mornings tugging him towards consciousness. Mingjue’s solid body tucked around Xichen's, holding tight. Xichen allowed himself an indulgent few extra minutes, which quickly turned to a quarter hour before he untangled himself from his husband's embrace. Mingjue grumbled and rolled into the spot Xichen abandoned, muttering unhappily even in sleep. Noticing the state of his hair, Xichen sighed fondly and quickly undid the tangle of braids, redoing them into something significantly simpler, which wouldn’t end up with Mingjue bemoaning the state of his head when he woke. Predictably, his husband slept through the entire affair. </p>
<p>He dressed for the day and started out, unsurprised at the empty corridors. He'd be shocked if any of the House woke before midday, and judging from the state of affairs he left behind when he took himself to bed, their guests would be in similar states of recovery. For all the indulgence, it was a wonderful evening. </p>
<p>The only exception, he thought sourly as he stepped onto the balcony overlooking the vast family gardens, happened to also be enjoying the view.</p>
<p>"Clan Leader Jin," Xichen said in greeting. "Good morning."</p>
<p>All good cheer and expansive grins, Jin Guangshan waved him forward. "Young Master Lan. Or is it Clan Leader? I'm sorry, but with your uncle conducting all your affairs…"</p>
<p>"My uncle does the Lan great honour by acting as Clan Leader. In deference and respect to his efforts, I will accept young master as a form of address." He didn't have to school this man in etiquette. He knew very well that he was speaking with an equal, but wanted the excuse for condescension. "Were you in search of something? These areas are restricted, but I am happy to assist in finding your destination." Despite Wuxian's arguments for it, they hadn't warded the hallways themselves; personal rooms could be excused away. Hallways might make it seem as though they had something to hide.</p>
<p>"No, no, just an old man's reminiscing." He gestured out to the garden, and Xichen looked down to see A-Yuan and Jingyi playing near one of the ponds. </p>
<p>His blood chilled as he considered what could have happened, if Jin Guangshan had spied A-Yuan shifting into his dragon skin. His nephew was far and beyond better at controlling it, but still not completely reliable in his efforts.</p>
<p>"I miss when Zixuan and Zixun were that age. So much energy. So much potential. Having a son is such a joy."</p>
<p>Xichen frowned. "You have more than one son, Jin Guangshan. You might take pains to remember it occasionally to absolve the rest of us of the responsibility of reminding you." It was the harshest he'd ever spoken—perhaps to anyone—but all he could think of was the  lost, confused frown when they offered Meng Yao a family; the reluctant hope when he realized they wanted nothing from him in return.</p>
<p>"His mother was a whore, Xichen, who is even to say the boy is mine?" That he could speak such horrible words while still smiling made Xichen want to take a page from Mingjue's book and rattle Shouyue in the scabbard. "But let us not quarrel. You've made a place for him here, and I'm sure he's well suited to it." Xichen only overlooked the insinuation in his tone because he had years of practice in suppressing the more violent of his emotional impulses.</p>
<p>"Meng Yao is a valued member of our house," Xichen stated coldly.</p>
<p>"You're welcome to him, Young Master Lan," Jin Guanghan stated. "Ah! But now, why don't you show me where I might find a meal. I could see my son's delicate touch in the wine served last night, but I'm not as young as I once was, and even a single jar has done my head few favours." He chuckled merrily.</p>
<p>"Follow me," Xichen said with a tilt of his head. Anything to remove him from a place where he might see the boys.</p>
<p>Behind them, A-Yuan shrieked in delight, followed quickly by the sound of a splash and Jingyi's quick, sunshine laughter.</p><hr/>
<p>Most of the guests left within the week, leaving only a few stragglers with independent business and Jin Zixun. Meng Yao fully anticipated every cutting word and comment, and accepted them with grace, fully aware that his cousin had the good sense not to say anything within hearing distance of Zixuan and thus limited in his ability to offer insult. </p>
<p>He was also limited in his ability to behave with anything resembling subterfuge. While Meng Yao now realized the House had been fully aware of his actions in sneaking about the Unclean Realm at night, it felt very different being on the other side of such matters. He’d spoken truly to Mingjue; Jin Zixun was a cruel, spiteful, ignorant bully but he was not stupid. His search did venture into some of the larger spaces within the walls, possibly because he failed to offer Meng Yao’s intelligence equal respect, but for the most part he did not repeat the efforts Meng Yao made himself upon arriving. There was something to his search Meng Yao did not care for; an erratic pattern that suggested a lack of strategy, and Jin Zixun had been on enough night hunts to know that a concentrated search pattern to be the most effective. Whatever he hoped to find, he was going about it poorly enough that Meng Yao had to wonder if they were missing something. </p>
<p>Regardless, the House had their fingers on the pulse of it, and he was much better occupied with the boys, his work with Mingjue, and—more pressingly—working on behalf of Jiang Cheng and Wen Qing to garner Madam Yu’s approval for their marriage. The Jiang Clan elder was obviously not thrilled with the idea of such a match, and Meng Yao and Nie Huaisang were tirelessly working to bring her on side. With all their efforts in finding a way to make such a match even remotely possible, they were unwilling to cede defeat now in the face of Madam Yu’s disapproval.</p>
<p>They enjoyed a brief reprieve while Jiang Cheng, Yanli-jie and Zixuan accompanied Madam Yu back to Lotus Pier. Official negotiation wouldn’t begin for another few months, at least, in respect to the timing of Yanli-jie’s wedding. They had all left early that morning, shortly after Lan Wangji and Wei Wuxian had departed to see to a request made by Wen Qing herself with a night hunt on Dafan Mountain gone awry.</p>
<p>To whit: Jin Zixun was so far from his mind as to be practically non-existent. Which meant it took Meng Yao by surprise to find himself cornered on his way back to his room from an evening meal, a rough hand on his shoulder and a sharp beam strutting out from the wall suddenly pressing into his back. </p>
<p>Despite months of tooth-aching sincerity, the habit of slipping his mask effortlessly back into place returned to him without a moment’s hesitation. </p>
<p>“You must be enjoying your time here, Meng Yao. Putting your skills to good use? On your back?” </p>
<p>“I see your odd obsession with my sexual prowess has persisted. Might I recommend developing a courting strategy of your own to allow you to focus such fixations in the appropriate direction? With the proper application of charm, you might have a chance of convincing some poor soul to have you.”</p>
<p>Shock quickly twisted quickly into rage, but instead of the blow that would have fallen at Koi Tower, he pressed hard knuckles into Meng Yao’s sternum, pressing his entire weight forward until Meng Yao could barely take a breath for the pain of it. He fought against the desire to twist his face up, meeting Jin Zixun’s eyes without blinking until his arm loosened and Meng Yao gasped in a breath. </p>
<p>“You think because you’ve gotten friendly with the Household of the Two Lords you can speak to me this way?” </p>
<p>“No. I think I can speak to you like this because if I use large words you probably won’t understand them.” </p>
<p>Jin Zixun scowled. It was a very subtle difference from the usual pinched look to his face and only obvious to those intimately acquainted with the nuances of his disdain. This time, the punch came swiftly and hammered into the same spot his knuckles had tenderized moments before. It stole the breath from Meng Yao’s lungs, and he braced for more. </p>
<p>It didn’t come. Seemingly remembering where they were, Jin Zixun pushed Meng Yao back against the wall and pulled away. </p>
<p>“The Two Lords won’t always have the corner on power, Meng Yao. You should remember that.” </p>
<p>He turned and took off. Meng Yao frowned as he went. He’d expected something similar; Jin Zixun’s ongoing failure to find anything of value meant he needed to violently express his anger instead of accepting himself as a failure. </p>
<p>So why did it feel as though they weren’t finished? </p>
<p>Meng Yao made his way back to his room, puzzling over the thought even as he struggled to take a substantial breath. He pressed his palm to the spot and wondered if the blow hadn’t bruised a rib. </p>
<p>He was three-quarters undressed when the realization hit.</p>
<p>Hastily donning his overrobe, he wound his way through the hallways and out to the houses beyond, the freestanding houses preferable in the open mountain air. He quickly found himself to where Lan Xichen and Nie Mingjue had taken up residence. </p>
<p>He knocked frantically, and after only a few moments’ hesitation, the door opened. Lan Xichen stood in the doorway, in a similar state of disarray as he prepared for bed, and frowned in concern when he saw Meng Yao. </p>
<p>“A-Yao—?”</p>
<p>“Jin Zixun knows something,” Meng Yao said. </p>
<p>Lan Xichen looked over his shoulder, scanning the surroundings for eavesdroppers, and then stepped back to allow Meng Yao inside. Before he spoke further, Lan Xichen put up a silencing barrier, finishing moments before Nie Mingjue stepped out from behind a privacy screen erected on the other side of the room, half-dressed and obviously preparing for bed. Meng Yao’s brain momentarily offered nothing but the word ‘chest’ before he blinked himself back into cognizance. </p>
<p>“What is it he knows, A-Yao?” Lan Xichen asked. </p>
<p>“I don’t know.” He shifted with a wince, which both of them immediately marked with hard glares. “He accosted me earlier. Nothing out of the ordinary, but he failed to ask me any questions about the dragons.” </p>
<p>“And you assume this means he knows something?” </p>
<p>“Undoubtedly.”</p>
<p>“All right.” Lan Xichen placed a hand on Meng Yao’s shoulder. “There’s nothing we can do about it tonight.”</p>
<p>Well, an assassination could be hastily arranged. Nie Huaisang likely wasn’t abed, and between the two of them they could suss something out. Maybe some sort of unsurvivable curse? No. he best ones took far too long, and it would cast too much suspicion on the House. It would be so much easier in Koi Tower, where everyone was always plotting and a few well-placed tugs on the threads of the golden peony tapestry could unravel someone’s life. </p>
<p>No one would miss him, either. Not even Jin Guangshan, as evidenced by his decision to leave him behind in the Unclean Realm with weak illusions as to his purpose. As he’d told Meng Yao, if he died Jin Guangshan lost nothing and despite his contempt for Meng Yao himself, he surely believed him more basically competent than Jin Zixun. </p>
<p>And yet, should Meng Yao murder someone in the Unclean Realm without the immediate need to defend his own life or the life of one of the House—even preemptively—he could not see Nie Mingjue or Lan Xichen forgiving it. And truth would out, as it always did. And he was struggling to behave as a decent person, despite the inherent conflict with his natural tendencies.</p>
