<p>Deeply aggrieved, he realized he’d come to the wrong room. Now he was here, standing before two men who trusted him <em>not</em> to perpetuate wicked acts under their roof, he was reluctant to follow through on his initial and very proper impulse to see Jin Zixun dead. </p>
<p>Trying to behave in a moral way was so exhausting. </p>
<p>Tucking the assassination option back away—for now—he reluctantly nodded and prepared to return to his room. </p>
<p>“You keep touching your chest. Are you injured?” Nie Mingjue demanded. </p>
<p>“It’s nothing, Da-ge,” Meng Yao assured him. “The usual casual abuse.” Nie Mingjue’s lip curled angrily and Lan Xichen grabbed his forearm. The touch calmed him, but barely, and Meng Yao fixed him with a foreboding eye. “We knew this would happen, remember.” </p>
<p>Wrestling down the remnants of his temper, Nie Mingjue shook his head. “I told you I wouldn’t like it.” </p>
<p>“Believe me, Da-ge, I don’t enjoy it either.” He rested his hand on Lan Xichen’s, still pressed into Nie Mingjue’s forearm, a shiver running up his arm at the contact. “But I can bear it. And tomorrow I will speak with Huaisang. Between the two of us, I’m sure we can think of something that doesn’t involve murder.”</p>
<p>“Murder?” Nie Mingjue repeated with a furrowed brow. “No one said anything about murder.” </p>
<p>“Which you should consider a sign of personal growth on my part.” He allowed a teasing smile, which Nie Mingjue scowled at. “Tomorrow. I’ve kept you both from bed long enough.”</p><hr/>
<p>Before they could summon Meng Yao to speak more of Jin Zixun the following morning, their meal was interrupted by an urgent courier. The young woman looked exhausted, her spiritual energy completely depleted by what was obviously a long flight through the night.</p>
<p>"Bodies were found at the entrance to Cloud Recesses," she reported, "Horribly mutilated. Master Lan has requested aid."</p>
<p>"What do you think?" Xichen asked, after sending her to a well-deserved rest. He’d stood halfway through her declaration, mind already halfway to Cloud Recesses.</p>
<p>"Wen Xu?" Mingjue whispered.</p>
<p>"He's dead," Xichen argued. "He has to be."</p>
<p>"I didn't say he wasn't." They exchanged grim looks. "I'll let A-Sang know. We can leave right away."</p>
<p>"But with the others all gone—"</p>
<p>"He and Meng Yao are capable of handling things for the moment." His lips twisted. "No doubt they both have plans if Jin Zixun tries anything." </p>
<p>They arranged for Jin Zixun to take a tour of their training grounds, far away from the landing. The whole time, Xichen couldn't help the sinking feeling in his gut something was wrong. One of them should stay behind. But how could they? If it truly was Wen Xu returned from the dead, it had taken them both last time to defeat him, and an entity powerful enough to kill and dismember five Lan cultivators would doubtless prove even harder to stop.</p>
<p>"Be careful, Da-ge, Xichen-ge," Huaisang whispered, eyes cast with a rare glimpse of real worry. "Last time…" He turned a meaningful eye on Xichen's midriff.</p>
<p>"As careful as we can." Mingjue tugged a loose lock of Huaisang's hair. "If there's trouble, we'll do our best to come home." Even on wing Gusu was a half-day's flight, and Yunmeng still further. He didn't like the idea of them all being so far out of reach, for all he trusted Huaisang and Meng Yao to take care of things.</p>
<p>"Safe flight," Huaisang said. </p>
<p>Xichen and Mingjue both shifted and took to the skies.</p><hr/>
<p>Meng Yao had been running around all morning. First it was to find Nie Mingjue and Lan Xichen to discuss his suspicions about Jin Zixun. When he had finally been informed that urgent business had taken them to Gusu—and he needed to work on his connection to the household staff if he wasn't being immediately informed about such things—he had thrown himself into figuring out Nie Mingjue's agenda for the day to make sure nothing important was shuffled aside.</p>
<p>He had barely made headway into the horrendous pile of papers when one of the guards from the main gate crashed into the office to report an inconsolable man screaming at their door. Nothing he would generally fret over, but it happened to be one of their most prosperous farmers, one they couldn't afford to ignore lest production suffer and impact half of Qinghe.</p>
<p>The source of his vexation was his neighbour, the second most prolific farmer in Qinghe, apparently doing something obscene in his back field. </p>
<p>He had then been shown onto a horse, alongside Nie Huaisang in case he needed more weight behind words he had to speak, and was pulled out into the countryside to examine what was supposedly an attack from a neighbouring farm, but in reality ended up being a fierce corpse that had somehow stumbled onto their land and been mistaken for the neighbour.</p>
<p>The fierce corpse was easily dispatched by their honour guard. The irate neighbour, offended at the accusations leveled his way, took somewhat longer to assuage.</p>
<p>It was midafternoon by the time they finally trudged back through the gates, and Meng Yao still had a sheaf of papers thicker than his thigh to address.</p>
<p>All this fell away when he saw a familiar face strolling through the courtyard.</p>
<p>"Master Nie Jun," Meng Yao called. The man turned. "Were you not with the boys this afternoon?" </p>
<p>Nie Jun was the singularly most reliable of the boy's temporary instructors. His grasp on history was remarkably basic, and anything he didn't understand he glossed over and passed onto Meng Yao for follow up. Meng Yao loved that particular brand of subservient ignorance.  He had left instructions for Nie Jun to step in, but hadn't stayed to see them carried out. If they'd been unsupervised the entire afternoon… well. They hadn't seen smoke during their approach, so Jingyi obviously hadn't attempted to recreate his experiments with congee.</p>
<p>Nie Huaisang appeared at his elbow.</p>
<p>“I was, Master Meng. They were very spirited this morning. Missing their parents, I think.” Wei Wuxian and Lan Wangji were due back from Dafan Mountain later that evening, and the boys always grew restless shortly before their parents arrived home. “I’m glad your cousin volunteered to take them for a bit.” </p>
<p>The bottom dropped from Meng Yao’s stomach. “What?” </p>
<p>Nie Jun continued with a nod, "Young Master Jin said you had given him permission to take the boys to the back training field to show them Jin sword forms. I thought it an excellent way for them to burn off the extra energy—"</p>
<p>Meng Yao and Huaisang exchanged gut-wrenching looks of panic, and took off together without another word, Meng Yao cursing his own stupidity the entire way. Of course he would go for the boys. They shouldn't have left them unsupervised, even with the pressing emergency.</p>
<p>The back field was cluttered with training paraphernalia, but exactly zero children. Forgetting himself, Meng Yao screamed, "A-Yuan! Jingyi!"</p>
<p>A muffled cry came from one of the sheds where broken weapons were stored before being melted down. Meng Yao threw the doors open and Jingyi stumbled out, bleeding from his temple.</p>
<p>"Teacher! He took A-Yuan. I tried to stop him, but he hit me, and…"</p>
<p>All the blood in Meng Yao's body rushed away, leaving him light-headed and desperate. He locked eyes with Huaisang. "I'll take him to the infirmary."</p>
<p>Huaisang adjusted his grip on his fan to grasp his white jade sword token. It glowed fiercely between his palms, but they both knew how long it would take for the others to return.</p>
<p>Huaisang jerked his head. "I'll get the horses."</p>
<p>Meng Yao hoisted Jingyi into his arms and took off at a run. Jin Zixun would have a generous start on them, but he wouldn't have been able to access the House's superior horses, and he would be riding double. There was a chance they could catch him before he made it to the border.</p>
<p>Jingyi was hysterical by the time they reached the infirmary, but he did not insist Meng Yao stay. Meng Yao pressed a quick kiss to his head, squeezed his arm, and took off towards the gates.</p>
<p>The horses were saddled and they rode out at a punishing pace. They could bring no honour guard, no additional protection; if they ended up crossing into Lanling, any sign of force would mean war, and he had no doubt Jin Guangshan would take the opportunity for what it was. Even Huaisang coming along was dangerous, but Meng Yao wasn’t going to be the one to suggest he remain at home.</p>
<p>It was nearly nightfall by the time they caught up to Jin Zixun, their horses half-dead with exertion. Meng Yao pulled wildly back on the reigns and stared in horror as they rounded a bend in the road and found themselves faced with a small army of Jin soldiers. Inside Qinghe borders.</p>
<p>"Yao-ge," Huaisang whispered.</p>
<p>Meng Yao looked into the crowd and spotted his father, Jin Zixun mounted proudly beside him. A-Yuan was nowhere to be seen.</p>
<p>Jin Guangshan was about to emerge the winner.</p>
<p>"Nie Huaisang," Meng Yao said, turning in his saddle. "That fan really is the ugliest thing I've ever seen."</p>
<p>"I—" Before he could speak another word, Meng Yao shoved a dagger into his side. Huaisang stared at Meng Yao, face twisted up, before slumping and toppling off his horse.</p>
<p>"What, the traitor now seeks my favour?" Jin Guangshan demanded. </p>
<p>Meng Yao dismounted his horse and moved to stand over Huaisang. The other man's eyes were quickly drooping shut. "Traitor? Who do you think orchestrated things so cousin Zixun could collect the boy? Did the timing not seem perfect, with the prominent members of the House all away from the Unclean Realm?"</p>
<p>"You couldn't know we planned to drop those bodies at Cloud Recesses," Jin Zixun pointed out through a curled lip.</p>
<p>"It merely moved up plans I already had in place." Meng Yao turned and bowed deeply. “They all knew I was there on your behalf, Sect Leader Jin. It took almost the full year to be taken into their confidence. How else would I have been entrusted with the care of the children? If I had given even a hint of my true intentions, I would not have been able to be of use to you. Especially when they began intercepting my letters.”</p>
<p>Jin Zixun continued to appear unconvinced. "You never said anything!"</p>
<p>"When was I meant to tell you? You were under scrutiny from the moment you entered the Unclean Realm," Meng Yao pointed out. "And you weren't subtle about your interest.”</p>
<p>He pulled his own token off his belt and held it up for his father to see. He then very deliberately dropped it atop Huaisang's bleeding wound. "You know my capabilities, Sect Leader Jin. If I have inadvertently deceived you while at the same time deceiving them, I apologize. But please take it as a sign of my efficacy." He bowed even lower. “I know more about the Household of the Two Lords and the Unclean Realm than anyone. I’m sure my words will prove their own worth as you prepare for their arrival.” </p>
<p>Jin Guangshan's lip drew up in consideration. How could he doubt it, when all Meng Yao had ever sought was his approval? "You should call me father."</p>
<p>Meng Yao's grin widened, a nasty curl of lips cutting across his face.</p>
<p>"My son, Jin Guangyao."</p>
<p>He bowed to his father and remounted his horse, which shuddered beneath him. The soldiers passed as he trotted to Jin Guangshan's side. Behind him, tucked away in a cage mounted on a heavily reinforced wagon, A-Yuan lay unconscious in his dragon skin. His breathing was slightly laboured, but Meng Yao could see no other injuries. He’d been correct after all: Jin Zixun had known something. He’d just never suspected it to be about A-Yuan. </p>
<p>"We should hurry back to Koi Tower," Jin Zixun stated, still peering at Meng Yao with suspicion. No matter. Suspicious could be allayed, and he knew Jin Zixun well enough to find a way to set his mind at ease, especially now he was legitimized and Jin Zixun was required to treat him as family. </p>
<p>Meng Yao nodded. "I could not stop Nie Huaisang from summoning the dragons before we left. They will doubtless catch us up before too long."</p>
<p>"Home, then."</p>
<p>The soldiers preceded them, surrounding the wagon in a heavily-armoured procession to protect their prize.</p>
<p>They left Huaisang behind them, bleeding into the dirt.</p><hr/>
<p>Boiling dark clouds rolled in a thunderhead towards the white walls of Koi Tower, a massive rage-filled storm crackling with lightning strong enough to shake the marrow in his bones.</p>
<p>Jin Guangshan stood at the top of the stairs, flanked by Meng Yao and Jin Zixun. His soldiers—both cultivators and the mediocre men eager for promotion he sent out to die early—lined the steps and guarded the bottommost stairs below.</p>
<p>It felt odd, after all these years, to finally be draped in Jin gold, the coveted vermillion mark upon his brow. He'd also chosen a hat, hoping to loom as large as the man beside him.</p>
<p>They didn't have to wait long for their guests to arrive.</p>
<p>Huangang-jun landed, maw pulled back over his intimidatingly sharp teeth. Wei Wuxian, sword already drawn, glared up the stairs at the three men gathered at the top. Meng Yao understood the precariousness of their position; they had to face the Jin head on until A-Yuan was safe. </p>
<p>Chifeng-zun landed moments later, and Xichen threw himself off his back. His vaunted neutrality had disappeared in rage, Shouyue clenched tightly in his hands.</p>
<p>"Nie Mingjue couldn't join us?" Jin Guangshan demanded. "Our negotiations will be incomplete without him."</p>
<p>"Give me back my son!" Wei Wuxian screamed.</p>
<p>"A dragon? Your son? Must have been quite the surprise to your husband, Young Master Wei," Jin Guangshan guffawed. Only Jin Zixun laughed along. "But in consideration to your… feelings, I am willing to be benevolent in this instance, and allow you short visits contingent on your good behaviour."</p>
<p>Wei Wuxian’s eyes burned with such hatred Meng Yao found his own gut twisted in fear. If Jin Zixun and Jin Guangshan failed to feel it, they overestimated the chances of their own survival.</p>
<p>"Father, I'm going to go check to make sure none of the others has slipped inside the back gates," Meng Yao whispered. His father nodded and waved him away. Meng Yao ducked his head and withdrew.</p>
<p>A-Yuan was still in his cage, tucked back into the grand hall away from sight of the gathered parties. He swung around the small space in agitation, bashing himself against the bars in fruitless attempts to escape.</p>
<p>"Sect Leader Jin wants you," Meng Yao said to two of the guards. They rushed to obey, leaving only the one standing in front of the cage. He did not consider Meng Yao a threat. Why would he? After all, until now he had only been a servant and he’d been handed everything he’d ever wanted by being named Jin Guangyao.</p>
<p>"What's wrong with it?" Meng Yao asked with a frown.</p>
<p>The guard turned his head to look, which gave Meng Yao the perfect opportunity to drive the  dagger into his back.</p>
<p><em>Here and here, A-Yao,</em> his mother had said. <em>This will kill a man fast. </em>This<em> will kill a man slow.</em></p>
<p>He pushed the body away and ducked down before the cage.</p>
<p>"A-Yuan," Meng Yao gasped. The child writhed in blind panic, knocking himself against the sides of the cage. He needed to calm down, but with his eyes glazed with panic he barely seemed to see Meng Yao at all. Desperate, Meng Yao dashed his hat to the ground and frantically scrubbed the dot from his brow in case A-Yuan couldn’t recognize him through the panic. “A-Yuan.” He shoved his hands through the bars and caught A-Yuan’s snout between his palms. A-Yuan stilled and looked at him with wide, terrified eyes. Meng Yao repeated a gesture he’d seen Wei Wuxian use to comfort his son, brushing the palm of his hand along the ridge above A-Yuan’s eye. Finally, the child regained some measure of calm, though his body thrummed with the strain. </p>
<p>"You need to go to baba." There was no angle for A-Yuan to see past him. "He's through the door, at the very bottom of the stairs." A-Yuan very deliberately nodded his head, and remained calm when Meng Yao withdrew his hands. “You cannot stop once you’re out of this cage, no matter what you see or hear. Do you understand?” A-Yuan nodded again. “Be brave. Your parents are so proud of you.” Meng Yao hesitated. “And so am I.” </p>
<p>He split the skin of his thumb with his teeth and pressed it against the lock. It sprung open, and for the first time in years, Meng Yao didn't viciously hate his father's pernicious blood running through his veins.</p>
<p>He tore the cage open and A-Yuan flung himself out, flying faster than anyone could hope to catch. Meng Yao paused only to grab the downed guard’s sword before running after him. He had no hope of beating trained soldiers, but all he had to do was draw their attention. The two he’d sent off to his father were charging back, Jin Zixun close behind them, and A-Yuan flung himself above their heads. They all grabbed for him as he flew by, opening themselves for attack. Meng Yao drove the sword through one and whipped out his dagger to stab the other. His aim proved true: the man toppled over with the blade struck through his heart. </p>
<p>It left only him and Jin Zixun. He bore no illusions: he had won against the guards only because of their distraction and the element of surprise. He had no hope against Jin Zixun. For all his varied faults, his cousin was a decent fighter, and Meng Yao had effectively disarmed himself when the guards had fallen and taken his weapons with them. </p>
<p>“I knew it,” Jin Zixun spat. He swiped his sword and Meng Yao barely managed to dodge. "You fucking whore's son." His arm came springing back up and caught the cloth on Meng Yao’s arm. The heavy robes offered little protection, but they did stop the skip from being flayed open from elbow to shoulder. </p>
<p>If he ran, he might make it to one of the servant’s corridors, and had a slim hope of losing Jin Zixun in Koi Tower’s labyrinthine back passageways. His cousin never bothered with such routes, when walking the same pathways as the servants was so beneath him. But the entrance to the closest one was too far for comfort, and Meng Yao doubted he could outrun Jin Zixun over any sort of distance. </p>
<p>He threw himself backwards to put the cage between himself and Jin Zixun. The other man’s face twisted in amusement. He darted forward, arm outstretched. Meng Yao tried to twist away, but caught the blow across his chest, barely able to draw back in time to avoid being split in half. His chest lit with fire and blood filled his mouth. </p>
<p>It put Jin Zixun on odd footing and Meng Yao took the chance for what it was. He charged forward to the front of the reception hall, hand desperately pressed against the wound in his chest. If A-Yuan had escaped, and he had to make sure of it, there were other corridors he could use to hide himself away that exited at the top of the stairs. As long as A-Yuan was safe, he could retreat afterwards to see to his wound.</p><hr/>
<p>Xichen cut through the Jin guards effortlessly, skills honed through long years of war more than adequate to dispatch the collected guards. Jin Guangshan’s decision to keep them out of the Sunshot Campaign had resulted in better numbers, but untried men. The greatest of the Jin warriors, Zixuan, was back in the Unclean Realm, reluctantly remaining behind to organize their forces in case this resulted in all-out war. </p>
<p>The second-greatest was nowhere to be seen, a sharp worry Xichen ruthlessly grinding against his mind. </p>
<p>“Do you see Jin Zixun?” Xichen demanded, cutting down an approaching cultivator. The force of his blow sent the man flying. </p>
<p>“Who?” Wei Wuxian demanded, launching himself off Hanguang-jun’s back and throwing himself into a knot of men tangled up too close together and cutting through them with ease. “Oh! That one? He ducked back inside!”</p>
<p>Worrisome. Xichen didn’t like to think about what might have pulled him away. </p>
<p>A sharp tug hauled him backwards, out of the path of a blade flying towards his head. Chifeng-zun’s tail, snugly wrapped about his waist, tightened for only a moment before flinging him back into the fray. He regretted following their first inclination, to arrive upon the backs of Hanguang-jun and Chifeng-zun instead of riding in on horseback. They’d hoped the sight would intimidate Jin Guangshan into surrendering A-Yuan, but all it meant was that unless they wanted to betray their secrets, they had lost two of their best fighters in Wangji and Mingjue. </p>
<p>“A-Yuan!” Wei Wuxian screamed. Xichen cut down the man in front of him and looked up as the child barrelled into his father’s chest, Wei Wuxian catching him with ease. The moment he wrapped himself in his father’s arms he lost the ability to hold his shape, and shifted back into his human skin. </p>
<p>The sight momentarily stunned the men surrounding him, which gave Hanguang-jun enough time to grab up both Wei Wuxian and A-Yuan and take off into the night sky. </p>
<p>“Archers!” Jin Guangshan screamed, far too late. Hanguang-jun had launched them directly upwards, aiming for the stormhead where Sandu Shengshou circled above to keep the clouds in place to cover their retreat; even the best archers would be hard-pressed to hit them.  </p>
<p>That only left collecting A-Yao. </p>
<p>The moment the thought crossed his mind, movement at the top of the Koi Tower stairs caught his eye and he looked up in time to catch sight of Meng Yao, watching Hanguang-jun’s retreat with relieved eyes, blood staining the front of his robes and caught on his lips as he coughed out a laboured breath. </p>
<p>Xichen propelled himself through the air, catching hold of Chifeng-zun’s neck as the other dragon reared backwards. They could grab A-Yao, and then—</p>
<p>The blood froze in his veins as Jin Zixun appeared behind him.</p><hr/>
<p>Meng Yao stumbled forward, making it to the top of the stairs in time to see A-Yuan collide with Wuxian, his father catching him with a joyous cry of relief as he shifted from dragon to child. Hanguang-jun swept them up and shot into the air lightning fast, carrying them safely away.</p>
<p>His father turned, face twisted in rage, and Meng Yao met his eyes. Let him see that all his ambitions had been ruined by Meng Shi. Let him see his own downfall in Meng Shi’s eyes. </p>
<p>Now he had to live to enjoy watching the man suffer through the consequences. </p>
<p>Meng Yao turned to escape to one of the servant corridors, and found himself suddenly stopped by the sight of Jin Zixun standing behind him and a terrible pressure in his sternum.</p>
<p>“I wanted them to see this,” Jin Zixun told him with a smug grin. He took a step forward and the pressure increased. Meng Yao looked down and discovered Jin Zixun's sword had been stabbed right through him, intersecting the gaping wound across his chest. </p>
<p>"A-Yao!" Someone was screaming his name, but he couldn't parse the voice from the fierce roar in his ears.</p>
<p>Jin Zixun grabbed his shoulder tight and pulled him further along his blade. Meng Yao's body split as though made of paper and Jin Zixun moved his grip to Meng Yao's throat. </p>
<p>Then, with a sneer, he snapped his sword back and shoved Meng Yao down the stairs.</p>
<p>He was airborne for a short eternity, his flight powered by crushing déjà vu. He eventually hit the edge of a lower step shoulder-first, and felt something inside his body crack. His world spun as he tumbled down, time stopping for only a moment when his head slammed against marble, before the angle of his body caught his foot on something solid and he was jerked to a rough stop.</p><hr/>
<p>Chifeng-zun whipped his neck to send Xichen hurtling forward, and he landed on the step next to Meng Yao just as Jin Zixun came to a halt in front of him. He held Shuoyue aloft, waiting for the other man to make his move. The rest of the Jin troops—those Xichen and Wei Wuxian had left alive, anyway—circled Chifeng-zun on the ground below, as though they had a hope of stopping him. </p>
<p>“Stay back,” Xichen warned, though he had little hope of warning Jin Zixun off completely. </p>
<p>Jin Zixun’s feet shifted, as though preparing to strike. If he came down and put them on even ground, Xichen had the advantage of both skill and experience. Unfortunately, his would-be opponent seemed to realize it.</p>
<p>He heard Chifeng-zun launch into the air with a rush of wind and Jin Zixun looked upwards just long enough for Xichen to strike. </p>
<p>Shouyue had a long reach, and Jin Zixun screamed as Xichen ruthlessly slashed his knees. As he toppled forward, Xichen stepped to the side and flicked his blade out, opening his neck from one ear to  the next. </p>
<p>Jin Zixun toppled down the remaining stairs, tumbling to a halt upon the ground below.</p><hr/>
<p>There was so much yelling—Meng Yao wanted to look and make sure his family escaped, but he couldn't move for the pain. Surely they would go, now they had A-Yuan back? They had to.  He’d seen enough to know Wei Wuxian and Hanguang-jun were safely on their way back to the Unclean Realm.</p>
<p>A face appeared in his line of sight, and Meng Yao mustered up the energy to frown. He hadn’t expected anyone to stay once A-Yuan was free.</p>
<p>"Er-ge," he whispered. “You need to go.” </p>
<p>"A-Yao." Xichen looked panicked. Panicked and still beautiful. Was there any circumstances in which his beauty fled?</p>
<p>A sudden fear snapped through the pain to focus his clamorous thoughts. "Er-ge," Meng Yao repeated. "A-Sang—"</p>
<p>"Recovering. Your aim was perfect, and your token let us find him with time to spare. Yanli took him home."</p>
<p>"Good," Meng Yao replied. The last dregs of adrenaline fled his body and his head slumped to the left. "'S good."</p>
<p>"A-Yao," Xichen gathered him close. All around them, the sound of yelling. Of fighting. Didn’t they know they had to run? Leave him and close ranks and allow Huaisang to work his magic with the other sects before Jin Guangshan sent word and made the Two Lords out to be the villains. He never wanted to die on the Koi Tower stairs. </p>
<p>Still. </p>
<p>Maybe...</p>
<p>Maybe this wasn't so bad. To die in Xichen's arms. He only wished Mingjue was there.</p>
<p>Chifeng-zun suddenly loomed large over them, tucking his claws beneath Meng Yao and lifting him into the air, Xichen flinging himself onto the dragon’s back and holding tight. Meng Yao had never flown before; cold wind streamed past him, weightlessness buoying his flagging heart. They passed into the storm. The air temperature dropped and a sudden mist of rain blanketed him, soaking his robes with something other than blood. </p>
<p>They descended all too soon amidst trees that marked Qinghe territory. Dying in Qinghe felt far preferable to dying in Lanling. He’d found his freedom in Qinghe. Chifeng-zun eased Meng Yao to the ground and transformed back into a face Meng Yao… </p>
<p>Well. No point in fooling himself when he was dying anyway. A face Meng Yao loved. </p>
<p>He couldn’t lift his arms. </p>
<p>“A-Yao,” he whispered, grabbing Meng Yao’s hands. “Do you want to live?” </p>
<p>Meng Yao struggled to answer, his throat choked with blood. Xichen appeared on his other side and eased him over to cough it out. </p>
<p>“If I could choose,” Meng Yao finally managed to gasp out. “I would.” </p>
<p>Darkness claimed him before he knew anything more. </p>
<p>And then light. </p>
<p>Brilliant, stunning light washing through him and carried him up and out of the darkness, light the flight he’d only just experienced. He opened his eyes and looked up into the stormclouds above, only vaguely aware of Xichen and Mingjue next to him. The sky called to him, as though he could feel the storm itself strumming through his veins as though every spark of lightning echoed with the breaths in his lungs. Meng Yao stood, lifting his face to the rain and feeling every drop that touched his skin in individual pinpricks of cleansing cool. Hands slid into his, one to either side, and he looked over to take in Xichen on his right and Mingjue on his left.</p>
<p>In the midst of the storm, he spotted Sandu Shengshou circling overhead, presumably keeping watch for pursuit. </p>
<p>An ugly thought rose in his mind. “Jin Guangshan and Jin Zixun.” Jin Guangshan was still a danger to everyone until words of his actions reached the other clans. They had a chance to control the narrative, but only if they moved quickly. </p>
<p>“Jin Zixun is dead,” Mingjue stated, his face grim. “He followed you down the stairs. Xichen made sure he didn’t live long enough to regret it.”</p>
<p>Meng Yao’s shoulders slumped. The movement made his chest ache and he pressed his palm to the wound still unhealed. </p>
<p>“You will heal faster, but it won’t be immediately,” Xichen told him. “Best for us to get you home, and let you have some rest. We will deal with your father.” </p>
<p>As long as Jin Guangshan lived he would be a danger. Meng Yao and Nie Huaisang would have to step up their plans. </p>
<p>“Come, Meng Yao,” Xichen said. He shifted, and Zewu-jun appeared before him, dipping his neck in an inviting fashion. </p>
<p>“Dragons only take one rider,” Meng Yao said, casting confused eyes at Mingjue. </p>
<p>“Yes,” Mingjue agreed. “But other dragons are not riders, A-Yao. That’s entirely different.” </p>
<p>“I don’t see how.” </p>
<p>“Well, now you’ve been blooded, you’ll have sufficient time to find out.” He shifted as well, and Chifeng-zun flanked Zewu-jun, both of them waiting. </p>
<p>Meng Yao approached slowly, and Zewu-jun lowered their front leg further. As he had seen Wei Wuxian do, he carefully stepped upon the broad expanse of muscle and scales and slowly pushed himself up, his torso aching with the strain. He looped his elbow around the largest of Zewu-jun’s mighty horns and used it to leverage himself into a space upon Zewu-jun’s back. </p>
<p>Between one breath and the next, they took into the sky, rising to the stormclouds above.</p>
  </div>
